MS_Algebra2Lessons — Unit1

--- Lesson 1.1: Review of Functions & Notation (Summary) ---

  Key Concepts: Review of Functions & Notation
Overview
This lesson covers the fundamental measures of center used to analyze and summarize data sets. You'll learn how to calculate and apply the mean, median, and mode, and understand when each is most appropriate.
Key Definitions
If f(x) = x² + 1, what is f(3)?
Substitute 3 into the function: f(3) = 3² + 1 = 9 + 1 = 10. The answer 9 forgets to add 1, while the others come from arithmetic mistakes.
What is the domain of f(x) = √(x - 4)?
The radicand must be non-negative: x - 4 ≥ 0 gives x ≥ 4. Note that x = 4 is included because √0 = 0 is defined.
If f(x) = 3x - 2, what is f(5)?
Substitute 5 into the function: f(5) = 3(5) - 2 = 15 - 2 = 13.
If f(x) = x² and g(x) = x + 3, what is (f ∘ g)(2)?
First compute g(2) = 2 + 3 = 5, then f(5) = 5² = 25. Composition means applying g first, then f.
What is a function?
A function is a relation in which every element of the domain (input) is paired with exactly one element of the range (output). This is the defining property that distinguishes functions from general relations.
What is the domain of a function?
The domain of a function is the complete set of all possible input values (typically x-values) for which the function is defined. It is often restricted by denominators equal to zero or negative values under even radicals.
What is the vertical line test?
The vertical line test states that a graph represents a function if and only if every vertical line intersects the graph at most once. If any vertical line crosses the graph more than once, the relation is not a function.
What is an inverse function?
An inverse function f⁻¹ undoes what the original function f does. If f(a) = b, then f⁻¹(b) = a. Graphically, the inverse is a reflection of the original over the line y = x.
What is the horizontal line test used for?
The horizontal line test determines whether a function is one-to-one. If every horizontal line crosses the graph at most once, the function is one-to-one and therefore has an inverse function.
A converter changes Celsius to Fahrenheit using F(C) = (9/5)C + 32. If a thermometer reads 20°C, what is the temperature in Fahrenheit?
Substitute C = 20: F(20) = (9/5)(20) + 32 = 36 + 32 = 68°F. This is the standard Celsius-to-Fahrenheit conversion formula.
A store applies a 10% discount first, then a $5 coupon. If the discount is d(p) = 0.9p and the coupon is c(p) = p - 5, what is the final price of a $60 item using (c ∘ d)(60)?
First apply the discount: d(60) = 0.9(60) = 54. Then apply the coupon: c(54) = 54 - 5 = 49. The composition (c ∘ d)(60) = $49.
A ball is dropped and its height after t seconds is modeled by h(t) = -16t² + 64. What is the height at t = 1 second?
Substitute t = 1: h(1) = -16(1)² + 64 = -16 + 64 = 48 feet. The ball has fallen 16 feet from its initial height of 64 feet.
An online store charges $8 per item plus a $5 shipping fee. If the total cost function is C(n) = 8n + 5, what is the domain of this function in context?
In context, n represents the number of items purchased, which must be a positive whole number. You cannot buy half an item or a negative number of items, so the domain is positive integers.
A biologist models a population with P(t) = 100(2)^t, where t is in years. She wants to know when the population was 100. Using the inverse concept, what is t?
Set P(t) = 100: 100(2)^t = 100. Divide both sides by 100: 2^t = 1. Since 2^0 = 1, t = 0. The population was 100 at the starting time.
A delivery service uses two pricing zones. Zone A charges f(x) = 3x (dollars for x miles), and a fuel surcharge adds g(x) = x + 2. If the total cost is (g ∘ f)(x), what is the total cost for a 5-mile delivery?
First compute f(5) = 3(5) = 15. Then g(15) = 15 + 2 = 17. So (g ∘ f)(5) = $17. The mileage charge is computed first, then the surcharge is applied.

--- Lesson 1.1: Review of Functions & Notation (Quiz) ---

  Q1. If f(x) = 2x + 3, find f(-2).
    [ ] 7
    [ ] -8
    [ ] -4
    [*] -1
    Explanation: Substitute -2 into the function: f(-2) = 2(-2) + 3 = -4 + 3 = -1. The other choices result from sign errors or incorrect order of operations.

  Q2. If f(x) = x² + 1, what is f(3)?
    [ ] 9
    [ ] 7
    [*] 10
    [ ] 12
    Explanation: Substitute 3 into the function: f(3) = 3² + 1 = 9 + 1 = 10. The answer 9 forgets to add 1, while the others come from arithmetic mistakes.

  Q3. What is the domain of f(x) = √(x - 4)?
    [ ] x ≤ 4
    [*] x ≥ 4
    [ ] x > 4
    [ ] All real numbers
    Explanation: The radicand must be non-negative: x - 4 ≥ 0 gives x ≥ 4. Note that x = 4 is included because √0 = 0 is defined.

  Q4. If f(x) = 3x - 2, what is f(5)?
    [ ] 11
    [ ] 17
    [ ] 15
    [*] 13
    Explanation: Substitute 5 into the function: f(5) = 3(5) - 2 = 15 - 2 = 13.

  Q5. The domain of f(x) = 1/(x - 4) excludes which value?
    [ ] x = 0
    [ ] x = -4
    [ ] x = 1
    [*] x = 4
    Explanation: A rational function is undefined where the denominator equals zero. Setting x - 4 = 0 gives x = 4, so this value must be excluded from the domain.

  Q6. If f(x) = x² and g(x) = x + 3, what is (f ∘ g)(2)?
    [*] 25
    [ ] 10
    [ ] 7
    [ ] 13
    Explanation: First compute g(2) = 2 + 3 = 5, then f(5) = 5² = 25. Composition means applying g first, then f.

  Q7. Find f⁻¹(x) if f(x) = 3x + 5.
    [ ] (x + 5)/3
    [ ] (5 - x)/3
    [*] (x - 5)/3
    [ ] 3x - 5
    Explanation: Replace f(x) with y: y = 3x + 5. Swap x and y: x = 3y + 5. Solve for y: y = (x - 5)/3. This is the inverse function.

  Q8. Which graph represents a function?
    [ ] A sideways parabola opening left
    [ ] A circle
    [ ] A vertical line
    [*] A parabola opening upward
    Explanation: A parabola opening upward passes the vertical line test — each x-value maps to exactly one y-value. Circles, vertical lines, and sideways parabolas fail this test.

  Q9. If f(x) = x², find f(3) + f(-3).
    [ ] 6
    [ ] 9
    [*] 18
    [ ] 0
    Explanation: f(3) = 9 and f(-3) = 9, so f(3) + f(-3) = 9 + 9 = 18. Since x² is an even function, f(a) = f(-a) for all a.

  Q10. If f(2) = 7, then f⁻¹(7) equals:
    [ ] -2
    [ ] 1/7
    [*] 2
    [ ] 7
    Explanation: An inverse function reverses the input and output of the original. Since f sends 2 to 7, the inverse sends 7 back to 2, so f⁻¹(7) = 2.

  Q11. What is a function?
    [*] A relation where each input has exactly one output
    [ ] A relation where each output has exactly one input
    [ ] A graph that passes the horizontal line test
    [ ] Any equation with two variables
    Explanation: A function is a relation in which every element of the domain (input) is paired with exactly one element of the range (output). This is the defining property that distinguishes functions from general relations.

  Q12. What does the notation f(x) represent?
    [ ] f multiplied by x
    [*] The output of function f when the input is x
    [ ] The inverse of f at x
    [ ] The derivative of f at x
    Explanation: Function notation f(x) — read 'f of x' — denotes the output value of the function f when x is the input. It is not multiplication; it is a way to name and evaluate functions.

  Q13. What is the domain of a function?
    [ ] The y-intercept of the graph
    [ ] The set of all possible output values
    [*] The set of all possible input values
    [ ] The x-intercepts of the graph
    Explanation: The domain of a function is the complete set of all possible input values (typically x-values) for which the function is defined. It is often restricted by denominators equal to zero or negative values under even radicals.

  Q14. What does the range of a function mean?
    [*] All possible output values of the function
    [ ] The slope of the function
    [ ] The difference between the maximum and minimum values
    [ ] All inputs for which the function is defined
    Explanation: The range is the set of all possible output values (y-values) that a function can produce. For example, the range of f(x) = x² is y ≥ 0 because a squared number is never negative.

  Q15. What is the vertical line test?
    [*] A test to determine if a graph represents a function
    [ ] A test to find the domain
    [ ] A test to find vertical asymptotes
    [ ] A test to determine if a function is one-to-one
    Explanation: The vertical line test states that a graph represents a function if and only if every vertical line intersects the graph at most once. If any vertical line crosses the graph more than once, the relation is not a function.

  Q16. What does 'composition of functions' mean?
    [ ] Multiplying two functions together
    [ ] Finding where two functions intersect
    [*] Applying one function to the result of another
    [ ] Adding two functions together
    Explanation: Composition of functions, written (f ∘ g)(x) = f(g(x)), means first applying function g to x, then applying function f to that result. It chains two functions together in sequence.

  Q17. What is an inverse function?
    [ ] A function reflected over the x-axis
    [ ] The negative of a function, -f(x)
    [ ] The reciprocal of a function, 1/f(x)
    [*] A function that reverses the input-output pairs of the original function
    Explanation: An inverse function f⁻¹ undoes what the original function f does. If f(a) = b, then f⁻¹(b) = a. Graphically, the inverse is a reflection of the original over the line y = x.

  Q18. What does it mean for a function to be 'one-to-one'?
    [ ] It passes the vertical line test
    [ ] It has exactly one x-intercept
    [*] Each output value corresponds to exactly one input value
    [ ] Its domain contains only one element
    Explanation: A one-to-one (injective) function maps distinct inputs to distinct outputs — no two different x-values produce the same y-value. This is verified by the horizontal line test and is required for the function to have an inverse.

  Q19. What does 'even function' mean in mathematics?
    [ ] A function whose degree is an even number
    [*] A function whose graph is symmetric about the y-axis, where f(-x) = f(x)
    [ ] A function that only outputs even numbers
    [ ] A function whose graph is symmetric about the origin
    Explanation: An even function satisfies f(-x) = f(x) for all x in its domain, meaning its graph is symmetric about the y-axis. Examples include f(x) = x² and f(x) = cos(x).

  Q20. What is the horizontal line test used for?
    [ ] To find horizontal asymptotes
    [ ] To find the range of the function
    [ ] To determine if a graph is a function
    [*] To determine if a function is one-to-one and has an inverse
    Explanation: The horizontal line test determines whether a function is one-to-one. If every horizontal line crosses the graph at most once, the function is one-to-one and therefore has an inverse function.

  Q21. A taxi company charges a flat fee of $3 plus $2 per mile. If the fare is modeled by f(m) = 2m + 3, how much does a 7-mile ride cost?
    [ ] $20
    [ ] $14
    [*] $17
    [ ] $10
    Explanation: Substitute m = 7 into the fare function: f(7) = 2(7) + 3 = 14 + 3 = $17. The flat fee of $3 is added to the mileage charge of $14.

  Q22. A gym membership costs $25 per month plus a one-time $50 sign-up fee. The total cost is C(m) = 25m + 50. After how many months will the total cost reach $200?
    [*] 6 months
    [ ] 5 months
    [ ] 7 months
    [ ] 8 months
    Explanation: Set 25m + 50 = 200. Subtract 50 from both sides: 25m = 150. Divide by 25: m = 6. The total reaches $200 after 6 months.

  Q23. A factory's daily production is modeled by P(w) = 50w + 200, where w is the number of workers. If the factory needs to produce 700 units, how many workers are needed?
    [ ] 14
    [*] 10
    [ ] 8
    [ ] 12
    Explanation: Set P(w) = 700: 50w + 200 = 700. Subtract 200: 50w = 500. Divide by 50: w = 10. The factory needs 10 workers to produce 700 units.

  Q24. A converter changes Celsius to Fahrenheit using F(C) = (9/5)C + 32. If a thermometer reads 20°C, what is the temperature in Fahrenheit?
    [*] 68°F
    [ ] 72°F
    [ ] 52°F
    [ ] 100°F
    Explanation: Substitute C = 20: F(20) = (9/5)(20) + 32 = 36 + 32 = 68°F. This is the standard Celsius-to-Fahrenheit conversion formula.

  Q25. A store applies a 10% discount first, then a $5 coupon. If the discount is d(p) = 0.9p and the coupon is c(p) = p - 5, what is the final price of a $60 item using (c ∘ d)(60)?
    [ ] $49.50
    [ ] $50
    [ ] $54
    [*] $49
    Explanation: First apply the discount: d(60) = 0.9(60) = 54. Then apply the coupon: c(54) = 54 - 5 = 49. The composition (c ∘ d)(60) = $49.

  Q26. A car rental costs $40 per day. A customer paid $280. Using the inverse of f(d) = 40d, find how many days the car was rented.
    [ ] 6 days
    [*] 7 days
    [ ] 5 days
    [ ] 8 days
    Explanation: The inverse of f(d) = 40d is f⁻¹(x) = x/40. So f⁻¹(280) = 280/40 = 7 days. The inverse function converts the total cost back to the number of days.

  Q27. A ball is dropped and its height after t seconds is modeled by h(t) = -16t² + 64. What is the height at t = 1 second?
    [ ] 32 feet
    [ ] 80 feet
    [*] 48 feet
    [ ] 16 feet
    Explanation: Substitute t = 1: h(1) = -16(1)² + 64 = -16 + 64 = 48 feet. The ball has fallen 16 feet from its initial height of 64 feet.

  Q28. An online store charges $8 per item plus a $5 shipping fee. If the total cost function is C(n) = 8n + 5, what is the domain of this function in context?
    [ ] All non-negative real numbers
    [*] Positive integers (n ≥ 1)
    [ ] All integers
    [ ] All real numbers
    Explanation: In context, n represents the number of items purchased, which must be a positive whole number. You cannot buy half an item or a negative number of items, so the domain is positive integers.

  Q29. A biologist models a population with P(t) = 100(2)^t, where t is in years. She wants to know when the population was 100. Using the inverse concept, what is t?
    [*] t = 0
    [ ] t = 10
    [ ] t = 2
    [ ] t = 1
    Explanation: Set P(t) = 100: 100(2)^t = 100. Divide both sides by 100: 2^t = 1. Since 2^0 = 1, t = 0. The population was 100 at the starting time.

  Q30. A delivery service uses two pricing zones. Zone A charges f(x) = 3x (dollars for x miles), and a fuel surcharge adds g(x) = x + 2. If the total cost is (g ∘ f)(x), what is the total cost for a 5-mile delivery?
    [ ] $15
    [*] $17
    [ ] $21
    [ ] $25
    Explanation: First compute f(5) = 3(5) = 15. Then g(15) = 15 + 2 = 17. So (g ∘ f)(5) = $17. The mileage charge is computed first, then the surcharge is applied.

--- Lesson 1.1: Review of Functions & Notation (Flashcards) ---

  1. Q: If f(x) = 2x + 3, what is f(5)?
     A: f(5) = 13. Substitute x=5: f(5) = 2(5) + 3 = 10 + 3 = 13.

  2. Q: What is the domain of f(x) = √(x - 4)?
     A: x ≥ 4. Radicand must be non-negative.

  3. Q: What is the range of f(x) = |x|?
     A: y ≥ 0. Absolute value is always non-negative.

  4. Q: Find (f ∘ g)(2) if f(x) = x² and g(x) = x + 1
     A: 9. (f ∘ g)(2) = f(g(2)) = f(3) = 9.

  5. Q: What is f⁻¹(x) if f(x) = 2x - 5?
     A: f⁻¹(x) = (x + 5)/2. Swap x and y, solve for y.

  6. Q: Is f(x) = 3x + 2 one-to-one?
     A: Yes. Linear functions with non-zero slope are one-to-one. Passes horizontal line test.

  7. Q: Find f(f⁻¹(7)) for any function f
     A: 7. Composing function with its inverse returns original input.

  8. Q: If f(2) = 5, what is the point on the graph?
     A: (2, 5). Graphs are plotted as (x, f(x)) points.

  9. Q: Determine if f(x) = x² is even or odd
     A: Even. f(-x) = f(x). Symmetric about y-axis.

  10. Q: Find the vertex of f(x) = (x - 3)² + 2
     A: (3, 2). Vertex form f(x) = a(x - h)² + k has vertex (h, k).

--- Lesson 1.2: Linear Equations & Graphing (Summary) ---

  Key Concepts: Linear Equations & Graphing
Overview
This lesson covers the fundamental measures of center used to analyze and summarize data sets. You'll learn how to calculate and apply the mean, median, and mode, and understand when each is most appropriate.
Key Definitions
What is the y-intercept of y = 4x - 7?
In slope-intercept form y = mx + b, the y-intercept is b. Here b = -7, so the graph crosses the y-axis at (0, -7).
What is the slope of the line 3x + 6y = 12?
Rewrite in slope-intercept form: 6y = -3x + 12, so y = -1/2 x + 2. The slope is -1/2.
What is the slope of a horizontal line?
A horizontal line has no rise (change in y = 0), so slope = 0/run = 0. Vertical lines, on the other hand, have undefined slope.
If a line passes through (1, 3) and (3, 7), what is its equation in slope-intercept form?
Slope = (7 - 3)/(3 - 1) = 4/2 = 2. Using point-slope with (1, 3): y - 3 = 2(x - 1), so y = 2x + 1.
What is the slope of a line perpendicular to y = (2/3)x + 4?
Perpendicular slopes are negative reciprocals. The negative reciprocal of 2/3 is -3/2.
What is slope-intercept form?
Slope-intercept form is y = mx + b. The coefficient m represents the slope (rate of change), and b represents the y-intercept (where the line crosses the y-axis).
What is point-slope form of a linear equation?
Point-slope form is y - y₁ = m(x - x₁), where m is the slope and (x₁, y₁) is a known point on the line. It is useful when you know one point and the slope.
What is a linear equation?
A linear equation in two variables is a first-degree equation whose graph is always a straight line. It can be written in the form Ax + By = C or y = mx + b.
What is the x-intercept of a graph?
The x-intercept is the point where a graph crosses the x-axis, meaning y = 0 at that point. To find it, substitute y = 0 into the equation and solve for x.
A phone plan costs $0.10 per text plus a $20 monthly fee. If a customer sent 150 texts, what is the total monthly bill?
Total = 0.10(150) + 20 = 15 + 20 = $35. The cost function is linear: C(t) = 0.10t + 20.
A car's value depreciates linearly from $24,000 to $12,000 over 6 years. What is the annual rate of depreciation?
Rate = (24,000 - 12,000)/6 = 12,000/6 = $2,000 per year. The slope of the value function V(t) = -2000t + 24000 is -2000.
A road rises 3 feet for every 100 feet of horizontal distance. What is the slope (grade) of the road, and is it steep or gentle?
Slope = rise/run = 3/100 = 0.03, which is a 3% grade. This is a gentle incline, typical of major highways.
A company's profit increases linearly. In year 1 profit was $10,000 and in year 5 it was $30,000. What is the profit in year 8?
Slope = (30000 - 10000)/(5 - 1) = 20000/4 = 5000 per year. Equation: P = 5000t + 5000. At t = 8: P = 5000(8) + 5000 = $45,000.

--- Lesson 1.2: Linear Equations & Graphing (Quiz) ---

  Q1. Find the slope between (2, 5) and (4, 11).
    [ ] 6
    [*] 3
    [ ] 2
    [ ] 1/3
    Explanation: Slope = (y₂ - y₁)/(x₂ - x₁) = (11 - 5)/(4 - 2) = 6/2 = 3.

  Q2. What is the y-intercept of y = 4x - 7?
    [ ] -4
    [ ] 4
    [*] -7
    [ ] 7
    Explanation: In slope-intercept form y = mx + b, the y-intercept is b. Here b = -7, so the graph crosses the y-axis at (0, -7).

  Q3. Write the equation of a line with slope 2 passing through (0, 5).
    [ ] y = 2x - 5
    [*] y = 2x + 5
    [ ] y = 5x + 2
    [ ] y = -2x + 5
    Explanation: Since the point (0, 5) is the y-intercept, use y = mx + b with m = 2 and b = 5 to get y = 2x + 5.

  Q4. What is the slope of the line 3x + 6y = 12?
    [ ] 3
    [*] -1/2
    [ ] -3
    [ ] 1/2
    Explanation: Rewrite in slope-intercept form: 6y = -3x + 12, so y = -1/2 x + 2. The slope is -1/2.

  Q5. Which line is parallel to y = 3x + 1?
    [ ] y = -3x + 4
    [*] y = 3x - 2
    [ ] y = -(1/3)x + 5
    [ ] y = (1/3)x + 1
    Explanation: Parallel lines have the same slope. The slope of y = 3x + 1 is 3, and y = 3x - 2 also has slope 3, so the lines are parallel.

  Q6. Find the x-intercept of the line 2x - 4y = 8.
    [ ] (0, 4)
    [ ] (0, -2)
    [ ] (-4, 0)
    [*] (4, 0)
    Explanation: Set y = 0: 2x - 4(0) = 8, so 2x = 8 and x = 4. The x-intercept is the point (4, 0).

  Q7. What is the slope of a horizontal line?
    [*] 0
    [ ] 1
    [ ] Undefined
    [ ] -1
    Explanation: A horizontal line has no rise (change in y = 0), so slope = 0/run = 0. Vertical lines, on the other hand, have undefined slope.

  Q8. If a line passes through (1, 3) and (3, 7), what is its equation in slope-intercept form?
    [ ] y = 2x + 3
    [ ] y = 2x - 1
    [*] y = 2x + 1
    [ ] y = x + 2
    Explanation: Slope = (7 - 3)/(3 - 1) = 4/2 = 2. Using point-slope with (1, 3): y - 3 = 2(x - 1), so y = 2x + 1.

  Q9. What is the slope of a line perpendicular to y = (2/3)x + 4?
    [*] -3/2
    [ ] 3/2
    [ ] -2/3
    [ ] 2/3
    Explanation: Perpendicular slopes are negative reciprocals. The negative reciprocal of 2/3 is -3/2.

  Q10. Convert 2x - y = 6 to slope-intercept form.
    [ ] y = -2x + 6
    [ ] y = 2x + 6
    [*] y = 2x - 6
    [ ] y = -2x - 6
    Explanation: Solve for y: -y = -2x + 6, so y = 2x - 6. The slope is 2 and the y-intercept is -6.

  Q11. What is slope-intercept form?
    [*] y = mx + b, where m is slope and b is y-intercept
    [ ] y - y₁ = m(x - x₁)
    [ ] y = a(x - h)² + k
    [ ] Ax + By = C, where A, B, C are constants
    Explanation: Slope-intercept form is y = mx + b. The coefficient m represents the slope (rate of change), and b represents the y-intercept (where the line crosses the y-axis).

  Q12. What does the slope of a line represent?
    [*] The rate of change of y with respect to x (rise over run)
    [ ] The point where the line crosses the x-axis
    [ ] The distance between two points
    [ ] The midpoint of the line segment
    Explanation: Slope measures the steepness and direction of a line. It is the ratio of vertical change (rise) to horizontal change (run) between any two points on the line: m = (y₂ - y₁)/(x₂ - x₁).

  Q13. What does 'y-intercept' mean?
    [ ] The slope of the line
    [*] The point where the line crosses the y-axis
    [ ] The point where the line crosses the x-axis
    [ ] The highest point on the graph
    Explanation: The y-intercept is the point where a graph crosses the y-axis. At this point, x = 0. In the equation y = mx + b, the y-intercept is the value b, giving the point (0, b).

  Q14. What is point-slope form of a linear equation?
    [ ] y = mx + b, particularly regarding
    [*] y - y₁ = m(x - x₁), using a known point and slope
    [ ] Ax + By = C, particularly regarding
    [ ] x/a + y/b = 1, particularly regarding
    Explanation: Point-slope form is y - y₁ = m(x - x₁), where m is the slope and (x₁, y₁) is a known point on the line. It is useful when you know one point and the slope.

  Q15. What does 'standard form' of a linear equation mean?
    [ ] y = mx + b
    [ ] y - y₁ = m(x - x₁)
    [*] Ax + By = C, where A, B, C are integers and A ≥ 0
    [ ] (x - h)² + (y - k)² = r²
    Explanation: Standard form of a linear equation is Ax + By = C, where A, B, and C are integers and A is typically non-negative. It is useful for finding intercepts and for systems of equations.

  Q16. What does it mean for two lines to be parallel?
    [ ] They intersect at exactly one point
    [*] They have the same slope but different y-intercepts
    [ ] Their slopes are negative reciprocals
    [ ] They are the same line
    Explanation: Two lines are parallel if and only if they have the same slope but different y-intercepts. Parallel lines never intersect — they maintain a constant distance apart.

  Q17. What does 'perpendicular' mean for two lines?
    [ ] They never intersect
    [ ] One is horizontal and the other has slope 1
    [*] They intersect at a 90-degree angle and have slopes that are negative reciprocals
    [ ] They have the same slope
    Explanation: Perpendicular lines meet at right angles (90°). Their slopes are negative reciprocals of each other: if one slope is m, the other is -1/m. For example, slopes of 2 and -1/2 are perpendicular.

  Q18. What is a linear equation?
    [*] An equation whose graph is a straight line
    [ ] An equation that contains an x² term
    [ ] Any equation with two variables
    [ ] An equation whose graph is a parabola
    Explanation: A linear equation in two variables is a first-degree equation whose graph is always a straight line. It can be written in the form Ax + By = C or y = mx + b.

  Q19. What is the x-intercept of a graph?
    [ ] The slope of the line
    [ ] The point where the graph crosses the y-axis
    [*] The point where the graph crosses the x-axis (where y = 0)
    [ ] The highest value of x
    Explanation: The x-intercept is the point where a graph crosses the x-axis, meaning y = 0 at that point. To find it, substitute y = 0 into the equation and solve for x.

  Q20. What does 'undefined slope' mean?
    [ ] The line is horizontal
    [ ] The line has a very steep slope
    [ ] The slope equals zero
    [*] The line is vertical, and division by zero occurs in the slope formula
    Explanation: A vertical line has an undefined slope because the run (change in x) is zero, and dividing by zero is undefined. The equation of a vertical line is x = c for some constant c.

  Q21. A plumber charges a $50 service fee plus $30 per hour. If the total bill is modeled by C(h) = 30h + 50, how much does a 4-hour job cost?
    [*] $170
    [ ] $200
    [ ] $120
    [ ] $80
    Explanation: Substitute h = 4: C(4) = 30(4) + 50 = 120 + 50 = $170. The slope of 30 represents the hourly rate, and the y-intercept of 50 is the service fee.

  Q22. A candle is 12 inches tall and burns at a rate of 0.5 inches per hour. The height is modeled by h(t) = -0.5t + 12. After how many hours will the candle be completely burned?
    [ ] 12 hours
    [*] 24 hours
    [ ] 6 hours
    [ ] 20 hours
    Explanation: Set h(t) = 0: -0.5t + 12 = 0, so 0.5t = 12, giving t = 24 hours. The negative slope means the height decreases over time.

  Q23. A phone plan costs $0.10 per text plus a $20 monthly fee. If a customer sent 150 texts, what is the total monthly bill?
    [ ] $170
    [ ] $30
    [ ] $15
    [*] $35
    Explanation: Total = 0.10(150) + 20 = 15 + 20 = $35. The cost function is linear: C(t) = 0.10t + 20.

  Q24. Two hikers start at the same trailhead. Hiker A walks at 3 mph along a trail modeled by y = 3x. Hiker B starts 2 miles ahead and walks at 2 mph, modeled by y = 2x + 2. When will Hiker A catch Hiker B?
    [ ] 3 hours
    [ ] 1 hour
    [ ] 4 hours
    [*] 2 hours
    Explanation: Set 3x = 2x + 2. Subtract 2x from both sides: x = 2. Hiker A catches Hiker B after 2 hours when both are 6 miles from the trailhead.

  Q25. A car's value depreciates linearly from $24,000 to $12,000 over 6 years. What is the annual rate of depreciation?
    [ ] $3,000 per year
    [*] $2,000 per year
    [ ] $1,000 per year
    [ ] $4,000 per year
    Explanation: Rate = (24,000 - 12,000)/6 = 12,000/6 = $2,000 per year. The slope of the value function V(t) = -2000t + 24000 is -2000.

  Q26. A swimming pool is being filled at a rate of 500 gallons per hour. It already has 2,000 gallons. The equation W(t) = 500t + 2000 gives the water level. How long until the 10,000-gallon pool is full?
    [ ] 20 hours
    [*] 16 hours
    [ ] 12 hours
    [ ] 10 hours
    Explanation: Set 500t + 2000 = 10000. Subtract 2000: 500t = 8000. Divide by 500: t = 16 hours.

  Q27. A road rises 3 feet for every 100 feet of horizontal distance. What is the slope (grade) of the road, and is it steep or gentle?
    [ ] 33.3 — an extremely steep grade
    [ ] 0.3 — a moderate grade
    [*] 0.03 — a gentle grade
    [ ] 3 — a very steep grade
    Explanation: Slope = rise/run = 3/100 = 0.03, which is a 3% grade. This is a gentle incline, typical of major highways.

  Q28. A taxi meter shows the fare equation F = 2.50m + 3.00, where m is miles driven. If two riders each pay half of an 8-mile fare, how much does each pay?
    [ ] $13.00
    [*] $11.50
    [ ] $11.00
    [ ] $23.00
    Explanation: F = 2.50(8) + 3.00 = 20.00 + 3.00 = $23.00 total. Each rider pays $23.00/2 = $11.50.

  Q29. A company's profit increases linearly. In year 1 profit was $10,000 and in year 5 it was $30,000. What is the profit in year 8?
    [ ] $50,000
    [*] $45,000
    [ ] $35,000
    [ ] $40,000
    Explanation: Slope = (30000 - 10000)/(5 - 1) = 20000/4 = 5000 per year. Equation: P = 5000t + 5000. At t = 8: P = 5000(8) + 5000 = $45,000.

  Q30. An elevator starts at floor 1 and rises 2 floors every 5 seconds. After 30 seconds, which floor is it on?
    [ ] Floor 7
    [ ] Floor 11
    [ ] Floor 12
    [*] Floor 13
    Explanation: Rate = 2 floors / 5 seconds = 0.4 floors/sec. After 30 sec: floors climbed = 0.4(30) = 12. Starting at floor 1: 1 + 12 = floor 13.

--- Lesson 1.2: Linear Equations & Graphing (Flashcards) ---

  1. Q: Find slope between (1, 2) and (4, 8)
     A: m = 2. m = (8-2)/(4-1) = 6/3 = 2.

  2. Q: Write equation in slope-intercept form: slope = 3, y-intercept = -2
     A: y = 3x - 2. Form: y = mx + b.

  3. Q: Find slope of x + 2y = 6
     A: m = -1/2. Rewrite: y = -x/2 + 3.

  4. Q: Find equation using point-slope: m = 4, point (2, 5)
     A: y - 5 = 4(x - 2) or y = 4x - 3. Use y - y₁ = m(x - x₁).

  5. Q: What is the x-intercept of y = 2x - 6?
     A: 3. Set y = 0: 0 = 2x - 6, so x = 3. Point: (3, 0).

  6. Q: Find equation of line parallel to y = 3x + 1 through (0, 5)
     A: y = 3x + 5. Parallel lines have same slope.

  7. Q: Find equation of line perpendicular to y = 2x - 1 through (1, 2)
     A: y - 2 = -1/2(x - 1) or y = -x/2 + 5/2. Perpendicular slopes: m₁ · m₂ = -1.

  8. Q: Is the line through (0,1), (1,3), (2,5) linear?
     A: Yes. Constant slope m = 2 between all points indicates linearity.

  9. Q: Solve for slope: line passes (a, b) and (a+1, b+2)
     A: m = 2. Slope = (b+2-b)/(a+1-a) = 2/1 = 2.

  10. Q: Find line through (3, 4) and (-1, 2)
     A: y - 4 = 1/2(x - 3) or y = x/2 + 5/2. m = (2-4)/(-1-3) = -2/-4 = 1/2.

--- Lesson 1.3: Systems of Linear Equations (Summary) ---

  Key Concepts: Systems of Linear Equations
Overview
This lesson covers the fundamental measures of center used to analyze and summarize data sets. You'll learn how to calculate and apply the mean, median, and mode, and understand when each is most appropriate.
Key Definitions
What is the solution of x - y = 4 and 2x + y = 8?
Add the equations: 3x = 12, so x = 4. Substitute: 4 - y = 4, so y = 0.
What is a system of linear equations?
A system of linear equations is a set of two or more linear equations involving the same set of variables. The solution is the set of values that satisfies all equations simultaneously.
What is the graphical meaning of the solution to a system of two linear equations?
The solution to a system of linear equations corresponds to the point(s) of intersection of their graphs. Each intersection point satisfies both equations simultaneously.
What is the 'elimination method' for solving systems?
The elimination method involves adding or subtracting equations (sometimes after multiplying by constants) so that one variable cancels out, leaving a single equation in one variable to solve.
What is the 'substitution method' for solving systems?
In the substitution method, you isolate one variable in one equation, then replace that variable in the other equation with the resulting expression. This gives a single equation in one variable.
What is the 'graphing method' for solving a system?
The graphing method involves graphing each equation on the same coordinate plane. The point(s) of intersection represent the solution(s). This method is visual but may lack precision for non-integer solutions.
A boat travels 24 miles downstream in 2 hours and 24 miles upstream in 3 hours. What is the speed of the boat in still water?
Downstream: b + c = 24/2 = 12. Upstream: b - c = 24/3 = 8. Add: 2b = 20, so b = 10 mph. The current is 2 mph.

--- Lesson 1.3: Systems of Linear Equations (Quiz) ---

  Q1. Solve the system: x + y = 5 and x - y = 1.
    [ ] x = 4, y = 1
    [ ] x = 2, y = 3
    [*] x = 3, y = 2
    [ ] x = 1, y = 4
    Explanation: Add the two equations: 2x = 6, so x = 3. Substitute back: 3 + y = 5, so y = 2.

  Q2. How many solutions does the system y = 2x + 1 and y = 2x + 5 have?
    [ ] Two, particularly
    [ ] Infinitely many
    [*] None — the lines are parallel
    [ ] One, particularly
    Explanation: Both lines have slope 2 but different y-intercepts (1 and 5), so they are parallel and never intersect. The system is inconsistent with no solution.

  Q3. Solve: 2x + 3y = 12 and x = 3.
    [ ] x = 3, y = 3
    [ ] x = 3, y = 4
    [ ] x = 3, y = 1
    [*] x = 3, y = 2
    Explanation: Substitute x = 3 into 2(3) + 3y = 12: 6 + 3y = 12, so 3y = 6 and y = 2.

  Q4. What is the solution of x - y = 4 and 2x + y = 8?
    [ ] x = 2, y = 4
    [ ] x = 0, y = -4
    [*] x = 4, y = 0
    [ ] x = 3, y = 2
    Explanation: Add the equations: 3x = 12, so x = 4. Substitute: 4 - y = 4, so y = 0.

  Q5. If two lines intersect at exactly one point, the system is called:
    [ ] Dependent
    [ ] Inconsistent
    [ ] Undefined
    [*] Independent and consistent
    Explanation: A system with exactly one solution is consistent (has a solution) and independent (the equations describe different lines). The intersection point is the unique solution.

  Q6. Solve: y = x + 2 and y = -x + 6.
    [ ] x = 3, y = 3
    [*] x = 2, y = 4
    [ ] x = 1, y = 5
    [ ] x = 4, y = 2
    Explanation: Set x + 2 = -x + 6: 2x = 4, so x = 2. Then y = 2 + 2 = 4.

  Q7. The system y = 3x + 2 and 2y = 6x + 4 has how many solutions?
    [ ] Two, particu
    [ ] One, particu
    [*] Infinitely many
    [ ] None, partic
    Explanation: Divide the second equation by 2: y = 3x + 2. Both equations are the same line, so there are infinitely many solutions (dependent system).

  Q8. Solve: 3x + y = 10 and x - y = 2.
    [*] x = 3, y = 1
    [ ] x = 1, y = 7
    [ ] x = 4, y = -2
    [ ] x = 2, y = 4
    Explanation: Add equations: 4x = 12, so x = 3. Substitute: 3 - y = 2, so y = 1.

  Q9. Where do the lines y = 2x - 1 and y = -x + 5 intersect?
    [ ] (1, 4)
    [*] (2, 3)
    [ ] (3, 2)
    [ ] (4, 1)
    Explanation: Set 2x - 1 = -x + 5: 3x = 6, so x = 2. Then y = 2(2) - 1 = 3. The intersection is (2, 3).

  Q10. Solve: x + 2y = 7 and 3x - 2y = 5.
    [*] x = 3, y = 2
    [ ] x = 5, y = 1
    [ ] x = 1, y = 3
    [ ] x = 2, y = 3
    Explanation: Add the equations: 4x = 12, so x = 3. Substitute: 3 + 2y = 7, so 2y = 4 and y = 2.

  Q11. What is a system of linear equations?
    [ ] Two equations that are always parallel
    [ ] An equation with no solution
    [*] Two or more linear equations with the same variables considered together
    [ ] A single equation with two variables
    Explanation: A system of linear equations is a set of two or more linear equations involving the same set of variables. The solution is the set of values that satisfies all equations simultaneously.

  Q12. What does 'consistent system' mean?
    [ ] A system that has no solution
    [ ] A system where both equations are the same
    [ ] A system with perpendicular lines
    [*] A system that has at least one solution
    Explanation: A consistent system has at least one solution — either exactly one (independent) or infinitely many (dependent). If the lines intersect or overlap, the system is consistent.

  Q13. What does 'inconsistent system' mean?
    [ ] A system with dependent equations
    [ ] A system with infinitely many solutions
    [ ] A system with exactly one solution
    [*] A system with no solution because the lines are parallel
    Explanation: An inconsistent system has no solution. This occurs when the lines are parallel (same slope, different y-intercepts) and never intersect.

  Q14. What does 'dependent system' mean?
    [ ] A system with no solution
    [ ] A system where one equation depends on a third variable
    [*] A system where both equations represent the same line, giving infinitely many solutions
    [ ] A system with exactly two solutions
    Explanation: A dependent system consists of equations that describe the same line. Every point on that line is a solution, so there are infinitely many solutions.

  Q15. What is the graphical meaning of the solution to a system of two linear equations?
    [ ] The slope of both lines
    [*] The point(s) where the two lines intersect
    [ ] The y-intercept of the first line
    [ ] The midpoint between the two lines
    Explanation: The solution to a system of linear equations corresponds to the point(s) of intersection of their graphs. Each intersection point satisfies both equations simultaneously.

  Q16. What does 'independent system' mean?
    [ ] A system with infinitely many solutions
    [ ] A system with no solution
    [ ] A system that cannot be solved
    [*] A system where the equations represent different lines with exactly one solution
    Explanation: An independent system has equations that represent distinct lines with different slopes. These lines intersect at exactly one point, giving a unique solution.

  Q17. What is the 'elimination method' for solving systems?
    [*] Adding or subtracting equations to eliminate one variable
    [ ] Graphing both lines and finding their intersection
    [ ] Solving one equation for a variable and plugging into the other
    [ ] Using matrices to find the solution
    Explanation: The elimination method involves adding or subtracting equations (sometimes after multiplying by constants) so that one variable cancels out, leaving a single equation in one variable to solve.

  Q18. What is the 'substitution method' for solving systems?
    [*] Solving one equation for one variable and substituting into the other equation
    [ ] Checking all integer solutions
    [ ] Adding equations together
    [ ] Graphing both equations to find the intersection
    Explanation: In the substitution method, you isolate one variable in one equation, then replace that variable in the other equation with the resulting expression. This gives a single equation in one variable.

  Q19. What does it mean to 'solve a system of equations'?
    [*] To find all ordered pairs (x, y) that satisfy every equation in the system
    [ ] To simplify each equation separately
    [ ] To rewrite the equations in standard form
    [ ] To graph the equations
    Explanation: Solving a system means finding all values of the variables that make every equation in the system true at the same time. This set of values is called the solution of the system.

  Q20. What is the 'graphing method' for solving a system?
    [ ] Using algebra to combine two equations
    [*] Plotting both equations on the same coordinate plane and identifying intersection points
    [ ] Using matrices to solve the system
    [ ] Substituting values until you find the answer
    Explanation: The graphing method involves graphing each equation on the same coordinate plane. The point(s) of intersection represent the solution(s). This method is visual but may lack precision for non-integer solutions.

  Q21. A movie theater sells adult tickets for $10 and child tickets for $6. If 50 tickets were sold for a total of $380, how many adult tickets were sold?
    [ ] 25
    [ ] 32
    [ ] 18
    [*] 20
    Explanation: Let a = adult, c = child. System: a + c = 50 and 10a + 6c = 380. From the first: c = 50 - a. Substitute: 10a + 6(50 - a) = 380 → 4a = 80 → a = 20. Verify: 10(20) + 6(30) = 200 + 180 = 380.

  Q22. A store sells notebooks for $3 and pens for $1. A student buys 10 items for $18. How many notebooks were purchased?
    [ ] 6
    [ ] 3
    [*] 4
    [ ] 5
    Explanation: Let n = notebooks and p = pens. n + p = 10 and 3n + p = 18. Subtract: 2n = 8, so n = 4. The student bought 4 notebooks and 6 pens.

  Q23. Two friends are 60 miles apart and drive toward each other. One drives 40 mph and the other 20 mph. When do they meet?
    [ ] 3 hours
    [ ] 2 hours
    [*] 1 hour
    [ ] 1.5 hours
    Explanation: Combined speed is 40 + 20 = 60 mph. Distance = rate × time: 60 = 60t, so t = 1 hour.

  Q24. A farmer has chickens and cows. He counts 30 heads and 80 legs. How many cows does he have?
    [ ] 15
    [*] 10
    [ ] 12
    [ ] 20
    Explanation: Let c = chickens and w = cows. c + w = 30 and 2c + 4w = 80. From the first: c = 30 - w. Substitute: 2(30 - w) + 4w = 80 → 60 - 2w + 4w = 80 → 2w = 20 → w = 10 cows.

  Q25. A chemist mixes a 20% acid solution with a 50% acid solution to get 30 liters of a 30% solution. How many liters of the 20% solution are needed?
    [ ] 10 liters
    [*] 20 liters
    [ ] 25 liters
    [ ] 15 liters
    Explanation: Let x = liters of 20%, y = liters of 50%. System: x + y = 30 and 0.20x + 0.50y = 9. From the first: y = 30 - x. Substitute: 0.20x + 0.50(30 - x) = 9 → 0.20x + 15 - 0.50x = 9 → -0.30x = -6 → x = 20 liters.

  Q26. A concert has $5 lawn seats and $15 reserved seats. If 200 tickets generate $2,000 in revenue, how many reserved seats were sold?
    [ ] 75
    [ ] 50
    [*] 100
    [ ] 150
    Explanation: Let L = lawn, R = reserved. L + R = 200 and 5L + 15R = 2000. Substitute L = 200 - R: 5(200 - R) + 15R = 2000 → 1000 + 10R = 2000 → R = 100.

  Q27. A school is ordering pizzas and drinks for a party. Pizzas cost $12 each and drinks cost $2 each. They order 20 items for $120. How many pizzas did they order?
    [ ] 6
    [ ] 12
    [*] 8
    [ ] 10
    Explanation: Let p = pizzas, d = drinks. p + d = 20 and 12p + 2d = 120. From the first: d = 20 - p. Substitute: 12p + 2(20 - p) = 120 → 12p + 40 - 2p = 120 → 10p = 80 → p = 8.

  Q28. A boat travels 24 miles downstream in 2 hours and 24 miles upstream in 3 hours. What is the speed of the boat in still water?
    [ ] 6 mph
    [*] 10 mph
    [ ] 12 mph
    [ ] 8 mph
    Explanation: Downstream: b + c = 24/2 = 12. Upstream: b - c = 24/3 = 8. Add: 2b = 20, so b = 10 mph. The current is 2 mph.

  Q29. A cashier has $5 bills and $10 bills totaling $95. She has 13 bills in all. How many $10 bills does she have?
    [ ] 7
    [ ] 4
    [*] 6
    [ ] 8
    Explanation: Let f = number of $5 bills, t = number of $10 bills. f + t = 13 and 5f + 10t = 95. From the first: f = 13 - t. Substitute: 5(13 - t) + 10t = 95 → 65 - 5t + 10t = 95 → 5t = 30 → t = 6.

  Q30. An investment of $5,000 is split between two accounts. One earns 4% interest and the other 6%. If the total annual interest is $260, how much was invested at 6%?
    [ ] $2,000
    [*] $3,000
    [ ] $4,000
    [ ] $2,500
    Explanation: Let x = amount at 4%, y = amount at 6%. x + y = 5000 and 0.04x + 0.06y = 260. Substitute x = 5000 - y: 0.04(5000 - y) + 0.06y = 260 → 200 - 0.04y + 0.06y = 260 → 0.02y = 60 → y = $3,000.

--- Lesson 1.3: Systems of Linear Equations (Flashcards) ---

  1. Q: Solve graphically: solution is intersection of y = x + 1 and y = -x + 3
     A: (1, 2). Check: (1) + 1 = 2 and -(1) + 3 = 2. ✓

  2. Q: Classify: x + y = 5 and 2x + 2y = 10
     A: Dependent (infinitely many solutions). Second is 2× the first, same line.

  3. Q: Classify: x + y = 3 and x + y = 5
     A: Inconsistent (no solution). Parallel lines, never intersect.

  4. Q: Solve by substitution: y = 2x and x + y = 9
     A: x = 3, y = 6. Substitute: x + 2x = 9, so 3x = 9.

  5. Q: Find intersection of x = 2 and y = -3
     A: (2, -3). Vertical and horizontal lines intersect at point.

  6. Q: Is (1, 1) a solution to 2x + 3y = 5?
     A: Yes. 2(1) + 3(1) = 5. ✓

  7. Q: How many solutions for consistent and independent system?
     A: Exactly one. Lines intersect at single point.

  8. Q: Solve: 2x - y = 4 and y = 2x - 4
     A: Dependent system, infinitely many solutions. Equations are identical.

  9. Q: Find point where y = 1/2·x intersects y = x - 1
     A: (2, 1). 1/2·x = x - 1 gives x/2 = 1, so x = 2.

  10. Q: What does a fake equation in system indicate?
     A: No solution (inconsistent). Example: 0 = 5 is impossible.

--- Lesson 1.4: Solving Systems by Substitution (Summary) ---

  Key Concepts: Solving Systems by Substitution
Overview
This lesson covers the fundamental measures of center used to analyze and summarize data sets. You'll learn how to calculate and apply the mean, median, and mode, and understand when each is most appropriate.
Key Definitions
What is the substitution method for solving systems of equations?
The substitution method involves isolating one variable in one equation and then replacing (substituting) that expression into the other equation, creating a single-variable equation that can be solved directly.
What is a 'solution to a system' of equations?
A solution to a system is an ordered pair (x, y) that makes every equation in the system true when the values are substituted in. It represents the point where all equations intersect.
What is an ordered pair?
An ordered pair (x, y) represents a point in the coordinate plane where x is the horizontal position and y is the vertical position. The order matters — (2, 3) is different from (3, 2).
What is a 'linear expression'?
A linear expression is one where variables appear only to the first power — like 3x + 2 or 5y - 1. There are no squared terms, square roots, or other nonlinear operations on the variables.
Real-World Applications
Example: A parking garage charges $3 for the first hour and $2 for each additional hour. If the total charge is C = 2h + 1 (where h is total hours), and a second garage charges C = 3h - 2, after how many hours do both garages charge the same amount?
Set 2h + 1 = 3h - 2: 1 + 2 = 3h - 2h → h = 3. After 3 hours both charge $7.
Example: A student scores y = 2x + 60 on a math test and y = -x + 90 on a science test, where x is hours of study. For how many hours of study will the scores be equal?
Set 2x + 60 = -x + 90: 3x = 30 → x = 10. Both scores equal 80 at 10 hours of study.

--- Lesson 1.4: Solving Systems by Substitution (Quiz) ---

  Q1. Solve by substitution: x = 2y and x + y = 9.
    [ ] y = 6, x = 3
    [ ] y = 2, x = 9
    [*] y = 3, x = 6
    [ ] y = 1, x = 2
    Explanation: Substitute x = 2y into x + y = 9: 2y + y = 9, so 3y = 9 and y = 3. Then x = 2(3) = 6.

  Q2. From y = 3x - 1, substitute into 2x + y = 9. What equation results?
    [ ] 2x + 3x + 1 = 9
    [ ] 2x - 3x + 1 = 9
    [ ] 2x(3x - 1) = 9
    [*] 2x + 3x - 1 = 9
    Explanation: Replace y with (3x - 1) in the second equation: 2x + (3x - 1) = 9. This is a direct substitution — replace the variable, not multiply.

  Q3. Solve by substitution: y = x + 4 and 2x + y = 10.
    [ ] x = 1, y = 5
    [ ] x = 4, y = 8
    [*] x = 2, y = 6
    [ ] x = 3, y = 7
    Explanation: Substitute y = x + 4 into 2x + y = 10: 2x + (x + 4) = 10 → 3x + 4 = 10 → 3x = 6 → x = 2. Then y = 2 + 4 = 6.

  Q4. Solve: x = 5 - y and 3x + 2y = 12.
    [ ] x = 4, y = 1
    [*] x = 2, y = 3
    [ ] x = 3, y = 2
    [ ] x = 1, y = 4
    Explanation: Substitute x = 5 - y into 3x + 2y = 12: 3(5 - y) + 2y = 12 → 15 - 3y + 2y = 12 → -y = -3 → y = 3. Then x = 5 - 3 = 2.

  Q5. Solve: y = -2x + 7 and y = x + 1.
    [*] x = 2, y = 3
    [ ] x = 4, y = 5
    [ ] x = 3, y = 4
    [ ] x = 1, y = 5
    Explanation: Set -2x + 7 = x + 1: -3x = -6, so x = 2. Then y = 2 + 1 = 3.

  Q6. Solve: 2x + y = 8 and y = x - 1.
    [ ] x = 5, y = 4
    [*] x = 3, y = 2
    [ ] x = 4, y = 3
    [ ] x = 2, y = 1
    Explanation: Substitute y = x - 1 into 2x + y = 8: 2x + (x - 1) = 8 → 3x - 1 = 8 → 3x = 9 → x = 3. Then y = 3 - 1 = 2.

  Q7. Solve: x + 3y = 11 and x = y + 3.
    [ ] x = 8, y = 1
    [ ] x = 3, y = 0
    [*] x = 5, y = 2
    [ ] x = 6, y = 3
    Explanation: Substitute x = y + 3 into x + 3y = 11: (y + 3) + 3y = 11 → 4y + 3 = 11 → 4y = 8 → y = 2. Then x = 2 + 3 = 5.

  Q8. Solve: y = 4x and 3x + y = 14.
    [ ] x = 3, y = 12
    [*] x = 2, y = 8
    [ ] x = 4, y = 16
    [ ] x = 1, y = 4
    Explanation: Substitute y = 4x into 3x + y = 14: 3x + 4x = 14 → 7x = 14 → x = 2. Then y = 4(2) = 8.

  Q9. Solve: x - y = 3 and 2x + 3y = 16.
    [ ] x = 4, y = 1
    [ ] x = 3, y = 0
    [ ] x = 7, y = 4
    [*] x = 5, y = 2
    Explanation: From the first equation: x = y + 3. Substitute into 2(y + 3) + 3y = 16 → 2y + 6 + 3y = 16 → 5y = 10 → y = 2. Then x = 2 + 3 = 5.

  Q10. Solve: 4x - y = 5 and y = 2x + 1.
    [ ] x = 1, y = 3
    [*] x = 3, y = 7
    [ ] x = 4, y = 9
    [ ] x = 2, y = 5
    Explanation: Substitute y = 2x + 1 into 4x - y = 5: 4x - (2x + 1) = 5 → 2x - 1 = 5 → 2x = 6 → x = 3. Then y = 2(3) + 1 = 7.

  Q11. What is the substitution method for solving systems of equations?
    [ ] Graphing both equations and finding the intersection
    [*] Solving one equation for one variable and replacing that variable in the other equation
    [ ] Multiplying both equations by the same constant
    [ ] Adding the two equations together
    Explanation: The substitution method involves isolating one variable in one equation and then replacing (substituting) that expression into the other equation, creating a single-variable equation that can be solved directly.

  Q12. What does 'isolate a variable' mean?
    [ ] Substitute a number for the variable
    [ ] Set the variable equal to zero
    [*] Rewrite the equation so one variable is alone on one side
    [ ] Remove the variable from the equation
    Explanation: Isolating a variable means rearranging an equation so that the chosen variable appears by itself on one side of the equals sign. For example, solving x + y = 5 for x gives x = 5 - y.

  Q13. What does it mean to 'substitute' in algebra?
    [ ] To eliminate a variable by adding equations
    [ ] To graph an equation
    [*] To replace a variable or expression with an equivalent value or expression
    [ ] To factor an expression
    Explanation: Substitution means replacing a variable with a number or an equivalent expression. In systems, if y = 3x, you substitute 3x for y in the other equation.

  Q14. What is a 'solution to a system' of equations?
    [ ] The slope of the lines
    [ ] Any ordered pair that satisfies the first equation
    [*] An ordered pair that satisfies all equations in the system simultaneously
    [ ] The y-intercept of any equation in the system
    Explanation: A solution to a system is an ordered pair (x, y) that makes every equation in the system true when the values are substituted in. It represents the point where all equations intersect.

  Q15. When is the substitution method most convenient to use?
    [ ] When the coefficients of one variable are opposites
    [ ] When you need an approximate answer
    [*] When one equation is already solved for a variable or can be easily solved for one
    [ ] When both equations are in standard form with large coefficients
    Explanation: Substitution is most efficient when one equation is already solved for a variable (like y = 3x + 2) or when a variable has a coefficient of 1 or -1, making it easy to isolate.

  Q16. What does 'back-substitution' mean?
    [*] Plugging the found value back into an equation to find the other variable
    [ ] Substituting in reverse order
    [ ] Checking if the answer is correct by graphing
    [ ] Undoing a substitution step
    Explanation: Back-substitution is the step where, after finding one variable's value, you plug it back into one of the original equations to find the remaining variable. It completes the solution process.

  Q17. What is an ordered pair?
    [*] Two numbers listed in a specific order, written as (x, y)
    [ ] Any two numbers added together
    [ ] The slope and y-intercept of a line
    [ ] Two equations solved simultaneously
    Explanation: An ordered pair (x, y) represents a point in the coordinate plane where x is the horizontal position and y is the vertical position. The order matters — (2, 3) is different from (3, 2).

  Q18. What does 'equivalent equations' mean?
    [*] Equations that have the same solution set
    [ ] Equations with the same slope
    [ ] Equations that are always true
    [ ] Equations that look the same
    Explanation: Equivalent equations have exactly the same set of solutions. For example, 2x = 6 and x = 3 are equivalent because both have the single solution x = 3.

  Q19. What does 'verify a solution' mean in the context of systems?
    [ ] Graph the solution
    [*] Substitute the solution into all original equations to confirm they are true
    [ ] Solve the system again using a different method
    [ ] Round the answer to the nearest integer
    Explanation: Verifying a solution means plugging the values back into each original equation to make sure both sides are equal. This confirms the answer is correct and no arithmetic errors were made.

  Q20. What is a 'linear expression'?
    [ ] An expression with a radical
    [ ] An expression with no variables
    [*] An expression where the variable has degree one (no exponents greater than 1)
    [ ] An expression containing a squared variable
    Explanation: A linear expression is one where variables appear only to the first power — like 3x + 2 or 5y - 1. There are no squared terms, square roots, or other nonlinear operations on the variables.

  Q21. A parking garage charges $3 for the first hour and $2 for each additional hour. If the total charge is C = 2h + 1 (where h is total hours), and a second garage charges C = 3h - 2, after how many hours do both garages charge the same amount?
    [*] 3 hours
    [ ] 5 hours
    [ ] 4 hours
    [ ] 2 hours
    Explanation: Set 2h + 1 = 3h - 2: 1 + 2 = 3h - 2h → h = 3. After 3 hours both charge $7.

  Q22. A tutoring center offers Plan A at $20/session and Plan B at $15/session plus a $30 registration fee. If a student attends s sessions, when do both plans cost the same?
    [ ] 10 sessions
    [ ] 4 sessions
    [*] 6 sessions
    [ ] 8 sessions
    Explanation: Plan A: C = 20s. Plan B: C = 15s + 30. Set equal: 20s = 15s + 30 → 5s = 30 → s = 6 sessions. Both cost $120.

  Q23. A pet store sells fish for $2 each and hamsters for $8 each. Maria buys 7 pets for $26. How many fish did she buy?
    [*] 5
    [ ] 6
    [ ] 3
    [ ] 4
    Explanation: Let f = fish, h = hamsters. f + h = 7 and 2f + 8h = 26. From the first: h = 7 - f. Substitute: 2f + 8(7 - f) = 26 → 2f + 56 - 8f = 26 → -6f = -30 → f = 5.

  Q24. A baker uses 2 cups of flour per loaf of bread and 3 cups per batch of cookies. She uses 24 cups total and makes 10 items. How many batches of cookies did she make?
    [ ] 3
    [ ] 5
    [ ] 6
    [*] 4
    Explanation: Let b = loaves, c = cookie batches. b + c = 10 and 2b + 3c = 24. From the first: b = 10 - c. Substitute: 2(10 - c) + 3c = 24 → 20 - 2c + 3c = 24 → c = 4.

  Q25. Two cell phone plans are being compared. Plan X charges $40/month plus $0.10/text, and Plan Y charges $25/month plus $0.25/text. For how many texts per month are they equal?
    [ ] 150 texts
    [ ] 75 texts
    [*] 100 texts
    [ ] 50 texts
    Explanation: Set 40 + 0.10t = 25 + 0.25t: 15 = 0.15t → t = 100 texts. Both plans cost $50 at 100 texts.

  Q26. A student scores y = 2x + 60 on a math test and y = -x + 90 on a science test, where x is hours of study. For how many hours of study will the scores be equal?
    [ ] 5 hours
    [ ] 15 hours
    [*] 10 hours
    [ ] 8 hours
    Explanation: Set 2x + 60 = -x + 90: 3x = 30 → x = 10. Both scores equal 80 at 10 hours of study.

  Q27. A juice stand mixes apple juice at $3/liter with grape juice at $5/liter to make 8 liters of a blend costing $3.50/liter. How many liters of apple juice are used?
    [ ] 4 liters
    [*] 6 liters
    [ ] 5 liters
    [ ] 3 liters
    Explanation: Let a = apple, g = grape. a + g = 8 and 3a + 5g = 28 (since 8 × 3.50 = 28). Substitute g = 8 - a: 3a + 5(8 - a) = 28 → 3a + 40 - 5a = 28 → -2a = -12 → a = 6.

  Q28. A rental company offers trucks for $30/day plus $0.20/mile and vans for $45/day plus $0.10/mile. After how many miles in one day does the truck cost the same as the van?
    [ ] 100 miles
    [*] 150 miles
    [ ] 200 miles
    [ ] 75 miles
    Explanation: Set 30 + 0.20m = 45 + 0.10m: 0.10m = 15 → m = 150 miles. At 150 miles both cost $60.

  Q29. A theater group sold 120 tickets. Adult tickets cost $8 and student tickets cost $5. Total revenue was $780. Using substitution, find how many student tickets were sold.
    [ ] 40
    [ ] 80
    [*] 60
    [ ] 50
    Explanation: Let a = adult, s = student. a + s = 120, so a = 120 - s. Substitute: 8(120 - s) + 5s = 780 → 960 - 3s = 780 → -3s = -180 → s = 60.

  Q30. An electrician charges a $50 call-out fee plus $35/hour. A plumber charges a $20 call-out fee plus $45/hour. After how many hours will they charge the same total?
    [ ] 2 hours
    [ ] 4 hours
    [*] 3 hours
    [ ] 5 hours
    Explanation: Set 50 + 35h = 20 + 45h: 30 = 10h → h = 3. Both charge $155 after 3 hours.

--- Lesson 1.4: Solving Systems by Substitution (Flashcards) ---

  1. Q: Solve by substitution: x = 3y + 1 and 2x - y = 5
     A: y = 1/7, x = 10/7. Substitute first into second.

  2. Q: Steps for substitution method?
     A: (1) Solve one equation for a variable, (2) Substitute into other, (3) Solve, (4) Back-substitute.

  3. Q: Solve: y = 2x and x - y = -3
     A: x = -3/1 = -3? No: x - 2x = -3, so -x = -3, x = 3, y = 6.

  4. Q: Solve: 2x + y = 11 and y = x + 2
     A: x = 3, y = 5. Substitute: 2x + (x+2) = 11 gives 3x = 9.

  5. Q: Word problem setup: pencils $0.25, pens $0.75, 20 items, $12 total. Equations?
     A: x + y = 20 and 0.25x + 0.75y = 12. Let x=pencils, y=pens.

  6. Q: Solve previous: how many pens?
     A: 10 pens (y=10). From equations: x=10, y=10.

  7. Q: Check solution x=2, y=3 in 2x + y = 7
     A: 2(2) + 3 = 7. âœ“ Solution is correct.

  8. Q: Solve: 3x - 2y = 4 and x = y + 1
     A: x = 2, y = 1. Substitute: 3(y+1) - 2y = 4 gives y = 1.

  9. Q: Why not divide by coefficient during substitution?
     A: Can cause fractions. Better to express one variable without division when possible.

  10. Q: Solve: 5x + y = 12 and y = -5x + 2
     A: Inconsistent (no solution, inconsistent equations). Leads to 0 = 10.

--- Lesson 1.5: Solving Systems by Elimination (Summary) ---

  Key Concepts: Solving Systems by Elimination
Overview
This lesson covers the fundamental measures of center used to analyze and summarize data sets. You'll learn how to calculate and apply the mean, median, and mode, and understand when each is most appropriate.
Key Definitions
What is the elimination method for solving systems?
The elimination method (also called the addition method) involves adding or subtracting the equations so that one variable is eliminated, leaving a single equation in one unknown.
What is a 'linear combination' of two equations?
A linear combination is formed by multiplying equations by constants and adding the results. This technique is the foundation of the elimination method for solving systems.
What is the 'addition property of equality'?
The addition property of equality states that if two equations are true, their sides can be added. This principle justifies the elimination method — you can add entire equations together.
What is a 'contradiction' when solving a system?
A contradiction (like 0 = 5) arises when the system has no solution — the lines are parallel. This means the system is inconsistent.
What is an 'identity' when solving a system?
When elimination produces a true identity like 0 = 0, both equations represent the same line, and every point on that line is a solution — giving infinitely many solutions.
A plane flies 600 miles with the wind in 2 hours and 600 miles against the wind in 3 hours. What is the plane's speed in still air?
With wind: p + w = 300. Against wind: p - w = 200. Add: 2p = 500 → p = 250 mph. The wind speed is 50 mph.
A farmer buys 6 bags of seed and 4 bags of fertilizer for $164. He later buys 3 bags of seed and 4 bags of fertilizer for $116. What is the cost of one bag of seed?
Let s = seed cost, f = fertilizer cost. 6s + 4f = 164 and 3s + 4f = 116. Subtract: 3s = 48 → s = $16.
Real-World Applications
Example: To eliminate x from x + 3y = 7 and 2x + y = 4, multiply the first equation by:
Multiply the first equation by -2 to get -2x - 6y = -14. Adding to 2x + y = 4 eliminates x: -5y = -10, so y = 2.
Example: What does 'LCM' (least common multiple) have to do with elimination?
When coefficients are not already opposites, finding the LCM of the coefficients of a variable helps determine what multipliers to use. For example, to eliminate y with coefficients 3 and 5, the LCM is 15.

--- Lesson 1.5: Solving Systems by Elimination (Quiz) ---

  Q1. Solve by elimination: 2x + y = 7 and x - y = 2.
    [ ] x = 2, y = 3
    [ ] x = 4, y = -1
    [*] x = 3, y = 1
    [ ] x = 1, y = 5
    Explanation: Add the equations: 3x = 9, so x = 3. Substitute back: 2(3) + y = 7, so y = 1.

  Q2. Solve by elimination: 3x + 2y = 16 and 3x - 2y = 8.
    [ ] x = 2, y = 4
    [ ] x = 3, y = 3
    [*] x = 4, y = 2
    [ ] x = 5, y = 1
    Explanation: Add the equations: 6x = 24, so x = 4. Substitute: 3(4) + 2y = 16 → 2y = 4 → y = 2.

  Q3. To eliminate y from 4x + 3y = 10 and 2x + 3y = 4, what should you do?
    [ ] Divide both equations by 3
    [*] Subtract the second equation from the first
    [ ] Multiply the first equation by 3
    [ ] Add the two equations
    Explanation: Since the y-coefficients are both +3, subtracting eliminates y: (4x + 3y) - (2x + 3y) = 10 - 4 → 2x = 6 → x = 3.

  Q4. Solve: x + 2y = 10 and 3x - 2y = 6.
    [ ] x = 5, y = 2
    [*] x = 4, y = 3
    [ ] x = 2, y = 4
    [ ] x = 3, y = 4
    Explanation: Add the equations: 4x = 16, so x = 4. Substitute: 4 + 2y = 10 → 2y = 6 → y = 3.

  Q5. Solve: 2x + 5y = 21 and 2x + y = 9.
    [ ] x = 2, y = 5
    [*] x = 3, y = 3
    [ ] x = 1, y = 3
    [ ] x = 2, y = 3
    Explanation: Subtract the second from the first: 4y = 12, so y = 3. Substitute: 2x + 3 = 9 → 2x = 6 → x = 3.

  Q6. Solve: 5x + 3y = 19 and 2x - 3y = -5.
    [*] x = 2, y = 3
    [ ] x = 3, y = 2
    [ ] x = 4, y = 1
    [ ] x = 1, y = 4
    Explanation: Add the equations: 7x = 14, so x = 2. Substitute: 5(2) + 3y = 19 → 3y = 9 → y = 3.

  Q7. To eliminate x from x + 3y = 7 and 2x + y = 4, multiply the first equation by:
    [ ] 3
    [*] -2
    [ ] 2
    [ ] -3
    Explanation: Multiply the first equation by -2 to get -2x - 6y = -14. Adding to 2x + y = 4 eliminates x: -5y = -10, so y = 2.

  Q8. Solve: 4x - y = 11 and 2x + y = 7.
    [ ] x = 1, y = 5
    [ ] x = 2, y = 3
    [ ] x = 4, y = -1
    [*] x = 3, y = 1
    Explanation: Add the equations: 6x = 18, so x = 3. Substitute: 2(3) + y = 7 → y = 1.

  Q9. Solve: 3x + 4y = 25 and 3x + 2y = 17.
    [ ] x = 4, y = 3
    [ ] x = 1, y = 7
    [ ] x = 5, y = 1
    [*] x = 3, y = 4
    Explanation: Subtract the second from the first: 2y = 8, so y = 4. Substitute: 3x + 2(4) = 17 → 3x = 9 → x = 3.

  Q10. Solve: 2x + 3y = 1 and 4x - 3y = 11.
    [ ] x = 3, y = -1
    [ ] x = 1, y = -1
    [ ] x = -1, y = 1
    [*] x = 2, y = -1
    Explanation: Add the equations: 6x = 12, so x = 2. Substitute: 2(2) + 3y = 1 → 3y = -3 → y = -1.

  Q11. What is the elimination method for solving systems?
    [ ] A method where you graph both lines
    [ ] A method where you guess and check solutions
    [*] A method where you add or subtract equations to cancel one variable
    [ ] A method where you solve for one variable and plug it in
    Explanation: The elimination method (also called the addition method) involves adding or subtracting the equations so that one variable is eliminated, leaving a single equation in one unknown.

  Q12. What does 'eliminate a variable' mean?
    [*] Remove a variable by combining equations so its coefficients cancel to zero
    [ ] Set a variable equal to zero
    [ ] Replace a variable with a number
    [ ] Ignore a variable and solve without it
    Explanation: Eliminating a variable means combining equations so that one variable cancels out. For example, adding x + y = 5 and x - y = 3 eliminates y, giving 2x = 8.

  Q13. What are 'opposite coefficients'?
    [ ] Coefficients that are both negative
    [ ] Coefficients that add up to 1
    [*] Coefficients that are equal in absolute value but opposite in sign
    [ ] Coefficients that are reciprocals of each other
    Explanation: Opposite coefficients are numbers like 3 and -3 or -5 and 5. When equations have opposite coefficients on the same variable, adding the equations will eliminate that variable.

  Q14. What is a 'linear combination' of two equations?
    [ ] A factored form of a polynomial
    [ ] The product of two equations
    [ ] An equation solved for both variables at once
    [*] An equation formed by multiplying each equation by a constant and then adding them
    Explanation: A linear combination is formed by multiplying equations by constants and adding the results. This technique is the foundation of the elimination method for solving systems.

  Q15. What does 'coefficient' mean?
    [ ] The exponent on a variable
    [ ] The variable in an equation
    [ ] The constant term in an equation
    [*] The numerical factor multiplied by a variable in a term
    Explanation: A coefficient is the number that multiplies a variable. In the term 5x, the coefficient is 5. In -3y, the coefficient is -3.

  Q16. What is the 'addition property of equality'?
    [ ] The order of addition does not matter
    [ ] Adding zero to any number gives the same number
    [*] If a = b and c = d, then a + c = b + d
    [ ] Adding the same number to both sides changes the solution
    Explanation: The addition property of equality states that if two equations are true, their sides can be added. This principle justifies the elimination method — you can add entire equations together.

  Q17. What does 'LCM' (least common multiple) have to do with elimination?
    [ ] LCM is only used in fraction problems, not elimination
    [ ] The LCM is the solution to the system
    [*] The LCM of coefficients determines the multipliers needed to create opposite coefficients for elimination
    [ ] The LCM determines which variable to eliminate first
    Explanation: When coefficients are not already opposites, finding the LCM of the coefficients of a variable helps determine what multipliers to use. For example, to eliminate y with coefficients 3 and 5, the LCM is 15.

  Q18. What is a 'contradiction' when solving a system?
    [ ] Finding negative values for both variables
    [*] Getting a false statement like 0 = 5, meaning no solution exists
    [ ] Getting two different answers for the same variable
    [ ] Getting a true statement like 0 = 0
    Explanation: A contradiction (like 0 = 5) arises when the system has no solution — the lines are parallel. This means the system is inconsistent.

  Q19. What is an 'identity' when solving a system?
    [*] A result like 0 = 0, meaning infinitely many solutions
    [ ] An equation with exactly one variable
    [ ] A result like 0 = 5, meaning no solution
    [ ] A system that equals the identity matrix
    Explanation: When elimination produces a true identity like 0 = 0, both equations represent the same line, and every point on that line is a solution — giving infinitely many solutions.

  Q20. What does 'scaling an equation' mean in the context of elimination?
    [ ] Dividing the equation by zero
    [ ] Graphing the equation on a different scale
    [ ] Changing the variables in the equation
    [*] Multiplying every term in the equation by the same nonzero constant
    Explanation: Scaling an equation means multiplying both sides by the same nonzero constant. This creates equivalent equations with coefficients that are easier to eliminate. For example, multiplying x + y = 5 by 3 gives 3x + 3y = 15.

  Q21. A school cafeteria orders apples at $0.50 each and oranges at $0.75 each. They order 100 pieces of fruit for $62.50. How many apples were ordered?
    [ ] 40
    [*] 50
    [ ] 60
    [ ] 70
    Explanation: Let a = apples, o = oranges. a + o = 100 and 0.50a + 0.75o = 62.50. Multiply the first by -0.50: -0.50a - 0.50o = -50. Add: 0.25o = 12.50 → o = 50. So a = 50.

  Q22. A store sells two sizes of coffee: small for $3 and large for $5. On Monday, 80 coffees were sold for $320. How many large coffees were sold?
    [ ] 20
    [ ] 30
    [ ] 50
    [*] 40
    Explanation: Let s = small, L = large. s + L = 80 and 3s + 5L = 320. Multiply the first by -3: -3s - 3L = -240. Add: 2L = 80 → L = 40.

  Q23. Two friends invest a combined $8,000. One account earns 5% and the other earns 8%. Total annual interest is $490. How much is invested at 8%?
    [ ] $4,000
    [*] $3,000
    [ ] $2,000
    [ ] $5,000
    Explanation: Let x = amount at 5%, y = amount at 8%. x + y = 8000 and 0.05x + 0.08y = 490. Multiply the first by -0.05: -0.05x - 0.05y = -400. Add: 0.03y = 90 → y = $3,000.

  Q24. A plane flies 600 miles with the wind in 2 hours and 600 miles against the wind in 3 hours. What is the plane's speed in still air?
    [ ] 150 mph
    [ ] 300 mph
    [ ] 200 mph
    [*] 250 mph
    Explanation: With wind: p + w = 300. Against wind: p - w = 200. Add: 2p = 500 → p = 250 mph. The wind speed is 50 mph.

  Q25. A chemistry lab mixes a 30% solution with a 70% solution to get 40 liters of a 45% solution. How many liters of the 30% solution are needed?
    [ ] 20 liters
    [ ] 15 liters
    [*] 25 liters
    [ ] 30 liters
    Explanation: Let x = liters of 30%, y = liters of 70%. x + y = 40 and 0.30x + 0.70y = 18. Multiply the first by -0.30: -0.30x - 0.30y = -12. Add: 0.40y = 6 → y = 15. So x = 25.

  Q26. A farmer buys 6 bags of seed and 4 bags of fertilizer for $164. He later buys 3 bags of seed and 4 bags of fertilizer for $116. What is the cost of one bag of seed?
    [ ] $20
    [*] $16
    [ ] $14
    [ ] $12
    Explanation: Let s = seed cost, f = fertilizer cost. 6s + 4f = 164 and 3s + 4f = 116. Subtract: 3s = 48 → s = $16.

  Q27. A nutritionist mixes Brand A cereal (3g protein/serving) with Brand B (5g protein/serving) to create 12 servings with 44g total protein. How many servings of Brand A?
    [ ] 4
    [ ] 6
    [*] 8
    [ ] 10
    Explanation: Let a = Brand A, b = Brand B. a + b = 12 and 3a + 5b = 44. Multiply the first by -3: -3a - 3b = -36. Add: 2b = 8 → b = 4. So a = 8.

  Q28. Two phone plans: Plan A costs $30 + $0.05/minute, Plan B costs $20 + $0.10/minute. At what number of minutes do they cost the same?
    [ ] 100 minutes
    [ ] 300 minutes
    [ ] 150 minutes
    [*] 200 minutes
    Explanation: Set 30 + 0.05m = 20 + 0.10m. Subtract: 10 = 0.05m → m = 200 minutes. Both cost $40.

  Q29. A theater has 400 seats in two sections. Section A seats cost $25 and Section B seats cost $40. If a sold-out show generates $12,250, how many Section A seats are there?
    [ ] 150
    [ ] 200
    [ ] 300
    [*] 250
    Explanation: Let a = A seats, b = B seats. a + b = 400 and 25a + 40b = 12250. Multiply the first by -25: -25a - 25b = -10000. Add: 15b = 2250 → b = 150. So a = 250.

  Q30. A rower can row 12 km downstream in 1.5 hours and 12 km upstream in 3 hours. Using elimination, find the speed of the current.
    [*] 2 km/h
    [ ] 1 km/h
    [ ] 3 km/h
    [ ] 4 km/h
    Explanation: Downstream: r + c = 12/1.5 = 8. Upstream: r - c = 12/3 = 4. Subtract: 2c = 4 → c = 2 km/h.

--- Lesson 1.5: Solving Systems by Elimination (Flashcards) ---

  1. Q: Solve by elimination: x + y = 5 and x - y = 1
     A: x = 3, y = 2. Add equations: 2x = 6, so x = 3. Then y = 2.

  2. Q: Solve by elimination: 2x + y = 3 and x - y = 3
     A: x = 2, y = -1. Add: 3x = 6, x = 2. Then y = -1.

  3. Q: Multiply first equation by 2: 3x + 2y = 8 and 2x + y = 5
     A: 6x + 4y = 16 and 2x + y = 5. Then multiply second by -4 and add.

  4. Q: Elimination strategy when no coefficients match?
     A: Multiply equations to make coefficients of one variable opposites, then add.

  5. Q: Solve: 3x - 2y = 6 and 2x + y = 5
     A: x = 16/7, y = 3/7. Multiply second by 2: 2|(2x+y=5). Add to first.

  6. Q: Why use elimination instead of substitution?
     A: Faster when coefficients are nice integers. Avoids fractions longer.

  7. Q: Solve: x + 2y = 7 and 3x - 2y = 5
     A: x = 3, y = 2. Add equations: 4x = 12, x = 3. Then y = 2.

  8. Q: Check solution x=1, y=2 in 2x+3y=8
     A: 2(1) + 3(2) = 8. âœ“

  9. Q: Solve: 4x - y = 10 and 2x + y = 2
     A: x = 2, y = -2. Add: 6x = 12, x = 2. Then y = -2.

  10. Q: When does elimination give infinite solutions?
     A: When equations are identical (dependent). Get 0 = 0 instead.

--- Lesson 1.6: Applications of Linear Systems (Summary) ---

  Key Concepts: Applications of Linear Systems
Overview
This lesson covers the fundamental measures of center used to analyze and summarize data sets. You'll learn how to calculate and apply the mean, median, and mode, and understand when each is most appropriate.
Key Definitions
A boat goes 30 km downstream in 2 hours and 30 km upstream in 3 hours. What is the speed of the boat in still water?
Downstream: b + c = 15, upstream: b - c = 10. Add: 2b = 25 → b = 12.5 km/h.
Two numbers have a sum of 20 and a difference of 6. What is the larger number?
x + y = 20 and x - y = 6. Add: 2x = 26 → x = 13. The larger number is 13 and the smaller is 7.
A rectangle has perimeter 30 cm. Its length is 3 cm more than its width. What is the length?
2L + 2W = 30 and L = W + 3. Substitute: 2(W + 3) + 2W = 30 → 4W + 6 = 30 → W = 6, L = 9 cm.
The sum of two numbers is 45 and one is three times the other. What is the smaller number?
x + y = 45 and y = 3x. Substitute: x + 3x = 45 → 4x = 45 → x = 11.25.
What is a 'mixture problem' in algebra?
A mixture problem involves combining two or more substances with different prices, concentrations, or rates to create a mixture with a desired property. These are naturally modeled by systems of equations.
What is a 'distance-rate-time' problem?
Distance-rate-time problems use the formula distance = rate x time (d = rt). Common scenarios involve upstream/downstream travel, where wind or current affects the effective speed.
What is 'simple interest'?
Simple interest is calculated using I = Prt (Interest = Principal x rate x time). Unlike compound interest, it is calculated only on the original principal amount.
What is a 'system of equations word problem'?
A system of equations word problem presents a real-world scenario with two or more unknown quantities related by two or more conditions. You translate the words into equations and solve the system.
What is a 'constraint' in a word problem?
A constraint is a condition that limits the values of variables. In systems of equations, each equation represents a constraint. For example, 'total items = 50' is a constraint.

--- Lesson 1.6: Applications of Linear Systems (Quiz) ---

  Q1. A store sells T-shirts for $12 and hats for $8. If 15 items were sold for $148, how many T-shirts were sold?
    [ ] 6
    [ ] 8
    [*] 7
    [ ] 9
    Explanation: Let t = T-shirts, h = hats. t + h = 15 and 12t + 8h = 148. Substitute h = 15 - t: 12t + 8(15 - t) = 148 → 4t + 120 = 148 → 4t = 28 → t = 7.

  Q2. A boat goes 30 km downstream in 2 hours and 30 km upstream in 3 hours. What is the speed of the boat in still water?
    [ ] 8 km/h
    [ ] 10 km/h
    [ ] 15 km/h
    [*] 12.5 km/h
    Explanation: Downstream: b + c = 15, upstream: b - c = 10. Add: 2b = 25 → b = 12.5 km/h.

  Q3. Two numbers have a sum of 20 and a difference of 6. What is the larger number?
    [ ] 14
    [ ] 12
    [*] 13
    [ ] 10
    Explanation: x + y = 20 and x - y = 6. Add: 2x = 26 → x = 13. The larger number is 13 and the smaller is 7.

  Q4. An investor puts $10,000 in two accounts earning 3% and 7%. If total interest is $460, how much is at 7%?
    [ ] $6,000
    [*] $4,000
    [ ] $5,000
    [ ] $3,000
    Explanation: x + y = 10000 and 0.03x + 0.07y = 460. Substitute x = 10000 - y: 300 - 0.03y + 0.07y = 460 → 0.04y = 160 → y = $4,000.

  Q5. A coffee blend mixes $6/lb beans with $10/lb beans. To make 20 lbs costing $7/lb, how many pounds of $6/lb beans are needed?
    [ ] 10
    [ ] 8
    [ ] 12
    [*] 15
    Explanation: x + y = 20 and 6x + 10y = 140. Substitute y = 20 - x: 6x + 200 - 10x = 140 → -4x = -60 → x = 15 lbs.

  Q6. A taxi charges $2.50 base plus $1.50/mile. A rideshare charges $5.00 base plus $1.00/mile. At how many miles do they cost the same?
    [ ] 3 miles
    [*] 5 miles
    [ ] 4 miles
    [ ] 6 miles
    Explanation: Set 2.50 + 1.50m = 5.00 + 1.00m: 0.50m = 2.50 → m = 5 miles. Both cost $10.

  Q7. A rectangle has perimeter 30 cm. Its length is 3 cm more than its width. What is the length?
    [ ] 8 cm
    [*] 9 cm
    [ ] 12 cm
    [ ] 10 cm
    Explanation: 2L + 2W = 30 and L = W + 3. Substitute: 2(W + 3) + 2W = 30 → 4W + 6 = 30 → W = 6, L = 9 cm.

  Q8. A class has 30 students. There are 4 more girls than boys. How many boys are in the class?
    [ ] 12
    [ ] 14
    [ ] 15
    [*] 13
    Explanation: b + g = 30 and g = b + 4. Substitute: b + (b + 4) = 30 → 2b = 26 → b = 13.

  Q9. A coin jar has nickels and dimes worth $3.50 total. There are 50 coins. How many dimes are there?
    [ ] 15
    [ ] 25
    [*] 20
    [ ] 30
    Explanation: n + d = 50 and 5n + 10d = 350. Substitute n = 50 - d: 250 - 5d + 10d = 350 → 5d = 100 → d = 20.

  Q10. The sum of two numbers is 45 and one is three times the other. What is the smaller number?
    [ ] 15
    [ ] 12
    [*] 11.25
    [ ] 9, 
    Explanation: x + y = 45 and y = 3x. Substitute: x + 3x = 45 → 4x = 45 → x = 11.25.

  Q11. What is a 'mixture problem' in algebra?
    [*] A problem where two substances of different concentrations or prices are combined
    [ ] A problem about mixing paint colors
    [ ] A problem that can only be solved by graphing
    [ ] A problem involving addition of fractions
    Explanation: A mixture problem involves combining two or more substances with different prices, concentrations, or rates to create a mixture with a desired property. These are naturally modeled by systems of equations.

  Q12. What is a 'distance-rate-time' problem?
    [ ] A problem about finding the area of a rectangle
    [*] A problem using the relationship d = rt to find distance, rate, or time
    [ ] A problem about compound interest
    [ ] A problem about measuring angles
    Explanation: Distance-rate-time problems use the formula distance = rate x time (d = rt). Common scenarios involve upstream/downstream travel, where wind or current affects the effective speed.

  Q13. What does 'break-even point' mean?
    [*] The point where total cost equals total revenue (no profit and no loss)
    [ ] The point where a product breaks
    [ ] The point where demand equals zero
    [ ] The maximum profit point
    Explanation: The break-even point is where revenue equals cost, meaning profit is zero. Selling more units than the break-even quantity produces profit; selling fewer produces a loss.

  Q14. What is 'simple interest'?
    [ ] The interest rate divided by 12
    [ ] Interest that compounds monthly
    [*] Interest calculated only on the original principal, using I = Prt
    [ ] A fixed fee charged per transaction
    Explanation: Simple interest is calculated using I = Prt (Interest = Principal x rate x time). Unlike compound interest, it is calculated only on the original principal amount.

  Q15. What does 'upstream' and 'downstream' mean in rate problems?
    [ ] Upstream means the river flows faster
    [ ] Both mean the same speed
    [ ] Upstream means going uphill; downstream means going downhill
    [*] Upstream means against the current (slower); downstream means with the current (faster)
    Explanation: Downstream means moving with the current, so the effective speed is boat speed + current speed. Upstream means against the current, so the effective speed is boat speed - current speed.

  Q16. What is a 'system of equations word problem'?
    [ ] A problem that cannot be solved algebraically
    [ ] A graphing exercise
    [ ] A problem with only words and no numbers
    [*] A real-world scenario that requires setting up and solving two or more equations
