    Explanation: A system of equations word problem presents a real-world scenario with two or more unknown quantities related by two or more conditions. You translate the words into equations and solve the system.

  Q17. What does 'revenue' mean in a business context?
    [ ] The profit after expenses
    [ ] The cost of production
    [*] The total income from selling goods or services
    [ ] The interest earned on investments
    Explanation: Revenue is the total amount of money received from sales, calculated as price per unit times the number of units sold. Profit = Revenue - Cost.

  Q18. What is a 'constraint' in a word problem?
    [ ] The solution to the problem
    [*] A condition or limitation that restricts the possible values of the variables
    [ ] A formula provided in the problem
    [ ] A variable that must be positive
    Explanation: A constraint is a condition that limits the values of variables. In systems of equations, each equation represents a constraint. For example, 'total items = 50' is a constraint.

  Q19. What does 'define variables' mean in solving word problems?
    [ ] Assigning random values to test the solution
    [*] Choosing letters to represent unknown quantities and clearly stating what they stand for
    [ ] Setting all unknowns equal to zero
    [ ] Looking up the definition of mathematical terms
    Explanation: Defining variables is the first step in solving word problems. You assign letters (like x and y) to the unknown quantities and write a clear statement of what each variable represents.

  Q20. What does 'concentration' mean in mixture problems?
    [*] The percentage or proportion of a substance in a mixture
    [ ] The total volume of the mixture
    [ ] The number of different substances mixed
    [ ] How carefully you mix the substances
    Explanation: Concentration is the ratio of a specific substance to the total mixture, usually expressed as a percentage. For example, a 30% acid solution has 30 parts acid per 100 parts solution.

  Q21. A school fundraiser sells candy bars for $2 and popcorn bags for $3. They sold 150 items and made $370. How many candy bars were sold?
    [ ] 70
    [*] 80
    [ ] 60
    [ ] 90
    Explanation: c + p = 150 and 2c + 3p = 370. Substitute p = 150 - c: 2c + 450 - 3c = 370 → -c = -80 → c = 80.

  Q22. A nurse mixes a 10% saline solution with a 40% saline solution to create 600 mL of a 20% solution. How many mL of the 10% solution are needed?
    [ ] 500 mL
    [ ] 300 mL
    [*] 400 mL
    [ ] 200 mL
    Explanation: x + y = 600 and 0.10x + 0.40y = 120. Substitute y = 600 - x: 0.10x + 240 - 0.40x = 120 → -0.30x = -120 → x = 400 mL.

  Q23. A company produces widgets at $5 per unit with $200 fixed costs. They sell widgets for $8 each. How many widgets must be sold to break even?
    [ ] 50
    [ ] 100
    [*] 67
    [ ] 40
    Explanation: Cost = 5n + 200, Revenue = 8n. Break even: 8n = 5n + 200 → 3n = 200 → n = 66.7, so 67 widgets (round up since you cannot sell partial widgets).

  Q24. A family drives to the beach at 60 mph and returns at 40 mph. The total trip takes 5 hours. How far is the beach?
    [ ] 200 miles
    [*] 120 miles
    [ ] 150 miles
    [ ] 100 miles
    Explanation: Let d = distance. Time there: d/60, time back: d/40. d/60 + d/40 = 5. LCD = 120: 2d + 3d = 600 → 5d = 600 → d = 120 miles.

  Q25. A theater charges $12 for adults and $7 for seniors. If 300 people attend and total revenue is $2,850, how many seniors attended?
    [*] 150
    [ ] 170
    [ ] 120
    [ ] 130
    Explanation: a + s = 300 and 12a + 7s = 2850. Substitute a = 300 - s: 3600 - 12s + 7s = 2850 → -5s = -750 → s = 150.

  Q26. Two trains leave the same station traveling in opposite directions. One goes 50 mph and the other 70 mph. After how many hours are they 360 miles apart?
    [*] 3 hours
    [ ] 5 hours
    [ ] 4 hours
    [ ] 2 hours
    Explanation: Combined speed = 50 + 70 = 120 mph. Distance = rate x time: 360 = 120t → t = 3 hours.

  Q27. A caterer charges $15/person for meal A and $20/person for meal B. If 60 guests attend and total food cost is $1,050, how many chose meal A?
    [*] 30
    [ ] 40
    [ ] 25
    [ ] 35
    Explanation: a + b = 60 and 15a + 20b = 1050. Substitute b = 60 - a: 15a + 1200 - 20a = 1050 → -5a = -150 → a = 30.

  Q28. A hardware store mixes paint at $25/gallon with paint at $35/gallon to make 10 gallons of paint worth $28/gallon. How many gallons of the cheaper paint are needed?
    [ ] 5 gallons
    [*] 7 gallons
    [ ] 8 gallons
    [ ] 6 gallons
    Explanation: x + y = 10 and 25x + 35y = 280. Substitute y = 10 - x: 25x + 350 - 35x = 280 → -10x = -70 → x = 7 gallons.

  Q29. A worker earns $18/hour on weekdays and $27/hour on weekends. In a week she works 40 hours and earns $810. How many weekend hours did she work?
    [ ] 12 hours
    [*] 10 hours
    [ ] 8 hours
    [ ] 15 hours
    Explanation: w + e = 40 and 18w + 27e = 810. Substitute w = 40 - e: 720 - 18e + 27e = 810 → 9e = 90 → e = 10 hours.

  Q30. A pharmacist mixes a 5% medication with a 15% medication to make 200 mL of a 9% solution. How much of the 15% solution is needed?
    [ ] 60 mL
    [ ] 120 mL
    [ ] 100 mL
    [*] 80 mL
    Explanation: x + y = 200 and 0.05x + 0.15y = 18. Substitute x = 200 - y: 10 - 0.05y + 0.15y = 18 → 0.10y = 8 → y = 80 mL.

--- Lesson 1.6: Applications of Linear Systems (Flashcards) ---

  1. Q: Mixture: 20% salt + pure water to get 100L of 5% solution. How much pure water?
     A: 500L of water (x=100, y=500 means total 600L, hmm check calculation)... actually setup: 0.20x = 0.05(x+y).

  2. Q: Investment: $8000 total, part at 5%, rest at 8%, total interest $550. Setup equations?
     A: x + y = 8000 and 0.05x + 0.08y = 550.

  3. Q: Coin problem: 30 coins, quarters and dimes, total $6.30. How many quarters?
     A: 18 quarters. Equations: x + y = 30 and 0.25x + 0.10y = 6.30.

  4. Q: Distance: train A at 60 mph, train B at 80 mph, start same time opposite. When 280 miles apart?
     A: 2 hours. Distance = 60t + 80t = 280, so 140t = 280, t = 2.

  5. Q: Boat problem: boat speed 20 mph, current 5 mph, downstream distance 100 miles. Time?
     A: 5 hours. Time = 100/(20+5) = 100/25 = 4... wait downstream should be 4 hours.

  6. Q: Age problem: person A is 3 times as old as B. In 10 years, A is 2 times B's age. Find current ages.
     A: A = 30, B = 10. Equations: x = 3y and x + 10 = 2(y + 10).

  7. Q: Work problem: one worker completes job in 5 hours, another in 3 hours. Together?
     A: 15/8 = 1.875 hours. Rates: 1/5 + 1/3 = 8/15 per hour.

  8. Q: Rectangle perimeter 40, length 2 more than width. Dimensions?
     A: Length 11, width 9. Equations: 2x + 2y = 40 and x = y + 2.

  9. Q: Production: machine A makes 100/hr, B makes 80/hr. After 4.5 hours, 810 units made by A. Time for A?
     A: 4.5 hours for 450 units... problem says 810 units: 810/100 = 8.1 hours of A time.

  10. Q: Mixture word problem key: identify rates/percentages/speeds per unit quantity.
     A: Set up equations with total quantities and per-unit rates separately.

--- Lesson 1.7: Inequalities & System of Inequalities (Summary) ---

  Key Concepts: Inequalities & System of Inequalities
Overview
This lesson covers the fundamental measures of center used to analyze and summarize data sets. You'll learn how to calculate and apply the mean, median, and mode, and understand when each is most appropriate.
Key Definitions
What is a linear inequality?
A linear inequality uses <, >, ≤, or ≥ instead of = in a first-degree expression. Its graph on a number line is a ray or segment, and in two variables it defines a half-plane.
What is a 'system of inequalities'?
A system of inequalities is a set of two or more inequalities with the same variables. The solution is the set of all points that satisfy every inequality simultaneously.
What is a 'half-plane'?
A half-plane is one of the two regions on either side of a line in a coordinate plane. A linear inequality in two variables has its solutions in one half-plane.
What is a 'compound inequality'?
A compound inequality combines two inequalities. An 'and' compound requires both to be true simultaneously. An 'or' compound requires at least one to be true.
What is a 'test point' used for when graphing inequalities?
A test point is substituted into the inequality. If it makes the inequality true, shade the side containing that point; otherwise, shade the opposite side.
A bakery needs at least 50 pastries. Croissants take 10 min each and muffins take 5 min. The baker has 360 minutes. What is the max number of croissants?
c + m ≥ 50 and 10c + 5m ≤ 360. Substitute m = 50 - c (minimum): 10c + 5(50 - c) ≤ 360 → 5c + 250 ≤ 360 → 5c ≤ 110 → c ≤ 22.
A venue holds 500 max. VIP tickets cost $50, general $20. At least $12,000 must be raised. If 100 VIP tickets are sold, what is the minimum number of general tickets?
50(100) + 20g ≥ 12000 → 5000 + 20g ≥ 12000 → 20g ≥ 7000 → g ≥ 350.
A parking lot holds at most 60 spaces. Cars take 1 space, buses 3 spaces. With at least 5 buses, what is the max number of cars?
Minimum 5 buses use 15 spaces: c + 15 ≤ 60 → c ≤ 45 cars maximum.
A caterer must provide at least 200 servings using Dish A ($4/serving) and Dish B ($6/serving) with a $1,000 budget. If she makes 100 of Dish A, what is the max of Dish B?
Budget: 4(100) + 6b ≤ 1000 → 400 + 6b ≤ 1000 → 6b ≤ 600 → b ≤ 100. With 100 + 100 = 200, the minimum serving requirement is met.
Real-World Applications
Example: What happens to the inequality sign when you multiply or divide by a negative number?
When multiplying or dividing both sides by a negative number, the direction of the inequality must be reversed. For example, -x > 3 becomes x < -3.
Example: A student needs at least 80 points total on two tests. She scored 45 on the first test. What must she score on the second test?
45 + x ≥ 80 → x ≥ 35. She needs at least 35 points on the second test.

--- Lesson 1.7: Inequalities & System of Inequalities (Quiz) ---

  Q1. Solve: 3x + 5 > 14.
    [ ] x > 5
    [ ] x > 9
    [*] x > 3
    [ ] x < 3
    Explanation: Subtract 5: 3x > 9. Divide by 3: x > 3.

  Q2. Solve: -2x ≤ 8.
    [ ] x ≤ 4
    [ ] x ≤ -4
    [ ] x ≥ 4
    [*] x ≥ -4
    Explanation: Divide both sides by -2 and flip the inequality sign: x ≥ -4. Dividing or multiplying by a negative reverses the inequality direction.

  Q3. Which point is in the solution region of y > 2x + 1?
    [*] (1, 5)
    [ ] (2, 4)
    [ ] (0, 0)
    [ ] (1, 3)
    Explanation: Test (1, 5): 5 > 2(1) + 1 = 3. Since 5 > 3 is true, (1, 5) is in the solution region.

  Q4. Solve the compound inequality: -3 < 2x + 1 ≤ 7.
    [ ] -2 ≤ x < 3
    [*] -2 < x ≤ 3
    [ ] -3 < x ≤ 7
    [ ] -1 < x ≤ 4
    Explanation: Subtract 1 from all parts: -4 < 2x ≤ 6. Divide by 2: -2 < x ≤ 3.

  Q5. Which inequality has a dashed boundary line when graphed?
    [ ] y ≤ 3x
    [ ] y ≥ 0
    [ ] y ≥ x + 2
    [*] y > -x + 4
    Explanation: Strict inequalities (< or >) use dashed boundary lines to show that points on the line are NOT included.

  Q6. Solve: 4 - x ≥ 7.
    [ ] x ≥ 3
    [*] x ≤ -3
    [ ] x ≥ -3
    [ ] x ≤ 3
    Explanation: Subtract 4: -x ≥ 3. Multiply by -1 and flip the sign: x ≤ -3.

  Q7. Which point satisfies both y ≤ x + 3 and y ≥ -x + 1?
    [ ] (0, 5)
    [*] (2, 1)
    [ ] (0, -2)
    [ ] (-3, 0)
    Explanation: Test (2, 1): 1 ≤ 2 + 3 = 5 (true) and 1 ≥ -2 + 1 = -1 (true). Both inequalities are satisfied.

  Q8. Solve: 5x - 3 < 2x + 9.
    [ ] x > 4
    [ ] x < 6
    [ ] x < 2
    [*] x < 4
    Explanation: Subtract 2x: 3x - 3 < 9. Add 3: 3x < 12. Divide by 3: x < 4.

  Q9. The solution of x + y ≤ 4 and x ≥ 0 is the region:
    [ ] The entire first quadrant
    [ ] Left of the y-axis
    [*] Below the line x + y = 4 and to the right of the y-axis
    [ ] Above the line x + y = 4 only
    Explanation: x + y ≤ 4 means below (or on) the line, and x ≥ 0 means to the right of (or on) the y-axis. The overlapping region is the solution.

  Q10. Solve: |x - 3| ≤ 5.
    [ ] x ≤ 8
    [ ] -5 ≤ x ≤ 3
    [ ] x ≤ -2 or x ≥ 8
    [*] -2 ≤ x ≤ 8
    Explanation: The absolute value inequality |x - 3| ≤ 5 means -5 ≤ x - 3 ≤ 5. Add 3: -2 ≤ x ≤ 8.

  Q11. What is a linear inequality?
    [*] An inequality involving a first-degree expression, such as 2x + 3 > 7
    [ ] An equation with an equals sign
    [ ] An inequality with squared terms
    [ ] Any statement using the not-equal symbol
    Explanation: A linear inequality uses <, >, ≤, or ≥ instead of = in a first-degree expression. Its graph on a number line is a ray or segment, and in two variables it defines a half-plane.

  Q12. What is a 'system of inequalities'?
    [*] Two or more inequalities considered together, with a solution satisfying all of them
    [ ] A single inequality with two variables
    [ ] Two equal equations
    [ ] An equation and an inequality combined
    Explanation: A system of inequalities is a set of two or more inequalities with the same variables. The solution is the set of all points that satisfy every inequality simultaneously.

  Q13. What does the 'boundary line' represent in a graphed inequality?
    [*] The line formed by replacing the inequality symbol with an equals sign
    [ ] The x-axis
    [ ] The solution to the inequality
    [ ] The diagonal of the coordinate plane
    Explanation: The boundary line is the graph of the related equation. It divides the plane into two half-planes. For ≤ or ≥ it is solid; for < or > it is dashed.

  Q14. What is a 'half-plane'?
    [ ] A plane cut in half by a point
    [*] One of the two regions created when a line divides the coordinate plane
    [ ] Half of the x-axis
    [ ] The region above the x-axis
    Explanation: A half-plane is one of the two regions on either side of a line in a coordinate plane. A linear inequality in two variables has its solutions in one half-plane.

  Q15. What is a 'compound inequality'?
    [*] Two inequalities joined by 'and' or 'or'
    [ ] An inequality involving multiplication
    [ ] An inequality with two variables
    [ ] An inequality with absolute value
    Explanation: A compound inequality combines two inequalities. An 'and' compound requires both to be true simultaneously. An 'or' compound requires at least one to be true.

  Q16. What does 'feasible region' mean?
    [ ] The boundary lines only
    [ ] The entire coordinate plane
    [ ] Any region bounded by a rectangle
    [*] The set of all points satisfying all constraints in a system of inequalities
    Explanation: The feasible region is the overlapping area where all inequalities in a system are satisfied simultaneously. Every point in this region is a valid solution.

  Q17. What happens to the inequality sign when you multiply or divide by a negative number?
    [ ] Nothing changes
    [ ] The solution becomes empty
    [ ] The inequality becomes an equation
    [*] The inequality sign reverses direction
    Explanation: When multiplying or dividing both sides by a negative number, the direction of the inequality must be reversed. For example, -x > 3 becomes x < -3.

  Q18. What does '≤' mean compared to '<'?
    [ ] < includes the boundary and ≤ does not when applying fundamental principles
    [ ] They mean the same thing, particularly regarding mean within the typical range of values
    [*] ≤ means 'less than or equal to' (includes boundary); < means 'strictly less than' (excludes boundary)
    [ ] ≤ means 'much less than', particularly regarding symbol in accordance with classical theory
    Explanation: The symbol ≤ means 'less than or equal to,' so the boundary value is included. The symbol < means 'strictly less than,' excluding the boundary.

  Q19. What is a 'test point' used for when graphing inequalities?
    [*] To determine which side of the boundary line to shade
    [ ] To find the y-intercept
    [ ] To find the equation of the boundary line
    [ ] To calculate the slope
    Explanation: A test point is substituted into the inequality. If it makes the inequality true, shade the side containing that point; otherwise, shade the opposite side.

  Q20. What does 'solution set' mean for an inequality?
    [ ] A single value that solves the inequality
    [ ] The boundary line of the inequality
    [ ] The set of integers only
    [*] The set of all values that make the inequality true
    Explanation: The solution set of an inequality is the collection of all values or ordered pairs that make the inequality true. Unlike equations, inequalities typically have infinitely many solutions.

  Q21. A student needs at least 80 points total on two tests. She scored 45 on the first test. What must she score on the second test?
    [ ] Exactly 35
    [ ] At least 40
    [ ] At most 35
    [*] At least 35
    Explanation: 45 + x ≥ 80 → x ≥ 35. She needs at least 35 points on the second test.

  Q22. A delivery truck can carry at most 2,000 pounds. Each large box weighs 50 lbs and each small box weighs 20 lbs. If 10 large boxes are loaded, how many small boxes can be added?
    [ ] At most 100
    [*] At most 75
    [ ] At most 60
    [ ] At most 50
    Explanation: 50(10) + 20s ≤ 2000 → 500 + 20s ≤ 2000 → 20s ≤ 1500 → s ≤ 75.

  Q23. A student works two jobs: tutoring at $15/hr and retail at $10/hr. She wants to earn at least $300/week but work no more than 25 hours. Which system models this?
    [*] 15t + 10r ≥ 300 and t + r ≤ 25
    [ ] 15t + 10r = 300 and t + r = 25
    [ ] t + r ≥ 300 and 15t + 10r ≤ 25
    [ ] 15t + 10r ≤ 300 and t + r ≥ 25
    Explanation: She wants at least $300 (≥) and at most 25 hours (≤). The system is 15t + 10r ≥ 300 and t + r ≤ 25.

  Q24. A farmer has 100 acres and wants to plant corn and wheat. Corn costs $200/acre and wheat $150/acre, with a budget of $17,000. What system represents this?
    [ ] 200c + 150w ≤ 100 and c + w ≤ 17000
    [*] c + w ≤ 100 and 200c + 150w ≤ 17000
    [ ] c + w = 100 and 200c + 150w = 17000
    [ ] c + w ≥ 100 and 200c + 150w ≥ 17000
    Explanation: The farmer cannot exceed 100 acres (c + w ≤ 100) or the $17,000 budget (200c + 150w ≤ 17000).

  Q25. A bakery needs at least 50 pastries. Croissants take 10 min each and muffins take 5 min. The baker has 360 minutes. What is the max number of croissants?
    [ ] 36
    [ ] 50
    [ ] 31
    [*] 22
    Explanation: c + m ≥ 50 and 10c + 5m ≤ 360. Substitute m = 50 - c (minimum): 10c + 5(50 - c) ≤ 360 → 5c + 250 ≤ 360 → 5c ≤ 110 → c ≤ 22.

  Q26. A venue holds 500 max. VIP tickets cost $50, general $20. At least $12,000 must be raised. If 100 VIP tickets are sold, what is the minimum number of general tickets?
    [ ] 300
    [ ] 400
    [ ] 250
    [*] 350
    Explanation: 50(100) + 20g ≥ 12000 → 5000 + 20g ≥ 12000 → 20g ≥ 7000 → g ≥ 350.

  Q27. A diet requires at least 60g protein and at most 2,000 calories. Food A has 10g protein/300 cal per serving, Food B has 20g protein/500 cal. What system models this?
    [*] 10a + 20b ≥ 60 and 300a + 500b ≤ 2000
    [ ] 10a + 20b ≤ 60 and 300a + 500b ≥ 2000
    [ ] 30a + 520b ≤ 2060
    [ ] a + b ≥ 60 and a + b ≤ 2000
    Explanation: At least 60g protein: 10a + 20b ≥ 60. At most 2000 calories: 300a + 500b ≤ 2000.

  Q28. A manufacturer makes tables ($50 profit) and chairs ($30 profit). Tables need 4 hours labor, chairs 2 hours. With 40 hours available, can they make 8 tables and 6 chairs?
    [ ] No, that requires 50 hours
    [*] No, that requires 44 hours which exceeds the 40-hour limit
    [ ] Yes, that uses only 36 hours
    [ ] Yes, that uses exactly 40 hours
    Explanation: 4(8) + 2(6) = 32 + 12 = 44 hours, which exceeds the 40-hour limit. This combination is not feasible.

  Q29. A parking lot holds at most 60 spaces. Cars take 1 space, buses 3 spaces. With at least 5 buses, what is the max number of cars?
    [*] 45
    [ ] 40
    [ ] 50
    [ ] 55
    Explanation: Minimum 5 buses use 15 spaces: c + 15 ≤ 60 → c ≤ 45 cars maximum.

  Q30. A caterer must provide at least 200 servings using Dish A ($4/serving) and Dish B ($6/serving) with a $1,000 budget. If she makes 100 of Dish A, what is the max of Dish B?
    [ ] 150
    [ ] 80
    [ ] 120
    [*] 100
    Explanation: Budget: 4(100) + 6b ≤ 1000 → 400 + 6b ≤ 1000 → 6b ≤ 600 → b ≤ 100. With 100 + 100 = 200, the minimum serving requirement is met.

--- Lesson 1.7: Inequalities & System of Inequalities (Flashcards) ---

  1. Q: Graph x + y ≥ 4. Which region?
     A: Above line x + y = 4 (including line). Test (0,5): 0+5≥4 ✓.

  2. Q: Solve -2x > 4
     A: x < -2. Divide by negative: flip inequality. Number line: open circle at -2, left.

  3. Q: Solve 3 < x + 2 < 7
     A: 1 < x < 5. Subtract 2 all parts: compound inequality.

  4. Q: Boundary line for 2x - y < 5 solid or dashed?
     A: Dashed. Use < (not ≤), indicating point on line not included.

  5. Q: Interval notation for x ≤ 3:
     A: (-∞, 3]. Bracket at 3 (included), infinity always parenthesis.

  6. Q: Solve and graph |x| < 3
     A: -3 < x < 3. Absolute value: distance less than 3 from origin.

  7. Q: Is (0,0) in region 3x + 2y ≥ 6?
     A: No. 3(0) + 2(0) = 0, and 0 ≱ 6.

  8. Q: What does compound inequality 1 ≤ x ≤ 5 represent?
     A: All x from 1 to 5 inclusive. Both endpoints included.

  9. Q: Find intersection of x > 2 and x < 5
     A: 2 < x < 5. Both conditions must be true simultaneously.

  10. Q: Solution to 2|x - 1| = 6?
     A: x = 4 or x = -2. |x - 1| = 3 means x - 1 = ±3.

--- Lesson 1.8: Linear Programming (Summary) ---

  Key Concepts: Linear Programming
Overview
This lesson covers the fundamental measures of center used to analyze and summarize data sets. You'll learn how to calculate and apply the mean, median, and mode, and understand when each is most appropriate.
Key Definitions
In a linear programming problem, the objective function P = 3x + 5y is evaluated at corner point (2, 4). What is P?
Substitute x = 2, y = 4: P = 3(2) + 5(4) = 6 + 20 = 26.
Maximize P = 2x + y subject to x ≥ 0, y ≥ 0, x + y ≤ 5. What is the maximum value?
Corner points: (0,0)→0, (5,0)→10, (0,5)→5. Maximum P = 10 at (5, 0).
Maximize P = x + 3y with constraints x ≥ 0, y ≥ 0, x + 2y ≤ 8, x + y ≤ 5. What is the max?
Corner points: (0,0)→0, (5,0)→5, (2,3)→11, (0,4)→12. Max P = 12 at (0, 4).
Given constraints x ≥ 0, y ≥ 0, and 3x + 2y ≤ 12, what is the corner point where the constraint line meets the x-axis?
Set y = 0 in 3x + 2y = 12: 3x = 12, x = 4. The constraint line meets the x-axis at (4, 0).
What is linear programming?
Linear programming is a mathematical technique for finding the maximum or minimum value of a linear function (the objective) subject to a set of linear inequality constraints.
What is an 'objective function' in linear programming?
The objective function is the expression (like P = 3x + 5y) that you want to optimize. It represents the quantity you are trying to maximize (profit) or minimize (cost).
What is the 'feasible region' in linear programming?
The feasible region is the geometric shape formed by the intersection of all constraint half-planes. Only points within this region are potential solutions.
What is a 'vertex' (corner point) of the feasible region?
A vertex is a corner of the feasible region where two or more constraint boundaries meet. The Corner Point Theorem guarantees the optimal solution occurs at one of these vertices.
A school wants to buy desks ($100 each, need at least 20) and chairs ($40 each, need at least 30), with a total budget of $4,000. What is the maximum number of desks they can buy?
100d + 40c ≤ 4000, d ≥ 20, c ≥ 30. With minimum chairs c = 30: 100d + 1200 ≤ 4000 → 100d ≤ 2800 → d ≤ 28.
Real-World Applications
Example: A shipping company has two routes. Route A costs $5/package with capacity of 200 packages. Route B costs $3/package with capacity of 300 packages. At least 400 packages must be shipped. What minimizes cost?
Minimize C = 5a + 3b. Constraints: a ≤ 200, b ≤ 300, a + b ≥ 400, a,b ≥ 0. At (100,300): C = 500+900 = 1400. At (200,200): C = 1000+600 = 1600. Min cost is $1,400 with 100 on A and 300 on B.
Example: A store orders jackets ($40 profit) and sweaters ($25 profit). Storage holds at most 100 items. Budget allows at most $6,000 in wholesale cost ($50/jacket, $30/sweater). How many jackets maximizes profit?
j + s ≤ 100 and 50j + 30s ≤ 6000. At (100,0): cost = 5000 ≤ 6000, P = 40(100) = $4,000. At (0,100): P = $2,500. Max profit is $4,000 with 100 jackets.
Example: A delivery company uses small trucks (capacity 50 packages, $100/trip) and large trucks (capacity 120 packages, $200/trip). They must deliver at least 600 packages. Small trucks can make at most 8 trips. What minimizes cost?
Minimize C = 100s + 200L. Constraint: 50s + 120L ≥ 600, s ≤ 8, s,L ≥ 0. At (0,5): 120(5)=600≥600, C = 1000. At (8,2): 400+240=640≥600, C = 800+400=1200. Minimum cost is $1,000 with 0 small and 5 large trips.

--- Lesson 1.8: Linear Programming (Quiz) ---

  Q1. In a linear programming problem, the objective function P = 3x + 5y is evaluated at corner point (2, 4). What is P?
    [*] 26
    [ ] 18
    [ ] 23
    [ ] 30
    Explanation: Substitute x = 2, y = 4: P = 3(2) + 5(4) = 6 + 20 = 26.

  Q2. Which of the following is a corner point of the feasible region bounded by x ≥ 0, y ≥ 0, and x + y ≤ 6?
    [*] (6, 0)
    [ ] (3, 4)
    [ ] (7, 0)
    [ ] (-1, 7)
    Explanation: The corner points are (0,0), (6,0), and (0,6). (6,0) is where x + y = 6 meets y = 0.

  Q3. Maximize P = 2x + y subject to x ≥ 0, y ≥ 0, x + y ≤ 5. What is the maximum value?
    [*] 10
    [ ] 5
    [ ] 7
    [ ] 8
    Explanation: Corner points: (0,0)→0, (5,0)→10, (0,5)→5. Maximum P = 10 at (5, 0).

  Q4. Minimize C = 4x + 3y subject to x ≥ 0, y ≥ 0, x + y ≥ 6, x ≤ 8. At which point is C minimized?
    [ ] (3, 3)
    [ ] (6, 0)
    [*] (0, 6)
    [ ] (8, 0)
    Explanation: At (0,6): C = 0 + 18 = 18. At (6,0): C = 24 + 0 = 24. Since y has a smaller coefficient, putting more weight on y minimizes cost. C = 18 at (0, 6).

  Q5. How many corner points does the feasible region of x ≥ 0, y ≥ 0, x + y ≤ 4, 2x + y ≤ 6 have?
    [ ] 2
    [*] 4
    [ ] 5
    [ ] 3
    Explanation: The corners are (0,0), (3,0), (2,2), and (0,4). The lines x + y = 4 and 2x + y = 6 intersect at (2,2), giving 4 corners.

  Q6. Evaluate P = 5x + 2y at the corner points (0,0), (4,0), (0,3). Where is P maximum?
    [ ] All give the same value
    [ ] (0, 0)
    [ ] (0, 3)
    [*] (4, 0)
    Explanation: P(0,0) = 0, P(4,0) = 20, P(0,3) = 6. Maximum is 20 at (4, 0).

  Q7. If the feasible region is empty (no overlapping area), the linear programming problem has:
    [*] No feasible solution
    [ ] Infinitely many solutions
    [ ] A negative solution
    [ ] Exactly one solution
    Explanation: If the constraints are contradictory and no point satisfies all of them, the feasible region is empty and the problem has no feasible solution.

  Q8. Maximize P = x + 3y with constraints x ≥ 0, y ≥ 0, x + 2y ≤ 8, x + y ≤ 5. What is the max?
    [ ] 10
    [ ] 15
    [*] 12
    [ ] 8
    Explanation: Corner points: (0,0)→0, (5,0)→5, (2,3)→11, (0,4)→12. Max P = 12 at (0, 4).

  Q9. In linear programming, the optimal solution always occurs at:
    [*] A corner (vertex) of the feasible region
    [ ] Any interior point
    [ ] The center of the feasible region
    [ ] The origin
    Explanation: The Fundamental Theorem of Linear Programming states that if a maximum or minimum exists, it occurs at a vertex (corner point) of the feasible region.

  Q10. Given constraints x ≥ 0, y ≥ 0, and 3x + 2y ≤ 12, what is the corner point where the constraint line meets the x-axis?
    [ ] (6, 0)
    [ ] (0, 4)
    [*] (4, 0)
    [ ] (0, 6)
    Explanation: Set y = 0 in 3x + 2y = 12: 3x = 12, x = 4. The constraint line meets the x-axis at (4, 0).

  Q11. What is linear programming?
    [ ] Solving systems of linear equations
    [*] A method to optimize a linear objective function subject to linear constraints
    [ ] Graphing linear equations
    [ ] Writing computer programs using lines of code
    Explanation: Linear programming is a mathematical technique for finding the maximum or minimum value of a linear function (the objective) subject to a set of linear inequality constraints.

  Q12. What is an 'objective function' in linear programming?
    [ ] The set of all possible solutions
    [*] The linear function you want to maximize or minimize
    [ ] The feasible region
    [ ] Any constraint inequality
    Explanation: The objective function is the expression (like P = 3x + 5y) that you want to optimize. It represents the quantity you are trying to maximize (profit) or minimize (cost).

  Q13. What are 'constraints' in linear programming?
    [ ] The corner points of the graph
    [ ] The optimal solution values
    [ ] The objective function written as an equation
    [*] Linear inequalities that limit the values of the decision variables
    Explanation: Constraints are the inequalities that restrict the decision variables. They represent real-world limitations like budget, capacity, time, or resource availability.

  Q14. What is the 'feasible region' in linear programming?
    [ ] Only the corner points
    [*] The set of all points that satisfy all constraint inequalities simultaneously
    [ ] The entire coordinate plane
    [ ] The area outside all constraint lines
    Explanation: The feasible region is the geometric shape formed by the intersection of all constraint half-planes. Only points within this region are potential solutions.

  Q15. What is a 'vertex' (corner point) of the feasible region?
    [ ] Any point inside the feasible region
    [ ] The origin
    [ ] The center of the feasible region
    [*] A point where two or more constraint boundary lines intersect
    Explanation: A vertex is a corner of the feasible region where two or more constraint boundaries meet. The Corner Point Theorem guarantees the optimal solution occurs at one of these vertices.

  Q16. What does 'optimize' mean in mathematics?
    [ ] To simplify an expression
    [ ] To solve an equation
    [*] To find the maximum or minimum value of a function
    [ ] To graph a function
    Explanation: To optimize means to find the best possible value (maximum or minimum) of a quantity. In linear programming, we optimize the objective function within the feasible region.

  Q17. What are 'decision variables'?
    [ ] The coefficients of the objective function
    [ ] Constants in the constraints
    [*] The variables whose values we choose to optimize the objective function
    [ ] The values of the objective function at each corner
    Explanation: Decision variables (typically x and y) represent the quantities you can control or decide. For example, the number of each product to manufacture.

  Q18. What does the 'Corner Point Theorem' state?
    [ ] The feasible region always has four corners
    [ ] The optimal solution is always at the origin
    [ ] Every corner point gives the same objective value
    [*] If an optimal solution exists, it occurs at a vertex of the feasible region
    Explanation: The Corner Point Theorem guarantees that the maximum or minimum of a linear objective function over a convex feasible region occurs at one (or more) of the vertices of that region.

  Q19. What does 'bounded feasible region' mean?
    [ ] A feasible region that is empty
    [ ] A feasible region on the number line
    [*] A feasible region that is enclosed and does not extend to infinity
    [ ] A feasible region with only two constraints
    Explanation: A bounded feasible region is a closed, finite polygon. Both maximum and minimum of the objective function are guaranteed to exist when the region is bounded.

  Q20. What does 'unbounded feasible region' mean?
    [ ] A feasible region with all four quadrants
    [ ] A feasible region with no corner points
    [ ] A feasible region that is empty
    [*] A feasible region that extends infinitely in at least one direction
    Explanation: An unbounded region extends infinitely. A maximum may not exist in an unbounded region (it could be infinite), but a minimum might still exist at a vertex.

  Q21. A factory makes chairs ($30 profit) and tables ($50 profit). Each chair needs 2 hours of labor, each table needs 4 hours. With 40 hours available and needing at least 5 items total, how many of each maximizes profit?
    [ ] 10 chairs, 5 tables for $550
    [ ] 0 chairs, 10 tables for $500
    [ ] 5 chairs, 5 tables for $400
    [*] 20 chairs, 0 tables for $600
    Explanation: Constraints: 2c + 4t ≤ 40, c + t ≥ 5, c,t ≥ 0. At (20,0): 2(20) = 40 hours, P = 30(20) = $600. At (0,10): P = $500. At (10,5): 20+20 = 40, P = 300+250 = $550. Maximum profit is $600 at 20 chairs, 0 tables.

  Q22. A farmer wants to plant corn ($200/acre profit) and soybeans ($150/acre profit) on 100 acres. Corn needs 3 hours/acre and soybeans 2 hours/acre. With 240 hours available, how many acres of corn maximizes profit?
    [ ] 50 acres
    [ ] 60 acres
    [ ] 80 acres
    [*] 40 acres
    Explanation: Constraints: c + s ≤ 100, 3c + 2s ≤ 240, c,s ≥ 0. Corner: (0,0)→0, (80,0)→16000, (40,60)→8000+9000=17000, (0,100)→15000. Max profit $17,000 at 40 acres corn, 60 acres soybeans.

  Q23. A bakery makes cakes ($15 profit) and pies ($10 profit). Each cake needs 45 min of oven time, each pie needs 30 min. The oven is available 6 hours (360 min). At most 10 items total can be made. How many cakes maximizes profit?
    [ ] 6
    [ ] 10
    [*] 8
    [ ] 4
    Explanation: Constraints: c + p ≤ 10, 45c + 30p ≤ 360, c,p ≥ 0. Corner (8,0): 45(8)=360, P=120. Corner (0,10): 30(10)=300, P=100. Corner (4,6): 45(4)+30(6)=360, P=60+60=120. Max P=120 at (8,0) or (4,6); 8 cakes is the answer with max cakes.

  Q24. A shipping company has two routes. Route A costs $5/package with capacity of 200 packages. Route B costs $3/package with capacity of 300 packages. At least 400 packages must be shipped. What minimizes cost?
    [ ] 200 on Route A, 200 on Route B
    [ ] 200 on Route A, 300 on Route B
    [*] 100 on Route A, 300 on Route B
    [ ] 0 on Route A, 300 on Route B
    Explanation: Minimize C = 5a + 3b. Constraints: a ≤ 200, b ≤ 300, a + b ≥ 400, a,b ≥ 0. At (100,300): C = 500+900 = 1400. At (200,200): C = 1000+600 = 1600. Min cost is $1,400 with 100 on A and 300 on B.

  Q25. A nutrition plan requires at least 30 units of vitamin A and 20 units of vitamin C. Food X provides 5 units A and 2 units C per serving ($3 each). Food Y provides 3 units A and 4 units C per serving ($2 each). What minimizes cost?
    [ ] 4 of X and 4 of Y for $20
    [ ] 6 of X and 0 of Y for $18
    [*] 3 of X and 5 of Y for $19
    [ ] 0 of X and 10 of Y for $20
    Explanation: Constraints: 5x + 3y ≥ 30, 2x + 4y ≥ 20, x,y ≥ 0. At (3,5): A = 15+15 = 30, C = 6+20 = 26 ≥ 20. Cost = 9+10 = $19. At (6,0): A = 30, C = 12 < 20, not feasible. At (0,10): A = 30, C = 40. Cost = $20. Min = $19.

  Q26. A company makes gadgets ($8 profit) and widgets ($6 profit). Machine time: gadgets 4 min, widgets 3 min (300 min available). Assembly: gadgets 2 min, widgets 3 min (210 min available). Maximum production of gadgets?
    [ ] 70
    [ ] 60
    [ ] 50
    [*] 75
    Explanation: From machine time: 4g ≤ 300 → g ≤ 75. From assembly: 2g ≤ 210 → g ≤ 105. Maximum gadgets = 75 (with w = 0).

  Q27. A store orders jackets ($40 profit) and sweaters ($25 profit). Storage holds at most 100 items. Budget allows at most $6,000 in wholesale cost ($50/jacket, $30/sweater). How many jackets maximizes profit?
    [*] 100
    [ ] 60
    [ ] 50
    [ ] 75
    Explanation: j + s ≤ 100 and 50j + 30s ≤ 6000. At (100,0): cost = 5000 ≤ 6000, P = 40(100) = $4,000. At (0,100): P = $2,500. Max profit is $4,000 with 100 jackets.

  Q28. A school wants to buy desks ($100 each, need at least 20) and chairs ($40 each, need at least 30), with a total budget of $4,000. What is the maximum number of desks they can buy?
    [ ] 25
    [ ] 30
    [ ] 40
    [*] 28
    Explanation: 100d + 40c ≤ 4000, d ≥ 20, c ≥ 30. With minimum chairs c = 30: 100d + 1200 ≤ 4000 → 100d ≤ 2800 → d ≤ 28.

  Q29. A caterer offers two menus: Menu A ($12/person, takes 15 min to prepare) and Menu B ($8/person, takes 10 min). For 100 guests with 1200 minutes of prep time, she wants to maximize revenue. How many get Menu A?
    [ ] 60
    [ ] 80
    [ ] 50
    [*] 40
    Explanation: a + b = 100 (must serve all), 15a + 10b ≤ 1200. Substitute b = 100 - a: 15a + 1000 - 10a ≤ 1200 → 5a ≤ 200 → a ≤ 40. Revenue R = 12a + 8(100-a) = 4a + 800, max at a = 40: R = $960.

  Q30. A delivery company uses small trucks (capacity 50 packages, $100/trip) and large trucks (capacity 120 packages, $200/trip). They must deliver at least 600 packages. Small trucks can make at most 8 trips. What minimizes cost?
    [*] 0 small trips and 5 large trips for $1,000
    [ ] 4 small trips and 3 large trips for $1,000
    [ ] 6 small trips and 3 large trips for $1,200
    [ ] 8 small trips and 2 large trips for $1,200
    Explanation: Minimize C = 100s + 200L. Constraint: 50s + 120L ≥ 600, s ≤ 8, s,L ≥ 0. At (0,5): 120(5)=600≥600, C = 1000. At (8,2): 400+240=640≥600, C = 800+400=1200. Minimum cost is $1,000 with 0 small and 5 large trips.

--- Lesson 1.8: Linear Programming (Flashcards) ---

  1. Q: Corner points of system: x â‰¥ 0, y â‰¥ 0, x + y â‰¤ 6
     A: (0,0), (0,6), (6,0). Vertices of feasible region triangle.

  2. Q: Maximize P = 3x + 2y subject to xâ‰¥0, yâ‰¥0, x+yâ‰¤5
     A: P = 15. Maximum at (5,0): 3(5)+2(0)=15.

  3. Q: Objective function for profit problem?
     A: Profit = (unit marginâ‚)(quantityâ‚) + (unit marginâ‚‚)(quantityâ‚‚).

  4. Q: Constraints for production: type A uses 2 hours, type B uses 3 hours, 12 hours available
     A: 2x + 3y â‰¤ 12, x â‰¥ 0, y â‰¥ 0.

  5. Q: At corner points only, maximize/minimize linear objective function?
     A: True. Optimal value always achieved at vertex of feasible region.

  6. Q: Feasible region for x < 0, y > 0?
     A: Second quadrant only, excluding axes. x-values negative, y-values positive.

  7. Q: Empty feasible region indicates what?
     A: No solution exists. Constraints are contradictory.

     A: Production scheduling, resource allocation, diet optimization, etc.

     A: C = 10. Minimum at (1,2): needs check: 1+2=3 < 4? Need point (2,2) instead: C=12. Actual minimum at (1,3): C=14.

  10. Q: If objective value same at two corners, infinite optimal solutions?
     A: Yes. Any point on edge connecting those corners is optimal.

--- Lesson 1.9: Advanced Linear Applications (Summary) ---

  Key Concepts: Advanced Linear Applications
Overview
This lesson covers the fundamental measures of center used to analyze and summarize data sets. You'll learn how to calculate and apply the mean, median, and mode, and understand when each is most appropriate.
Key Definitions
A piecewise function is defined as f(x) = 2x for x < 3 and f(x) = x + 5 for x ≥ 3. What is f(3)?
Since x = 3 satisfies x ≥ 3, use the second piece: f(3) = 3 + 5 = 8.
What is the vertex of f(x) = |x - 3| + 2?
The absolute value function f(x) = |x - h| + k has vertex at (h, k). Here h = 3 and k = 2, so the vertex is (3, 2).
What is the slope of the line passing through (-1, 4) and (3, -8)?
Slope = (-8 - 4)/(3 - (-1)) = -12/4 = -3.
A three-variable system has equations x + y + z = 10, x = 2, and y = 3. What is z?
Substitute x = 2 and y = 3: 2 + 3 + z = 10 → z = 5.
A piecewise-linear function has f(x) = -x + 4 for x ≤ 2 and f(x) = x for x > 2. What is f(2)?
Since x = 2 satisfies x ≤ 2, use the first piece: f(2) = -2 + 4 = 2.
What is a piecewise function?
A piecewise function uses different expressions for different parts of its domain. For example, tax brackets create a piecewise-linear function.
What is the absolute value function?
The absolute value |x| gives the distance from x to 0 on the number line. Its graph is V-shaped, and |x| is always ≥ 0.
What is a step function?
A step function has constant values on intervals and jumps at certain points, creating a staircase pattern. The greatest integer function (floor function) is a common example.
What is a 'system of three equations in three variables'?
A 3x3 system has three equations with three unknowns. The solution is an ordered triple (x, y, z) that satisfies all three equations. Geometrically, it is the intersection of three planes.
What is the 'greatest integer function' (floor function)?
The greatest integer function ⌊x⌋ returns the greatest integer less than or equal to x. For example, ⌊3.7⌋ = 3 and ⌊-1.2⌋ = -2.
What is a 'discontinuity' in a function?
A discontinuity occurs where a function is not continuous — there is a break, jump, or hole. Step functions have jump discontinuities at each step.
A parking garage charges $5 for the first hour and $3 for each additional hour (or part thereof). Using the step function, what is the cost for parking 4.5 hours?
First hour: $5. Additional hours: 4.5 - 1 = 3.5, rounded up to 4 additional hours at $3 each = $12. Total: $5 + $12 = $17.
A shipping company charges based on weight: $5 for 0-2 lbs, $8 for 2-5 lbs, $12 for 5-10 lbs. What is the cost to ship a 4 lb package?
A 4 lb package falls in the 2-5 lb range, so the cost is $8. This is a step (piecewise-constant) function.
An engineer needs parts from two suppliers. Supplier A charges $10/part for orders under 50 and $8/part for 50 or more. The function is piecewise. If she orders 60 parts, what is the total cost?
Since 60 ≥ 50, the price is $8/part. Total = $8 × 60 = $480.
A thermometer reads temperatures in both Celsius and Fahrenheit. The absolute error in a reading is |measured - actual|. If the actual temperature is 100°F and the measured is 97°F, what is the absolute error?
|97 - 100| = |-3| = 3°F. Absolute error is always non-negative since it uses absolute value.
A company pays salespeople based on performance: $2,000/month base for sales under $10,000, plus a 10% commission on sales over $10,000. If a salesperson sells $15,000, what is their pay?
Base pay: $2,000. Commission on amount over $10,000: 0.10(15000 - 10000) = 0.10(5000) = $500. Total: $2,000 + $500 = $2,500.
A cell phone plan charges $30 for up to 100 minutes, then $0.25 per additional minute. If a customer uses 140 minutes, what is the bill?
Base: $30 for first 100 min. Extra: 40 minutes × $0.25 = $10. Total: $30 + $10 = $40.
Real-World Applications
Example: A step function rounds shipping weight up to the next pound. A 3.4 lb package is charged at which weight?
The ceiling function rounds up to the next integer. A 3.4 lb package is charged at 4 lbs.
Example: A parking garage charges $5 for the first hour and $3 for each additional hour (or part thereof). Using the step function, what is the cost for parking 4.5 hours?
First hour: $5. Additional hours: 4.5 - 1 = 3.5, rounded up to 4 additional hours at $3 each = $12. Total: $5 + $12 = $17.
Example: A shipping company charges based on weight: $5 for 0-2 lbs, $8 for 2-5 lbs, $12 for 5-10 lbs. What is the cost to ship a 4 lb package?
A 4 lb package falls in the 2-5 lb range, so the cost is $8. This is a step (piecewise-constant) function.
Example: A company pays salespeople based on performance: $2,000/month base for sales under $10,000, plus a 10% commission on sales over $10,000. If a salesperson sells $15,000, what is their pay?
Base pay: $2,000. Commission on amount over $10,000: 0.10(15000 - 10000) = 0.10(5000) = $500. Total: $2,000 + $500 = $2,500.

--- Lesson 1.9: Advanced Linear Applications (Quiz) ---

  Q1. A piecewise function is defined as f(x) = 2x for x < 3 and f(x) = x + 5 for x ≥ 3. What is f(3)?
    [ ] 11
    [*] 8
    [ ] 6
    [ ] 5
    Explanation: Since x = 3 satisfies x ≥ 3, use the second piece: f(3) = 3 + 5 = 8.

  Q2. Solve |2x - 6| = 10.
    [ ] x = 2 or x = -8
    [*] x = 8 or x = -2
    [ ] x = 5 or x = -5
    [ ] x = 8 only
    Explanation: Case 1: 2x - 6 = 10 → 2x = 16 → x = 8. Case 2: 2x - 6 = -10 → 2x = -4 → x = -2.

  Q3. What is the vertex of f(x) = |x - 3| + 2?
    [ ] (2, 3)
    [*] (3, 2)
    [ ] (-3, 2)
    [ ] (3, -2)
    Explanation: The absolute value function f(x) = |x - h| + k has vertex at (h, k). Here h = 3 and k = 2, so the vertex is (3, 2).

  Q4. A step function rounds shipping weight up to the next pound. A 3.4 lb package is charged at which weight?
    [ ] 3 lbs
    [*] 4 lbs
    [ ] 3.4 lbs
    [ ] 3.5 lbs
    Explanation: The ceiling function rounds up to the next integer. A 3.4 lb package is charged at 4 lbs.

  Q5. Solve |x + 1| > 4.
    [*] x > 3 or x < -5
    [ ] x > 5 or x < -3
    [ ] x > 4 or x < -4
    [ ] -5 < x < 3
    Explanation: For |x + 1| > 4: x + 1 > 4 → x > 3, or x + 1 < -4 → x < -5.

  Q6. What is the slope of the line passing through (-1, 4) and (3, -8)?
    [ ] 1/3
    [*] -3
    [ ] -1/3
    [ ] 3
    Explanation: Slope = (-8 - 4)/(3 - (-1)) = -12/4 = -3.

  Q7. Write the equation of a line through (2, 5) perpendicular to y = (1/3)x + 7.
    [ ] y = -3x + 1
    [ ] y = (1/3)x + 13/3
    [ ] y = 3x - 1
    [*] y = -3x + 11
    Explanation: Perpendicular slope = -3. Point-slope: y - 5 = -3(x - 2) → y = -3x + 6 + 5 = -3x + 11.

  Q8. A three-variable system has equations x + y + z = 10, x = 2, and y = 3. What is z?
    [*] 5
    [ ] 6
    [ ] 4
    [ ] 3
    Explanation: Substitute x = 2 and y = 3: 2 + 3 + z = 10 → z = 5.

  Q9. Solve the absolute value equation: |3x| = 15.
    [ ] x = 3 or x = -3
    [*] x = 5 or x = -5
    [ ] x = 15 or x = -15
    [ ] x = 5 only
    Explanation: 3x = 15 gives x = 5, and 3x = -15 gives x = -5. Both values make |3x| = 15.

  Q10. A piecewise-linear function has f(x) = -x + 4 for x ≤ 2 and f(x) = x for x > 2. What is f(2)?
    [ ] 0
    [ ] 6
    [ ] 4
    [*] 2
    Explanation: Since x = 2 satisfies x ≤ 2, use the first piece: f(2) = -2 + 4 = 2.

  Q11. What is a piecewise function?
    [ ] A function with only one formula
    [*] A function defined by different formulas on different intervals of its domain
    [ ] A function that is always linear
    [ ] A function that is undefined at some points
    Explanation: A piecewise function uses different expressions for different parts of its domain. For example, tax brackets create a piecewise-linear function.

  Q12. What is the absolute value function?
    [ ] f(x) = x², which squares the input
    [ ] f(x) = √x, the square root function
    [*] f(x) = |x|, which returns the distance of x from zero (always non-negative)
    [ ] f(x) = 1/x, the reciprocal function
    Explanation: The absolute value |x| gives the distance from x to 0 on the number line. Its graph is V-shaped, and |x| is always ≥ 0.

  Q13. What is a step function?
    [ ] A continuous linear function
    [ ] A function that always steps downward
    [*] A piecewise-constant function whose graph looks like a staircase
    [ ] A function that increases by one at each integer
    Explanation: A step function has constant values on intervals and jumps at certain points, creating a staircase pattern. The greatest integer function (floor function) is a common example.

  Q14. What does 'absolute value equation' mean?
    [ ] An equation that has exactly one solution
    [*] An equation containing an absolute value expression, which typically has two cases to solve
    [ ] An equation with no negative coefficients
    [ ] An equation that is always positive
    Explanation: An absolute value equation like |ax + b| = c splits into two cases: ax + b = c and ax + b = -c (when c > 0). This is because both c and -c have the same distance from zero.

  Q15. What is a 'system of three equations in three variables'?
    [ ] Three separate equations each with one variable
    [ ] Three inequalities graphed in 2D
    [*] Three equations involving three unknowns (x, y, z) solved simultaneously
    [ ] A system that always has three solutions
    Explanation: A 3x3 system has three equations with three unknowns. The solution is an ordered triple (x, y, z) that satisfies all three equations. Geometrically, it is the intersection of three planes.

  Q16. What does 'continuous' mean for a function?
    [*] The graph has no breaks, jumps, or holes
    [ ] The function is defined for all real numbers
    [ ] The function has a constant slope
    [ ] The function is always increasing
    Explanation: A continuous function has no breaks, jumps, or holes in its graph — you can draw it without lifting your pen. Step functions and some piecewise functions are discontinuous.

  Q17. What is the 'greatest integer function' (floor function)?
    [ ] A function that finds the largest number in a set
    [ ] A function that returns only positive integers
    [ ] A function that rounds up to the nearest integer
    [*] A function that rounds down to the nearest integer less than or equal to x
    Explanation: The greatest integer function ⌊x⌋ returns the greatest integer less than or equal to x. For example, ⌊3.7⌋ = 3 and ⌊-1.2⌋ = -2.

  Q18. What does 'piecewise-linear' mean?
    [ ] A function with curved segments
    [ ] A linear function defined for all real numbers
    [ ] A function with only one straight line
    [*] A function made up of straight-line segments on different intervals
    Explanation: A piecewise-linear function is composed of linear (straight-line) pieces on different intervals. The absolute value function is a classic example with two linear pieces meeting at a vertex.

  Q19. What is a 'discontinuity' in a function?
    [ ] A maximum or minimum point
    [ ] A point where the slope changes
    [ ] A point where the function equals zero
    [*] A point where the function has a break, jump, or hole in its graph
    Explanation: A discontinuity occurs where a function is not continuous — there is a break, jump, or hole. Step functions have jump discontinuities at each step.

  Q20. What does 'extraneous solution' mean?
    [*] A solution obtained algebraically that does not satisfy the original equation
    [ ] A solution that is a fraction when applying fundamental principles
    [ ] A very large solution, particularly regarding valid as
    [ ] A solution that is negative as observed in standard experiments
    Explanation: An extraneous solution arises from valid algebraic steps (like squaring both sides) but does not satisfy the original equation. Always check solutions in the original equation.

  Q21. A parking garage charges $5 for the first hour and $3 for each additional hour (or part thereof). Using the step function, what is the cost for parking 4.5 hours?
    [*] $17
    [ ] $14
    [ ] $20
    [ ] $16.50
    Explanation: First hour: $5. Additional hours: 4.5 - 1 = 3.5, rounded up to 4 additional hours at $3 each = $12. Total: $5 + $12 = $17.

  Q22. A shipping company charges based on weight: $5 for 0-2 lbs, $8 for 2-5 lbs, $12 for 5-10 lbs. What is the cost to ship a 4 lb package?
    [*] $8
    [ ] $5
    [ ] $10
    [ ] $12
    Explanation: A 4 lb package falls in the 2-5 lb range, so the cost is $8. This is a step (piecewise-constant) function.

  Q23. An engineer needs parts from two suppliers. Supplier A charges $10/part for orders under 50 and $8/part for 50 or more. The function is piecewise. If she orders 60 parts, what is the total cost?
    [ ] $500
    [ ] $600
    [*] $480
    [ ] $540
    Explanation: Since 60 ≥ 50, the price is $8/part. Total = $8 × 60 = $480.

  Q24. A thermometer reads temperatures in both Celsius and Fahrenheit. The absolute error in a reading is |measured - actual|. If the actual temperature is 100°F and the measured is 97°F, what is the absolute error?
    [ ] 0°F
    [*] 3°F
    [ ] -3°F
    [ ] 197°F
    Explanation: |97 - 100| = |-3| = 3°F. Absolute error is always non-negative since it uses absolute value.

  Q25. A company pays salespeople based on performance: $2,000/month base for sales under $10,000, plus a 10% commission on sales over $10,000. If a salesperson sells $15,000, what is their pay?
    [ ] $2,000
    [*] $2,500
    [ ] $1,500
    [ ] $3,500
    Explanation: Base pay: $2,000. Commission on amount over $10,000: 0.10(15000 - 10000) = 0.10(5000) = $500. Total: $2,000 + $500 = $2,500.

  Q26. A quality inspector rejects items where the weight deviates from the target by more than 0.5 grams. If the target is 50 grams, which inequality models acceptable weights?
    [ ] w ≤ 50.5
    [*] |w - 50| ≤ 0.5
    [ ] w > 49.5
    [ ] |w - 50| > 0.5
    Explanation: Acceptable weights are within 0.5g of the target: |w - 50| ≤ 0.5, which gives 49.5 ≤ w ≤ 50.5.

  Q27. Three friends order meals costing $x, $y, and $z. The total is $45, the first meal costs twice the third, and the second costs $5 more than the third. How much is the third meal?
    [*] $10
    [ ] $8
    [ ] $12
    [ ] $15
    Explanation: x = 2z, y = z + 5, x + y + z = 45. Substitute: 2z + (z + 5) + z = 45 → 4z + 5 = 45 → 4z = 40 → z = $10.

  Q28. A cell phone plan charges $30 for up to 100 minutes, then $0.25 per additional minute. If a customer uses 140 minutes, what is the bill?
    [ ] $35
    [*] $40
    [ ] $65
    [ ] $45
    Explanation: Base: $30 for first 100 min. Extra: 40 minutes × $0.25 = $10. Total: $30 + $10 = $40.

  Q29. A warehouse stores items in three sections. Section A holds x items, B holds y, and C holds z. Total capacity is 500, A holds 100 more than C, and B holds twice as many as C. How many does B hold?
    [*] 200
    [ ] 250
    [ ] 150
    [ ] 100
    Explanation: x = z + 100, y = 2z, x + y + z = 500. Substitute: (z + 100) + 2z + z = 500 → 4z = 400 → z = 100. So y = 2(100) = 200.

  Q30. A manufacturer's tolerance for a bolt diameter is |d - 10| ≤ 0.02 mm, where d is the actual diameter. A batch has bolts measuring 9.97, 10.01, and 10.03 mm. How many pass inspection?
    [ ] 2
    [*] 1
    [ ] 0
    [ ] 3
    Explanation: Acceptable: 9.98 ≤ d ≤ 10.02. Check: 9.97 is below range (fail), 10.01 is within (pass), 10.03 is above (fail). Only 1 bolt passes.

--- Lesson 1.9: Advanced Linear Applications (Flashcards) ---

  1. Q: Solve 3×3 system to find x, y, z form solution set
     A: Process: Gaussian elimination to row echelon form, then back-substitute.

  2. Q: Augmented matrix for x+y+z=6, 2x-y+z=3, x+2y-z=2?
     A: [1 1 1 | 6], [2 -1 1 | 3], [1 2 -1 | 2].

  3. Q: What does a row [0 0 0 | 5] mean in reduced matrix?
     A: Inconsistent system (0=5 is false). No solution exists.

  4. Q: Row [0 0 0 | 0] indicates what?
     A: Dependent system (infinitely many solutions). Free variables exist.

  5. Q: Back-substitution: from z=1 in 2x+y+3z=8, 2y+z=3
     A: From 2y+1=3: y=1. From 2x+1+3=8: x=2.

  6. Q: Parametric solution if z is free: x=3-z, y=2+z, z=t?
     A: Infinitely many: (3-t, 2+t, t). One parameter, line of solutions.

  7. Q: Classify system: x+y=1, x+y=2
     A: Inconsistent (parallel lines). No solution.

  8. Q: Solve: x-2y+z=0, 2x+y-z=5, x+y=2
     A: x=7/3, y=-1/3, z=5/3. Use elimination/substitution systematically.

  9. Q: AP Connection: how many solutions for generic 3×3 system?
     A: Unique (1), infinitely many, or none. Determinant crucial for existence.

  10. Q: Linear combination test: is (1,2,3) solution to x+y+z=6, 2x-y+z=3?
     A: 1+2+3=6 ✓, 2(1)-2+3=3 ✓. Yes, satisfies both (third equation needed).

--- Lesson 2.1: Quadratic Functions & Parabolas (Summary) ---

  Key Concepts: Quadratic Functions & Parabolas
Overview
This lesson covers the fundamental measures of center used to analyze and summarize data sets. You'll learn how to calculate and apply the mean, median, and mode, and understand when each is most appropriate.
Key Definitions
What is the vertex of f(x) = x² − 4x + 3?
Using x = −b/(2a) = 4/2 = 2, then y = (2)² − 4(2) + 3 = 4 − 8 + 3 = −1. The vertex is (2, −1).
What is the y-intercept of f(x) = x² − 6x + 8?
The y-intercept is found by setting x = 0: f(0) = 0 − 0 + 8 = 8. In y = ax² + bx + c, the y-intercept is always c.
What is the minimum value of f(x) = 3(x + 1)² + 2?
In vertex form f(x) = a(x − h)² + k, the minimum (when a > 0) is k. Here k = 2, so the minimum value is 2, occurring at x = −1.
What is the vertex of y = (x − 3)² − 4?
In vertex form y = a(x − h)² + k, the vertex is (h, k). Here h = 3 and k = −4, so the vertex is (3, −4).
What is the minimum value of y = x² − 4x + 7?
The vertex x-coordinate is x = 4/2 = 2. Then y = (2)² − 4(2) + 7 = 4 − 8 + 7 = 3. Since a = 1 > 0, the minimum value is 3.
What is a quadratic function?
A quadratic function is a polynomial of degree 2, written f(x) = ax² + bx + c where a ≠ 0. Its graph is always a parabola.
What is a parabola?
A parabola is the U-shaped curve produced by graphing a quadratic function. It is symmetric about a vertical line called the axis of symmetry.
What is the vertex of a parabola?
The vertex is the turning point of the parabola — its maximum (if the parabola opens down) or minimum (if it opens up). It lies on the axis of symmetry.
What is the 'standard form' of a quadratic function?
Standard form is y = ax² + bx + c. It directly shows the y-intercept (c) and is useful for applying the quadratic formula.
What is the 'vertex form' of a quadratic function?
Vertex form is y = a(x − h)² + k. It immediately reveals the vertex (h, k) and the direction of opening (sign of a).
What is the 'factored form' of a quadratic function?
Factored form is y = a(x − p)(x − q). It directly shows the zeros (x-intercepts) at x = p and x = q, making it useful for graphing and solving.
A football is kicked and its height in feet is modeled by h(t) = −16t² + 48t. What is the maximum height the football reaches?
The maximum occurs at t = −48/(2·(−16)) = 1.5 seconds. h(1.5) = −16(1.5)² + 48(1.5) = −36 + 72 = 36 feet.
A store sells shirts and models its daily revenue as R(p) = −2p² + 80p, where p is the price in dollars. What price maximizes revenue, and what is the maximum revenue?
Maximum revenue is at p = −80/(2·(−2)) = 20. Then R(20) = −2(400) + 80(20) = −800 + 1600 = $800.
A bridge arch is modeled by h(x) = −0.01x² + 2x, where x is the horizontal distance in feet. What is the maximum height of the arch?
The vertex x-coordinate is x = −2/(2·(−0.01)) = 100. Then h(100) = −0.01(10000) + 2(100) = −100 + 200 = 100 feet.
A cliff diver jumps from a 40-foot cliff. Her height is h(t) = −16t² + 8t + 40. What is the maximum height she reaches above the water?
Maximum at t = −8/(2·(−16)) = 0.25 s. h(0.25) = −16(0.0625) + 8(0.25) + 40 = −1 + 2 + 40 = 41 feet.

--- Lesson 2.1: Quadratic Functions & Parabolas (Quiz) ---

  Q1. What is the vertex of f(x) = x² − 4x + 3?
    [ ] (1, 0)
    [*] (2, −1)
    [ ] (3, 0)
    [ ] (0, 3)
    Explanation: Using x = −b/(2a) = 4/2 = 2, then y = (2)² − 4(2) + 3 = 4 − 8 + 3 = −1. The vertex is (2, −1).

  Q2. The formula for the axis of symmetry of y = ax² + bx + c is:
    [ ] y = −b/(2a)
    [*] x = −b/(2a)
    [ ] x = b/2a
    [ ] x = a/b
    Explanation: The axis of symmetry of a parabola y = ax² + bx + c is the vertical line x = −b/(2a). This line passes through the vertex and divides the parabola into two mirror-image halves.

  Q3. Does the parabola f(x) = −2x² + 5 open upward or downward?
    [ ] It depends on x
    [ ] Sideways
    [ ] Upward
    [*] Downward
    Explanation: Since the leading coefficient a = −2 is negative, the parabola opens downward. A positive leading coefficient would make it open upward.

  Q4. What is the y-intercept of f(x) = x² − 6x + 8?
    [ ] −8
    [ ] −6
    [*] 8
    [ ] 6
    Explanation: The y-intercept is found by setting x = 0: f(0) = 0 − 0 + 8 = 8. In y = ax² + bx + c, the y-intercept is always c.

  Q5. To complete the square for x² − 8x, what number must be added?
    [ ] 8
    [ ] 4
    [*] 16
    [ ] 64
    Explanation: Take half the coefficient of x: (−8/2)² = (−4)² = 16. Adding 16 gives x² − 8x + 16 = (x − 4)², a perfect square trinomial.

  Q6. What is the minimum value of f(x) = 3(x + 1)² + 2?
    [ ] 3
    [ ] 0
    [*] 2
    [ ] −1
    Explanation: In vertex form f(x) = a(x − h)² + k, the minimum (when a > 0) is k. Here k = 2, so the minimum value is 2, occurring at x = −1.

  Q7. Which equation represents a parabola with vertex (5, 3) that opens upward?
    [*] f(x) = a(x − 5)² + 3, where a > 0
    [ ] f(x) = a(x − 3)² + 5
    [ ] f(x) = a(x + 5)² − 3
    [ ] f(x) = a(x − 5)² + 3, where a < 0
    Explanation: Vertex form is f(x) = a(x − h)² + k with vertex (h, k). For vertex (5, 3) and opening upward, h = 5, k = 3, and a > 0.

  Q8. If a > 0 in y = ax² + bx + c, the parabola opens:
    [ ] Left
    [ ] Downward
    [ ] Right
    [*] Upward
    Explanation: When a > 0, the parabola opens upward and has a minimum value at its vertex. When a < 0, it opens downward with a maximum.

  Q9. What is the vertex of y = (x − 3)² − 4?
    [ ] (−3, −4)
    [ ] (−3, 4)
    [ ] (3, 4)
    [*] (3, −4)
    Explanation: In vertex form y = a(x − h)² + k, the vertex is (h, k). Here h = 3 and k = −4, so the vertex is (3, −4).

  Q10. What is the minimum value of y = x² − 4x + 7?
    [*] 3
    [ ] 7
    [ ] 4
    [ ] −3
    Explanation: The vertex x-coordinate is x = 4/2 = 2. Then y = (2)² − 4(2) + 7 = 4 − 8 + 7 = 3. Since a = 1 > 0, the minimum value is 3.

  Q11. What is a quadratic function?
    [*] A function of the form f(x) = ax² + bx + c where a ≠ 0
    [ ] Any function with an x² term
    [ ] A function whose graph is a straight line
    [ ] A function of the form f(x) = ax³ + bx + c
    Explanation: A quadratic function is a polynomial of degree 2, written f(x) = ax² + bx + c where a ≠ 0. Its graph is always a parabola.

  Q12. What is a parabola?
    [ ] A straight line graph, particularly regarding called as
    [*] The U-shaped (or inverted-U) curve that is the graph of a quadratic function
    [ ] Any curved graph, particularly regarding parabola based on
    [ ] A circle on the coordinate plane in the context of this analysis
    Explanation: A parabola is the U-shaped curve produced by graphing a quadratic function. It is symmetric about a vertical line called the axis of symmetry.

  Q13. What is the vertex of a parabola?
    [ ] The y-intercept of the parabola
    [ ] The point where the parabola crosses the y-axis
    [ ] The point where the parabola crosses the x-axis
    [*] The highest or lowest point on the parabola
    Explanation: The vertex is the turning point of the parabola — its maximum (if the parabola opens down) or minimum (if it opens up). It lies on the axis of symmetry.

  Q14. What does 'axis of symmetry' mean for a parabola?
    [ ] The line y = x, particularly regarding every as typically
    [ ] The x-axis, particularly regarding does as typically
    [ ] A horizontal line through the vertex
    [*] The vertical line that divides the parabola into two mirror-image halves
    Explanation: The axis of symmetry is the vertical line x = −b/(2a) that passes through the vertex. Every point on the parabola has a mirror point on the other side of this line.

  Q15. What is the 'standard form' of a quadratic function?
    [ ] y = a(x − h)² + k
    [*] y = ax² + bx + c
    [ ] y = a(x − p)(x − q)
    [ ] y = mx + b
    Explanation: Standard form is y = ax² + bx + c. It directly shows the y-intercept (c) and is useful for applying the quadratic formula.

  Q16. What is the 'vertex form' of a quadratic function?
    [ ] y = mx + b, particularly regarding
    [*] y = a(x − h)² + k, where (h, k) is the vertex
    [ ] y = ax² + bx + c in most standard
    [ ] y = a(x − p)(x − q) when measured
    Explanation: Vertex form is y = a(x − h)² + k. It immediately reveals the vertex (h, k) and the direction of opening (sign of a).

  Q17. What does the 'leading coefficient' of a quadratic tell you about the parabola?
    [ ] It tells you the vertex location
    [ ] It gives the y-intercept
    [*] It determines the direction the parabola opens and how wide or narrow it is
    [ ] It determines the x-intercepts
    Explanation: The leading coefficient a determines direction (positive = up, negative = down) and width (larger |a| = narrower, smaller |a| = wider).

  Q18. What does 'maximum value' mean for a quadratic function?
    [*] The largest y-value the function attains, occurring at the vertex when a < 0
    [ ] The largest coefficient in the equation
    [ ] The largest x-value in the domain
    [ ] The y-intercept
    Explanation: When a < 0, the parabola opens downward and the vertex is the highest point. The y-coordinate of the vertex is the maximum value of the function.

  Q19. What is the 'factored form' of a quadratic function?
    [ ] y = ax² + bx + c, particularly regarding
    [ ] y = mx + b, particularly regarding graphing
    [*] y = a(x − p)(x − q), where p and q are the x-intercepts
    [ ] y = a(x − h)² + k following the established framework
    Explanation: Factored form is y = a(x − p)(x − q). It directly shows the zeros (x-intercepts) at x = p and x = q, making it useful for graphing and solving.

  Q20. What does 'completing the square' mean?
    [ ] Drawing a square on the coordinate grid
    [ ] Finding the square root of the quadratic
    [*] A method that rewrites a quadratic expression as a perfect square trinomial plus a constant
    [ ] Multiplying a binomial by itself
    Explanation: Completing the square converts ax² + bx + c into vertex form a(x − h)² + k by adding and subtracting (b/(2a))² to create a perfect square trinomial.

  Q21. A football is kicked and its height in feet is modeled by h(t) = −16t² + 48t. What is the maximum height the football reaches?
    [ ] 16 feet
    [ ] 48 feet
    [ ] 24 feet
    [*] 36 feet
    Explanation: The maximum occurs at t = −48/(2·(−16)) = 1.5 seconds. h(1.5) = −16(1.5)² + 48(1.5) = −36 + 72 = 36 feet.

  Q22. A company's profit is modeled by P(x) = −5x² + 200x − 1500, where x is the number of units sold. How many units should be sold to maximize profit?
    [*] 20 units
    [ ] 10 units
    [ ] 30 units
    [ ] 40 units
    Explanation: Maximum profit occurs at the vertex: x = −200/(2·(−5)) = −200/(−10) = 20 units. Since a < 0, this is indeed a maximum.

  Q23. A farmer has 60 meters of fencing and wants to enclose a rectangular garden along a barn wall (so only three sides need fencing). If the width is w meters, the area is A(w) = w(60 − 2w). What width maximizes the area?
    [ ] 10 meters
    [ ] 30 meters
    [*] 15 meters
    [ ] 20 meters
    Explanation: Expand: A(w) = −2w² + 60w. The vertex is at w = −60/(2·(−2)) = 15. The maximum area is A(15) = 15(60 − 30) = 450 m².

  Q24. A ball is thrown upward from a 20-foot rooftop with an initial velocity of 32 ft/s. Its height is h(t) = −16t² + 32t + 20. When does the ball hit the ground (h = 0)?
    [ ] Approximately 3.5 seconds
    [*] Approximately 2.5 seconds
    [ ] Exactly 1 second
    [ ] Exactly 2 seconds
    Explanation: Set h(t) = 0: −16t² + 32t + 20 = 0, or 4t² − 8t − 5 = 0. Using the quadratic formula: t = (8 ± √(64 + 80))/8 = (8 ± 12)/8. The positive solution is t = 20/8 = 2.5 seconds.

  Q25. A store sells shirts and models its daily revenue as R(p) = −2p² + 80p, where p is the price in dollars. What price maximizes revenue, and what is the maximum revenue?
    [ ] $20 per shirt; $400 maximum revenue
    [*] $20 per shirt; $800 maximum revenue
    [ ] $40 per shirt; $800 maximum revenue
    [ ] $10 per shirt; $600 maximum revenue
    Explanation: Maximum revenue is at p = −80/(2·(−2)) = 20. Then R(20) = −2(400) + 80(20) = −800 + 1600 = $800.

  Q26. A bridge arch is modeled by h(x) = −0.01x² + 2x, where x is the horizontal distance in feet. What is the maximum height of the arch?
    [*] 100 feet
    [ ] 200 feet
    [ ] 50 feet
    [ ] 150 feet
    Explanation: The vertex x-coordinate is x = −2/(2·(−0.01)) = 100. Then h(100) = −0.01(10000) + 2(100) = −100 + 200 = 100 feet.

  Q27. A toy rocket's height is h(t) = −4.9t² + 29.4t + 2 meters. At what time does it reach its maximum height?
    [ ] 2 seconds
    [*] 3 seconds
    [ ] 4 seconds
    [ ] 5 seconds
    Explanation: Maximum height occurs at t = −29.4/(2·(−4.9)) = −29.4/(−9.8) = 3 seconds.

  Q28. A rectangular playground has a perimeter of 100 meters. Its area A = w(50 − w), where w is the width. What dimensions maximize the area?
    [*] 25 m × 25 m (a square)
    [ ] 15 m × 35 m
    [ ] 20 m × 30 m
    [ ] 10 m × 40 m
    Explanation: A = −w² + 50w has its vertex at w = 50/2 = 25. Then the length is also 50 − 25 = 25, forming a square with maximum area 625 m².

  Q29. A theater charges $10 per ticket and sells 200 tickets. For every $1 increase in price, 10 fewer tickets are sold. Revenue is R(x) = (10 + x)(200 − 10x). What price increase x maximizes revenue?
    [ ] $3
    [*] $5
    [ ] $10
    [ ] $8
    Explanation: Expand: R(x) = −10x² + 100x + 2000. Vertex at x = −100/(2·(−10)) = 5. The optimal ticket price is $10 + $5 = $15 with revenue R(5) = $2,250.

  Q30. A cliff diver jumps from a 40-foot cliff. Her height is h(t) = −16t² + 8t + 40. What is the maximum height she reaches above the water?
    [ ] 48 feet
    [ ] 40 feet
    [ ] 44 feet
    [*] 41 feet
    Explanation: Maximum at t = −8/(2·(−16)) = 0.25 s. h(0.25) = −16(0.0625) + 8(0.25) + 40 = −1 + 2 + 40 = 41 feet.

--- Lesson 2.1: Quadratic Functions & Parabolas (Flashcards) ---

  1. Q: Find vertex of f(x) = x² - 4x + 3
     A: (2, -1). h = -b/2a = 4/2 = 2, k = f(2) = 4-8+3 = -1.

  2. Q: Axis of symmetry for f(x) = 2(x-3)²+5
     A: x = 3. From vertex form (x-h)²+k, axis is x = h.

  3. Q: Does f(x) = -x² + 2x - 3 open up or down?
     A: Down. a = -1 < 0 opens downward.

  4. Q: Y-intercept of f(x) = x² - 6x + 8?
     A: 8. Set x=0: f(0) = 0 - 0 + 8 = 8. Point: (0,8).

  5. Q: Find vertex by completing the square: f(x) = x² - 8x + 5
     A: (4, -11). x² - 8x + 5 = (x-4)² - 16 + 5 = (x-4)² - 11.

  6. Q: Minimum or maximum of f(x) = 3(x+1)² + 2?
     A: Minimum = 2. a=3>0 opens up, minimum is k-value.

  7. Q: Vertex form with vertex (5, -3)?
     A: f(x) = a(x-5)² - 3 for some a≠0.

  8. Q: Standard form from f(x) = (x-2)² - 4?
     A: f(x) = x² - 4x + 4 - 4 = x² - 4x. Expand and simplify.

  9. Q: If vertex (2, 3) and point (4, 7) on parabola, find a
     A: a = 1. 7 = a(4-2)² + 3 = 4a + 3, so a = 1.

  10. Q: Domain and range of f(x) = -(x-1)²+4?
     A: Domain: all reals. Range: (-∞, 4]. Opens down, max = 4.

--- Lesson 2.2: Transformations of Quadratics (Summary) ---

  Key Concepts: Transformations of Quadratics
Overview
This lesson covers the fundamental measures of center used to analyze and summarize data sets. You'll learn how to calculate and apply the mean, median, and mode, and understand when each is most appropriate.
Key Definitions
What is the vertex of y = (x − 3)² + 7?
In vertex form y = a(x - h)² + k, the vertex is (h, k). Here h = 3 and k = 7, so the vertex is (3, 7).
What is the vertex of y = −2(x + 4)² − 1?
In vertex form y = a(x − h)² + k, the vertex is (h, k). Here (x + 4) = (x − (−4)), so h = −4 and k = −1, giving vertex (−4, −1).
What is a vertical stretch of a quadratic function?
A vertical stretch occurs when the coefficient |a| > 1 in y = ax². It multiplies all y-values by that factor, pulling the graph away from the x-axis and making the parabola narrower.
What is a vertical compression of a quadratic function?
A vertical compression occurs when 0 < |a| < 1. It pushes the graph closer to the x-axis, making the parabola wider and flatter.
What is the 'parent function' for quadratic transformations?
The parent function y = x² is the most basic quadratic. All other quadratic functions can be obtained by applying transformations such as shifts, stretches, compressions, and reflections to this parent.
What is the 'axis of symmetry' of a transformed quadratic?
The axis of symmetry is the vertical line x = h that passes through the vertex. Every point on one side of this line has a mirror point on the other side.
What is meant by 'order of transformations' for quadratics?
When applying multiple transformations, the standard approach is to apply horizontal shifts first, then stretches/compressions and reflections, and finally vertical shifts to ensure the correct graph.
A drone starts at ground level and its altitude in meters is modeled by A(t) = −2(t − 5)² + 50 where t is time in seconds. What is the drone's maximum altitude?
The equation is in vertex form with vertex (5, 50). Since a = −2 < 0, the parabola opens downward and the vertex gives the maximum altitude of 50 meters.
An architect designs a parabolic window described by y = −0.5(x − 4)² + 8. Is this window wider or narrower than the standard arch y = −x², and what is the peak height?
Since |a| = 0.5 < 1, the parabola is vertically compressed (wider) than y = −x². The vertex is at (4, 8), so the peak height is 8 units.
A roller coaster track dip is modeled by y = 3(x − 10)² − 12 where y is height in meters relative to a reference point. What is the lowest point of the dip?
With a = 3 > 0, the parabola opens upward and the vertex (10, −12) is the minimum. The lowest point is 12 meters below the reference at x = 10.

--- Lesson 2.2: Transformations of Quadratics (Quiz) ---

  Q1. What is the vertex of y = (x − 3)² + 7?
    [ ] (3, -7)
    [ ] (-3, 7)
    [*] (3, 7)
    [ ] (7, 3)
    Explanation: In vertex form y = a(x - h)² + k, the vertex is (h, k). Here h = 3 and k = 7, so the vertex is (3, 7).

  Q2. Compared to y = x², the graph of y = x² − 4 is shifted:
    [ ] Left 4 units
    [*] Down 4 units
    [ ] Up 4 units
    [ ] Right 4 units
    Explanation: Adding or subtracting a constant outside the squared term shifts the graph vertically. Subtracting 4 shifts the graph down 4 units.

  Q3. Compared to y = x², the graph of y = (x + 5)² is shifted:
    [ ] Right 5 units
    [ ] Down 5 units
    [*] Left 5 units
    [ ] Up 5 units
    Explanation: In y = (x + 5)², the +5 inside the parentheses means x is replaced by (x − (−5)), so h = −5, which shifts the graph left 5 units.

  Q4. The graph of y = −x² is a reflection of y = x² over which axis?
    [ ] The line y = x
    [ ] The y-axis
    [ ] The origin
    [*] The x-axis
    Explanation: Multiplying the entire function by −1 (negating the output) reflects the graph over the x-axis, flipping it upside down.

  Q5. The graph of y = 4x² compared to y = x² is:
    [ ] Wider (vertical compression)
    [ ] Reflected
    [ ] Shifted up 4
    [*] Narrower (vertical stretch by factor 4)
    Explanation: When |a| > 1, the parabola is vertically stretched and appears narrower. Since a = 4 > 1, the graph is narrower than y = x².

  Q6. The graph of y = (1/3)x² compared to y = x² is:
    [*] Wider (vertical compression by factor 1/3)
    [ ] Narrower
    [ ] Shifted right 3
    [ ] Reflected over the x-axis
    Explanation: When 0 < |a| < 1, the parabola is vertically compressed and appears wider. Since a = 1/3, the graph is wider than y = x².

  Q7. What transformation converts y = x² to y = (x − 2)² + 6?
    [ ] Left 2, down 6
    [*] Right 2, up 6
    [ ] Right 2, down 6
    [ ] Left 2, up 6
    Explanation: In y = (x − 2)² + 6, h = 2 shifts right 2 units and k = 6 shifts up 6 units from the parent function y = x².

  Q8. What is the vertex of y = −2(x + 4)² − 1?
    [ ] (−4, 1)
    [ ] (4, 1)
    [*] (−4, −1)
    [ ] (4, −1)
    Explanation: In vertex form y = a(x − h)² + k, the vertex is (h, k). Here (x + 4) = (x − (−4)), so h = −4 and k = −1, giving vertex (−4, −1).

  Q9. Which of the following has the widest graph?
    [ ] y = 5x²
    [*] y = (1/5)x²
    [ ] y = 2x²
    [ ] y = x²
    Explanation: The smaller the value of |a|, the wider the parabola. Since |1/5| = 0.2 is the smallest among the choices, y = (1/5)x² is the widest.

  Q10. Reflecting y = x² over the y-axis gives:
    [ ] y = x² + 1, particularly
    [*] y = x² (the same graph, since x² = (−x)²)
    [ ] y = −x² + 1, particularly
    [ ] y = −x², particularly regarding
    Explanation: Reflecting over the y-axis replaces x with −x, giving y = (−x)² = x². Because y = x² is symmetric about the y-axis, the reflection is identical to the original.

  Q11. What is a vertical stretch of a quadratic function?
    [ ] A shift of the graph up or down as predicted by standard models
    [ ] A reflection across the x-axis in accordance with classical theory
    [*] A transformation that multiplies y-values by a factor greater than 1, making the parabola narrower
    [ ] A shift of the graph left or right as observed in standard experiments
    Explanation: A vertical stretch occurs when the coefficient |a| > 1 in y = ax². It multiplies all y-values by that factor, pulling the graph away from the x-axis and making the parabola narrower.

  Q12. What is a vertical compression of a quadratic function?
    [ ] A shift of the graph down
    [ ] A flip of the graph over the x-axis
    [*] A transformation that multiplies y-values by a factor between 0 and 1, making the parabola wider
    [ ] A transformation that makes the parabola narrower
    Explanation: A vertical compression occurs when 0 < |a| < 1. It pushes the graph closer to the x-axis, making the parabola wider and flatter.

  Q13. What does 'translation' mean in the context of quadratic transformations?
    [ ] A reflection over an axis, particularly regarding every under normal circumstances
    [ ] A stretch or compression of the graph when evaluated systematically
    [ ] A rotation of the graph, particularly regarding moves as typically measured in practice
    [*] A sliding movement of the entire graph horizontally, vertically, or both without changing its shape
    Explanation: A translation (or shift) moves every point of the graph the same distance in the same direction, preserving the shape and orientation of the parabola.

  Q14. What is the 'parent function' for quadratic transformations?
    [ ] y = |x|, particularly regarding function as typically measured in practice
    [ ] y = mx + b, particularly regarding other in the context of this analysis
    [ ] y = 2x, particularly regarding such in the context of this analysis
    [*] y = x² — the simplest quadratic function from which all others are derived through transformations
    Explanation: The parent function y = x² is the most basic quadratic. All other quadratic functions can be obtained by applying transformations such as shifts, stretches, compressions, and reflections to this parent.

  Q15. What does the parameter 'h' represent in vertex form y = a(x − h)² + k?
    [ ] The direction the parabola opens
    [ ] The stretch or compression factor
    [*] The horizontal shift — the x-coordinate of the vertex
    [ ] The vertical shift (up or down)
    Explanation: In y = a(x − h)² + k, h gives the horizontal shift from the parent function and equals the x-coordinate of the vertex.

  Q16. What does the parameter 'k' represent in vertex form y = a(x − h)² + k?
    [ ] The axis of symmetry
    [ ] The stretch factor
    [*] The vertical shift — the y-coordinate of the vertex
    [ ] The horizontal shift
    Explanation: In y = a(x − h)² + k, the parameter k gives the vertical shift from the parent function and equals the y-coordinate of the vertex.

  Q17. What does 'reflection over the x-axis' mean for a quadratic?
    [ ] Making the parabola narrower
    [ ] Shifting the graph below the x-axis
    [*] Flipping the graph upside down by negating the function, so y = x² becomes y = −x²
    [ ] Replacing x with −x in the function
    Explanation: A reflection over the x-axis negates every y-value. For a quadratic, this turns an upward-opening parabola into a downward-opening one (and vice versa).

  Q18. What is the 'axis of symmetry' of a transformed quadratic?
    [*] The vertical line x = h that passes through the vertex and divides the parabola into two mirror-image halves
    [ ] The x-axis, particularly regarding through under the given assumptions
    [ ] The y-intercept of the parabola, particularly regarding vertical as observed in standard experiments
    [ ] The horizontal line through the vertex following the established framework
