    Explanation: The axis of symmetry is the vertical line x = h that passes through the vertex. Every point on one side of this line has a mirror point on the other side.

  Q19. What does 'horizontal shift' mean in transformations?
    [ ] Reflecting the graph over the y-axis
    [ ] Stretching the graph horizontally
    [ ] Moving the graph up or down by adding a constant outside the function
    [*] Moving the graph left or right by replacing x with (x − h) inside the function
    Explanation: A horizontal shift replaces x with (x − h). If h > 0 the graph moves right; if h < 0 the graph moves left. The shape of the parabola remains unchanged.

  Q20. What is meant by 'order of transformations' for quadratics?
    [*] The recommended sequence: horizontal shifts first, then stretches/compressions and reflections, then vertical shifts
    [ ] Reflections must always be applied last
    [ ] Vertical shifts must always come before horizontal shifts
    [ ] Transformations can always be applied in any order with the same result
    Explanation: When applying multiple transformations, the standard approach is to apply horizontal shifts first, then stretches/compressions and reflections, and finally vertical shifts to ensure the correct graph.

  Q21. A drone starts at ground level and its altitude in meters is modeled by A(t) = −2(t − 5)² + 50 where t is time in seconds. What is the drone's maximum altitude?
    [ ] 5 meters
    [ ] 100 meters
    [ ] 25 meters
    [*] 50 meters
    Explanation: The equation is in vertex form with vertex (5, 50). Since a = −2 < 0, the parabola opens downward and the vertex gives the maximum altitude of 50 meters.

  Q22. A water fountain's arch is modeled by y = −(x − 3)² + 9, where y is height in feet and x is horizontal distance. Compared to y = −x², this arch has been shifted:
    [ ] Left 3 and down 9
    [ ] Right 9 and up 3
    [ ] Left 3 and up 9
    [*] Right 3 and up 9
    Explanation: In y = −(x − 3)² + 9, h = 3 shifts the arch right 3 feet and k = 9 shifts it up 9 feet from the parent function y = −x².

  Q23. An architect designs a parabolic window described by y = −0.5(x − 4)² + 8. Is this window wider or narrower than the standard arch y = −x², and what is the peak height?
    [ ] Wider; peak height is 4 units
    [ ] Narrower; peak height is 8 units
    [*] Wider; peak height is 8 units
    [ ] Narrower; peak height is 4 units
    Explanation: Since |a| = 0.5 < 1, the parabola is vertically compressed (wider) than y = −x². The vertex is at (4, 8), so the peak height is 8 units.

  Q24. A roller coaster track dip is modeled by y = 3(x − 10)² − 12 where y is height in meters relative to a reference point. What is the lowest point of the dip?
    [ ] 3 meters below the reference at x = 10
    [*] 12 meters below the reference at x = 10
    [ ] 12 meters above the reference at x = 10
    [ ] 10 meters below the reference at x = 12
    Explanation: With a = 3 > 0, the parabola opens upward and the vertex (10, −12) is the minimum. The lowest point is 12 meters below the reference at x = 10.

  Q25. A ball is thrown and its height is h(t) = −16(t − 1.5)² + 36. A second ball follows h(t) = −16(t − 1.5)² + 49. How much higher does the second ball reach compared to the first?
    [ ] 85 feet higher
    [ ] 49 feet higher
    [*] 13 feet higher
    [ ] 36 feet higher
    Explanation: The first ball reaches a maximum of 36 feet and the second reaches 49 feet. The difference is 49 − 36 = 13 feet higher.

  Q26. A spotlight projects a parabolic beam modeled by y = 5x². If the beam is adjusted to y = 5(x − 2)² + 3, how has the center of the beam moved?
    [ ] Left 2 units and down 3 units
    [*] Right 2 units and up 3 units
    [ ] Left 2 units and up 3 units
    [ ] Right 3 units and up 2 units
    Explanation: The vertex moved from (0, 0) to (2, 3). That is a shift of 2 units right and 3 units up.

  Q27. A physics teacher demonstrates that a ball dropped from rest follows h = −16t² + 64 and a ball thrown downward follows h = −48t² + 64. Is the thrown ball's path narrower or wider, and why?
    [ ] Wider, because |a| is larger
    [ ] The same width, because both have the same starting height
    [ ] Wider, because the ball is going faster
    [*] Narrower, because |−48| > |−16| means a greater vertical stretch
    Explanation: A larger |a| value produces a narrower (steeper) parabola. Since |−48| = 48 > 16 = |−16|, the thrown ball's graph is narrower, indicating it descends more steeply.

  Q28. A company's daily profit in dollars is modeled by P(x) = −(x − 50)² + 2500 where x is the number of units sold. If the company lowers costs so the model becomes P(x) = −(x − 50)² + 3000, what changed?
    [ ] The parabola became wider
    [ ] The optimal number of units changed from 50 to 60
    [*] The maximum profit increased by $500 while the optimal quantity stayed the same
    [ ] The graph reflected over the x-axis
    Explanation: Only k changed from 2500 to 3000, an increase of $500. The vertex moved from (50, 2500) to (50, 3000), so the maximum profit rose by $500 while the optimal quantity stayed at 50 units.

  Q29. An engineer models a bridge cable as y = 0.01(x − 100)² + 5. If the cable is redesigned to y = 0.02(x − 100)² + 5, how does the cable shape change?
    [ ] The lowest point of the cable rises
    [ ] The cable shifts to the right
    [ ] The cable becomes flatter (wider parabola)
    [*] The cable becomes steeper (narrower parabola) while the lowest point stays the same
    Explanation: Changing a from 0.01 to 0.02 doubles the vertical stretch factor, making the parabola narrower (steeper). The vertex remains at (100, 5), so the lowest point does not change.

  Q30. A student graphs y = x² and then needs to graph y = −2(x + 3)² + 4. Which sequence of transformations should they apply?
    [ ] Reflect over y-axis, shift left 3, compress by 2, shift down 4
    [ ] Shift right 3, stretch by 2, reflect over x-axis, shift up 4
    [*] Shift left 3, stretch by 2, reflect over x-axis, shift up 4
    [ ] Shift left 3, compress by 1/2, shift up 4
    Explanation: From y = x², shift left 3 (x + 3), then vertically stretch by factor 2 and reflect over the x-axis (multiply by −2), then shift up 4 (+4). This gives y = −2(x + 3)² + 4 with vertex (−3, 4).

--- Lesson 2.2: Transformations of Quadratics (Flashcards) ---

  1. Q: g(x) = 2f(x). How does parabola transform?
     A: Vertical stretch by factor 2. Parabola opens faster, narrower.

  2. Q: g(x) = f(x) - 5. Shift how?
     A: Down 5 units. Subtract k shifts down by k.

  3. Q: g(x) = f(x+3). Shift how?
     A: Left 3 units. Add inside (x+h) shifts left by h.

  4. Q: g(x) = -f(x). What transformation?
     A: Reflect over x-axis. Negative coefficient flips parabola.

  5. Q: Transformation: f(x) = x², g(x) = (x-2)² + 3
     A: Right 2, up 3. Both vertex shift transformations.

  6. Q: Vertex of f(x) = -2(x+1)² - 4?
     A: (-1, -4). From vertex form a(x-h)²+k: h=-1 (so right -1=left 1).

  7. Q: Write parabola: vertex (-2, 1), opens down, stretch factor 3
     A: f(x) = -3(x+2)² + 1.

  8. Q: g(x) = 1/2·f(x). Effect?
     A: Vertical compression by 1/2. Parabola opens slower, wider.

  9. Q: g(x) = f(-x). What transformation?
     A: Reflect over y-axis. Replace x with -x.

  10. Q: Multiple transformations: f(x) = x², h(x) = -f(2x) + 3?
     A: Horizontal compression 1/2, reflect x-axis, up 3: h(x) = -4x² + 3.

--- Lesson 2.3: Completing the Square (Summary) ---

  Key Concepts: Completing the Square
Overview
This lesson covers the fundamental measures of center used to analyze and summarize data sets. You'll learn how to calculate and apply the mean, median, and mode, and understand when each is most appropriate.
Key Definitions
What is the vertex form of y = x² − 6x + 5?
Complete the square: x² − 6x + 9 − 9 + 5 = (x − 3)² − 4. The vertex is (3, −4).
What is the vertex of y = x² + 4x + 1?
Complete the square: x² + 4x + 4 − 4 + 1 = (x + 2)² − 3. The vertex is (−2, −3).
For 3x² + 18x + 10, what is the first step to complete the square?
When the leading coefficient is not 1, factor it out from the x² and x terms first: 3(x² + 6x) + 10. Then complete the square inside the parentheses.
What is 'completing the square'?
Completing the square is the process of adding a specific constant to x² + bx to form a perfect square trinomial (x + b/2)², which allows conversion to vertex form.
What is a 'perfect square trinomial'?
A perfect square trinomial has the form x² + 2ax + a² = (x + a)². It factors into the square of a single binomial.
What is the meaning of 'half the coefficient of x, then square it' in completing the square?
For x² + bx, taking (b/2)² gives the exact constant needed so that x² + bx + (b/2)² = (x + b/2)², which is a perfect square.
What is the relationship between completing the square and the quadratic formula?
The quadratic formula x = (−b ± sqrt(b² − 4ac))/(2a) is obtained by applying completing the square to the general quadratic ax² + bx + c = 0.
What is the 'square root property' used in completing the square?
The square root property states that if (expression)² = q, then expression = ±sqrt(q). The ± accounts for both the positive and negative roots.
A company finds that its profit (in thousands of dollars) is P(x) = −3x² + 36x − 80, where x is thousands of units produced. By completing the square, what is the maximum profit?
P(x) = −3(x² − 12x) − 80 = −3(x² − 12x + 36 − 36) − 80 = −3(x − 6)² + 108 − 80 = −3(x − 6)² + 28. The maximum profit is 28 thousand dollars = $28,000.

--- Lesson 2.3: Completing the Square (Quiz) ---

  Q1. To complete the square for x² + 10x, what value must you add?
    [ ] 10
    [*] 25
    [ ] 100
    [ ] 5
    Explanation: To complete the square for x² + bx, add (b/2)². Here b = 10, so (10/2)² = 5² = 25.

  Q2. What is the vertex form of y = x² − 6x + 5?
    [ ] y = (x − 3)² + 5
    [ ] y = (x + 3)² − 4
    [ ] y = (x − 6)² + 5
    [*] y = (x − 3)² − 4
    Explanation: Complete the square: x² − 6x + 9 − 9 + 5 = (x − 3)² − 4. The vertex is (3, −4).

  Q3. Solve x² + 8x = −7 by completing the square.
    [ ] x = 1 or x = 7
    [*] x = −1 or x = −7
    [ ] x = 0 or x = −8
    [ ] x = −4 or x = 4
    Explanation: Add 16 to both sides: x² + 8x + 16 = 9, so (x + 4)² = 9. Then x + 4 = ±3, giving x = −1 or x = −7.

  Q4. x² + 12x + 36 factors as which perfect square?
    [*] (x + 6)²
    [ ] (x − 6)²
    [ ] (x + 3)²
    [ ] (x + 12)²
    Explanation: x² + 12x + 36 = (x + 6)² because (12/2)² = 36 and the binomial has half the linear coefficient.

  Q5. Convert y = 2x² − 8x + 3 to vertex form.
    [ ] y = 2(x + 2)² + 3
    [ ] y = (x − 2)² − 5
    [*] y = 2(x − 2)² − 5
    [ ] y = 2(x − 4)² − 1
    Explanation: Factor out 2: y = 2(x² − 4x) + 3. Complete the square: 2(x² − 4x + 4 − 4) + 3 = 2(x − 2)² − 8 + 3 = 2(x − 2)² − 5.

  Q6. Solve (x − 5)² = 25.
    [ ] x = 5 only
    [*] x = 10 or x = 0
    [ ] x = 0 only
    [ ] x = 30 or x = −20
    Explanation: Take the square root of both sides: x − 5 = ±5. So x = 5 + 5 = 10 or x = 5 − 5 = 0.

  Q7. What is the vertex of y = x² + 4x + 1?
    [ ] (2, −3)
    [ ] (4, −3)
    [ ] (−4, 1)
    [*] (−2, −3)
    Explanation: Complete the square: x² + 4x + 4 − 4 + 1 = (x + 2)² − 3. The vertex is (−2, −3).

  Q8. To complete the square for x² − 14x, what value must you add?
    [ ] 14
    [ ] 7
    [*] 49
    [ ] 196
    Explanation: For x² + bx, add (b/2)². Here b = −14, so (−14/2)² = (−7)² = 49.

  Q9. Solve x² − 2x − 8 = 0 by completing the square.
    [*] x = 4 or x = −2
    [ ] x = 1 or x = −8
    [ ] x = −4 or x = 2
    [ ] x = 8 or x = −1
    Explanation: x² − 2x = 8. Add 1: (x − 1)² = 9. Then x − 1 = ±3, so x = 4 or x = −2.

  Q10. For 3x² + 18x + 10, what is the first step to complete the square?
    [ ] Take the square root of 3
    [*] Factor out 3 from the x-terms: 3(x² + 6x) + 10
    [ ] Divide everything by 10
    [ ] Add 9 to both sides
    Explanation: When the leading coefficient is not 1, factor it out from the x² and x terms first: 3(x² + 6x) + 10. Then complete the square inside the parentheses.

  Q11. What is 'completing the square'?
    [ ] A way to multiply two binomials
    [ ] A technique for graphing linear functions
    [*] A method for adding a constant to a quadratic expression to create a perfect square trinomial
    [ ] A method for finding the slope of a quadratic
    Explanation: Completing the square is the process of adding a specific constant to x² + bx to form a perfect square trinomial (x + b/2)², which allows conversion to vertex form.

  Q12. What is a 'perfect square trinomial'?
    [ ] A trinomial whose coefficients are all perfect squares
    [ ] Any trinomial with three terms
    [ ] A trinomial that equals zero
    [*] A trinomial that can be written as the square of a binomial, such as (x + a)²
    Explanation: A perfect square trinomial has the form x² + 2ax + a² = (x + a)². It factors into the square of a single binomial.

  Q13. What does 'vertex form' of a quadratic mean?
    [ ] The form y = a(x − r)(x − s)
    [ ] The form y = mx + b
    [*] The form y = a(x − h)² + k, where (h, k) is the vertex
    [ ] The form y = ax² + bx + c
    Explanation: Vertex form y = a(x − h)² + k directly reveals the vertex (h, k) and the direction/stretch of the parabola through the value of a.

  Q14. What does 'standard form' of a quadratic mean?
    [*] The form y = ax² + bx + c, where a, b, and c are constants and a is not zero
    [ ] The form y = a(x − r)(x − s) as typically measured in practice
    [ ] Any equation with x², particularly regarding what following
    [ ] The form y = a(x − h)² + k according to conventional analysis
    Explanation: Standard form y = ax² + bx + c is the expanded polynomial form. The y-intercept is c, and the vertex can be found using x = −b/(2a).

  Q15. What is the meaning of 'half the coefficient of x, then square it' in completing the square?
    [ ] It gives the value of the x-intercept
    [ ] It gives the vertex of the parabola directly
    [*] It is the formula (b/2)² that produces the constant needed to form a perfect square trinomial from x² + bx
    [ ] It is another name for the discriminant
    Explanation: For x² + bx, taking (b/2)² gives the exact constant needed so that x² + bx + (b/2)² = (x + b/2)², which is a perfect square.

  Q16. What does it mean to 'factor out the leading coefficient' before completing the square?
    [*] Factoring the leading coefficient from the x² and x terms so the coefficient of x² inside the parentheses becomes 1
    [ ] Dividing the entire equation by the leading coefficient
    [ ] Multiplying the equation by the leading coefficient
    [ ] Ignoring the leading coefficient
    Explanation: When a is not 1, factor a from the x² and x terms (e.g., 2x² + 8x becomes 2(x² + 4x)) so you can complete the square on x² + 4x where the leading coefficient is 1.

  Q17. What is the relationship between completing the square and the quadratic formula?
    [ ] They are unrelated methods
    [ ] The quadratic formula replaces completing the square entirely
    [ ] Completing the square can only be used when the quadratic formula fails
    [*] The quadratic formula is derived by completing the square on the general equation ax² + bx + c = 0
    Explanation: The quadratic formula x = (−b ± sqrt(b² − 4ac))/(2a) is obtained by applying completing the square to the general quadratic ax² + bx + c = 0.

  Q18. What does 'isolate the squared binomial' mean when solving by completing the square?
    [*] Move the constant term to the other side so the perfect square trinomial equals a number, then take the square root
    [ ] Graph the equation to find roots, particularly regarding mean based on established principles
    [ ] Set each factor equal to zero, particularly regarding binomial within the typical range of values
    [ ] Factor the equation completely, particularly regarding solving following the established framework
    Explanation: After forming the perfect square, arrange the equation as (x + p)² = q, then take the square root of both sides: x + p = ±sqrt(q), and solve for x.

  Q19. What is the 'square root property' used in completing the square?
    [ ] Square roots can only be positive
    [*] If (x + p)² = q, then x + p = ±sqrt(q), yielding two solutions
    [ ] If x² = a, then x = a/2
    [ ] If x² = a, then x = sqrt(a) only
    Explanation: The square root property states that if (expression)² = q, then expression = ±sqrt(q). The ± accounts for both the positive and negative roots.

  Q20. What does 'balance the equation' mean when completing the square?
    [ ] Setting both sides equal to zero, particularly regarding complete as observed in standard experiments
    [ ] Multiplying both sides by the same number when evaluated systematically
    [*] Adding the same value to both sides (or adding and subtracting on the same side) so the equation remains equivalent
    [ ] Graphing both sides to check they match under equilibrium conditions
    Explanation: When you add (b/2)² to complete the square, you must also add it to the other side (or subtract it on the same side) to keep the equation balanced and equivalent to the original.

  Q21. A gardener has a rectangular plot described by the area equation A = −x² + 12x, where x is the width in meters. By completing the square, find the width that maximizes the area.
    [*] 6 meters
    [ ] 8 meters
    [ ] 12 meters
    [ ] 4 meters
    Explanation: Complete the square: A = −(x² − 12x) = −(x² − 12x + 36 − 36) = −(x − 6)² + 36. The vertex is (6, 36), so the width that maximizes area is 6 meters.

  Q22. A toy rocket's height is h(t) = −16t² + 64t + 5 feet. By completing the square, find the maximum height the rocket reaches.
    [ ] 64 feet
    [ ] 53 feet
    [*] 69 feet
    [ ] 80 feet
    Explanation: h(t) = −16(t² − 4t) + 5 = −16(t² − 4t + 4 − 4) + 5 = −16(t − 2)² + 64 + 5 = −16(t − 2)² + 69. The maximum height is 69 feet at t = 2 seconds.

  Q23. A store's daily revenue is R(p) = −5p² + 200p − 1500 dollars, where p is the price per item. By completing the square, find the price that maximizes revenue.
    [*] $20
    [ ] $40
    [ ] $30
    [ ] $10
    Explanation: R(p) = −5(p² − 40p) − 1500 = −5(p² − 40p + 400 − 400) − 1500 = −5(p − 20)² + 2000 − 1500 = −5(p − 20)² + 500. Maximum revenue occurs at p = $20.

  Q24. A farmer wants to build a pen against a barn using 80 meters of fencing for three sides. The area is A = −2w² + 80w, where w is the width. What width maximizes the area?
    [*] 20 meters
    [ ] 40 meters
    [ ] 30 meters
    [ ] 10 meters
    Explanation: A = −2(w² − 40w) = −2(w² − 40w + 400 − 400) = −2(w − 20)² + 800. The vertex is (20, 800), so a width of 20 meters maximizes the area at 800 m².

  Q25. A basketball is shot and its height is h(t) = −16t² + 32t + 6 feet. By completing the square, determine after how many seconds the ball reaches its maximum height.
    [*] 1 second
    [ ] 0.5 seconds
    [ ] 2 seconds
    [ ] 1.5 seconds
    Explanation: h(t) = −16(t² − 2t) + 6 = −16(t² − 2t + 1 − 1) + 6 = −16(t − 1)² + 16 + 6 = −16(t − 1)² + 22. The maximum height of 22 feet occurs at t = 1 second.

  Q26. An engineer models the cross-section of a tunnel as y = −x² + 10x − 16 (in meters). By completing the square, find the maximum height of the tunnel.
    [ ] 10 meters
    [*] 9 meters
    [ ] 5 meters
    [ ] 16 meters
    Explanation: y = −(x² − 10x) − 16 = −(x² − 10x + 25 − 25) − 16 = −(x − 5)² + 25 − 16 = −(x − 5)² + 9. The maximum height is 9 meters at x = 5.

  Q27. A company finds that its profit (in thousands of dollars) is P(x) = −3x² + 36x − 80, where x is thousands of units produced. By completing the square, what is the maximum profit?
    [ ] $108,000
    [ ] $80,000
    [*] $28,000
    [ ] $36,000
    Explanation: P(x) = −3(x² − 12x) − 80 = −3(x² − 12x + 36 − 36) − 80 = −3(x − 6)² + 108 − 80 = −3(x − 6)² + 28. The maximum profit is 28 thousand dollars = $28,000.

  Q28. A diver's height above water is h(t) = −5t² + 10t + 15 meters. By completing the square, find the diver's maximum height above the water.
    [ ] 15 meters
    [ ] 10 meters
    [ ] 25 meters
    [*] 20 meters
    Explanation: h(t) = −5(t² − 2t) + 15 = −5(t² − 2t + 1 − 1) + 15 = −5(t − 1)² + 5 + 15 = −5(t − 1)² + 20. The maximum height is 20 meters at t = 1 second.

  Q29. A city park wants a rectangular play area with 60 meters of fencing. The area function is A(w) = w(30 − w) = −w² + 30w. Use completing the square to find the maximum area.
    [ ] 200 m²
    [ ] 900 m²
    [ ] 150 m²
    [*] 225 m²
    Explanation: A = −(w² − 30w) = −(w² − 30w + 225 − 225) = −(w − 15)² + 225. The maximum area is 225 m² when w = 15 meters (a 15 m by 15 m square).

  Q30. A student solves x² + 6x − 2 = 0 by completing the square and finds (x + 3)² = 11. What are the exact solutions?
    [*] x = −3 + sqrt(11) or x = −3 − sqrt(11)
    [ ] x = −6 + sqrt(11) or x = −6 − sqrt(11)
    [ ] x = sqrt(11) or x = −sqrt(11)
    [ ] x = 3 + sqrt(11) or x = 3 − sqrt(11)
    Explanation: From (x + 3)² = 11, take the square root: x + 3 = ±sqrt(11). Then x = −3 ± sqrt(11). The two solutions are x = −3 + sqrt(11) and x = −3 − sqrt(11).

--- Lesson 2.3: Completing the Square (Flashcards) ---

  1. Q: Complete the square: x² + 6x
     A: x² + 6x + 9 = (x+3)². Add (b/2)² = 9.

  2. Q: Complete the square: x² - 10x + ?
     A: x² - 10x + 25 = (x-5)². Add (-10/2)² = 25.

  3. Q: Find vertex of f(x) = x² + 4x - 7 by completing square
     A: (-2, -11). x² + 4x + 4 - 4 - 7 = (x+2)² - 11.

  4. Q: Vertex form of f(x) = 2x² - 8x + 3?
     A: f(x) = 2(x-2)² - 5. Factor: 2(x² - 4x) + 3 = 2(x² - 4x+4) - 8 + 3.

  5. Q: Complete square with leading coefficient: 3x² + 12x
     A: 3(x² + 4x) = 3(x² + 4x + 4 - 4) = 3(x+2)² - 12.

  6. Q: From x² + 8x = 9, complete square and solve
     A: (x+4)² = 25, so x = 1 or x = -9. x² + 8x + 16 = 9 + 16.

  7. Q: Vertex of f(x) = -x² + 6x - 2?
     A: (3, 7). -1(x² - 6x) - 2 = -(x-3)² + 9 - 2 = -(x-3)² + 7.

  8. Q: Write in vertex form: f(x) = x² - 2x
     A: f(x) = (x-1)² - 1.

  9. Q: Connection to vertex formula: x = -b/2a matches vertex form
     A: True. Completing square derives both equivalent methods.

  10. Q: Solve using completion: x² + 5x - 24 = 0
     A: x = 3 or x = -8. x² + 5x + 25/4 = 24 + 25/4 = 121/4, (x+5/2)² = (11/2)².

--- Lesson 2.4: Quadratic Formula & Discriminant (Summary) ---

  Key Concepts: Quadratic Formula & Discriminant
Overview
This lesson covers the fundamental measures of center used to analyze and summarize data sets. You'll learn how to calculate and apply the mean, median, and mode, and understand when each is most appropriate.
Key Definitions
What is the discriminant of 3x² − 4x + 1 = 0?
The discriminant is b² − 4ac = (−4)² − 4(3)(1) = 16 − 12 = 4.
What is the discriminant of x² + 4 = 0?
With a=1, b=0, c=4: discriminant = 0² − 4(1)(4) = −16. Since it is negative, there are no real solutions.
For x² − 6x + 9 = 0, what is the discriminant and the solution?
Discriminant = (−6)² − 4(1)(9) = 36 − 36 = 0. With discriminant = 0, x = 6/2 = 3 is the repeated root.
What is the sum of the roots of 2x² − 10x + 8 = 0?
By Vieta's formulas, the sum of roots = −b/a = −(−10)/2 = 5. (The roots are x = 1 and x = 4, and 1 + 4 = 5.)
What is the product of the roots of x² + 3x − 10 = 0?
By Vieta's formulas, the product of roots = c/a = −10/1 = −10. (The roots are x = 2 and x = −5, and 2 × (−5) = −10.)
What is the 'quadratic formula'?
The quadratic formula x = [−b ± sqrt(b² − 4ac)]/(2a) solves any quadratic equation ax² + bx + c = 0 where a is not zero.
What is the 'discriminant' of a quadratic equation?
The discriminant, denoted b² − 4ac, is the expression under the radical in the quadratic formula. Its sign determines the number and type of solutions.
A rectangular garden has an area of 60 m² and the length is 7 m more than the width. Using the quadratic formula on w² + 7w − 60 = 0, what is the width?
w = (−7 ± sqrt(49 + 240))/2 = (−7 ± sqrt(289))/2 = (−7 ± 17)/2. The positive solution is w = 10/2 = 5 meters. (Length = 12 m, and 5 × 12 = 60.)

--- Lesson 2.4: Quadratic Formula & Discriminant (Quiz) ---

  Q1. Solve x² − 5x + 6 = 0 using the quadratic formula.
    [*] x = 2 or x = 3
    [ ] x = −2 or x = −3
    [ ] x = 1 or x = 6
    [ ] x = −1 or x = −6
    Explanation: Using x = (−b ± sqrt(b² − 4ac))/(2a) with a=1, b=−5, c=6: x = (5 ± sqrt(25−24))/2 = (5 ± 1)/2, giving x = 3 or x = 2.

  Q2. What is the discriminant of 3x² − 4x + 1 = 0?
    [ ] −4
    [*] 4
    [ ] 0
    [ ] 28
    Explanation: The discriminant is b² − 4ac = (−4)² − 4(3)(1) = 16 − 12 = 4.

  Q3. If the discriminant of a quadratic equation equals 0, how many real solutions does it have?
    [ ] Two distinct real solutions
    [ ] No real solutions
    [*] Exactly one real (repeated) solution
    [ ] Infinitely many solutions
    Explanation: When the discriminant equals 0, the ± part of the formula gives ±0, so there is exactly one repeated real solution.

  Q4. What is the discriminant of x² + 4 = 0?
    [*] −16
    [ ] 16
    [ ] 0
    [ ] 4
    Explanation: With a=1, b=0, c=4: discriminant = 0² − 4(1)(4) = −16. Since it is negative, there are no real solutions.

  Q5. Solve 2x² + 5x − 3 = 0 using the quadratic formula.
    [ ] x = −1/2 or x = 3
    [*] x = 1/2 or x = −3
    [ ] x = 5/2 or x = −3/2
    [ ] x = 3 or x = −1
    Explanation: x = (−5 ± sqrt(25 + 24))/4 = (−5 ± sqrt(49))/4 = (−5 ± 7)/4. So x = 2/4 = 1/2 or x = −12/4 = −3.

  Q6. If the discriminant equals 49, what type of solutions does the equation have?
    [ ] One repeated solution
    [*] Two distinct real rational solutions
    [ ] Two complex solutions
    [ ] No solutions
    Explanation: Since 49 > 0, there are two distinct real solutions. Since sqrt(49) = 7 is rational, both solutions will be rational numbers.

  Q7. For x² − 6x + 9 = 0, what is the discriminant and the solution?
    [ ] Discriminant = −36; no real solution
    [ ] Discriminant = 9; x = 6
    [*] Discriminant = 0; x = 3 (repeated)
    [ ] Discriminant = 36; x = 3 or x = −3
    Explanation: Discriminant = (−6)² − 4(1)(9) = 36 − 36 = 0. With discriminant = 0, x = 6/2 = 3 is the repeated root.

  Q8. What is the sum of the roots of 2x² − 10x + 8 = 0?
    [*] 5
    [ ] 4
    [ ] −5
    [ ] 10
    Explanation: By Vieta's formulas, the sum of roots = −b/a = −(−10)/2 = 5. (The roots are x = 1 and x = 4, and 1 + 4 = 5.)

  Q9. What is the product of the roots of x² + 3x − 10 = 0?
    [ ] 10
    [ ] −3
    [*] −10
    [ ] 3
    Explanation: By Vieta's formulas, the product of roots = c/a = −10/1 = −10. (The roots are x = 2 and x = −5, and 2 × (−5) = −10.)

  Q10. If the discriminant of a quadratic is negative, the solutions are:
    [ ] One repeated real solution
    [ ] Undefined
    [ ] Two distinct real solutions
    [*] Two complex conjugate solutions (no real solutions)
    Explanation: A negative discriminant means you take the square root of a negative number, producing imaginary numbers. The two solutions are complex conjugates of the form a ± bi.

  Q11. What is the 'quadratic formula'?
    [ ] x = (b ± sqrt(b² + 4ac))/(2a), particularly regarding equation when considering all relevant factors
    [ ] x = −b/(2a), particularly regarding zero as observed in standard experiments
    [*] x = [−b ± sqrt(b² − 4ac)]/(2a), a formula that gives the solutions of any quadratic equation ax² + bx + c = 0
    [ ] x = c/(−b), particularly regarding where based on the prevailing evidence
    Explanation: The quadratic formula x = [−b ± sqrt(b² − 4ac)]/(2a) solves any quadratic equation ax² + bx + c = 0 where a is not zero.

  Q12. What is the 'discriminant' of a quadratic equation?
    [*] The expression b² − 4ac, found under the square root in the quadratic formula
    [ ] The value −b/(2a), particularly regarding determines
    [ ] The sum of the roots, particularly regarding discriminant
    [ ] The coefficient a in ax² + bx + c following conventional understanding
    Explanation: The discriminant, denoted b² − 4ac, is the expression under the radical in the quadratic formula. Its sign determines the number and type of solutions.

  Q13. What does 'two distinct real roots' mean?
    [ ] The equation has one solution that is counted twice
    [ ] The equation has no solutions
    [ ] The equation has imaginary solutions
    [*] The equation has exactly two different real number solutions (discriminant > 0)
    Explanation: Two distinct real roots means the parabola crosses the x-axis at two different points. This occurs when the discriminant is positive.

  Q14. What does 'repeated root' (or 'double root') mean?
    [ ] The equation must be factored twice
    [*] The equation has exactly one real solution where the parabola touches the x-axis at its vertex (discriminant = 0)
    [ ] The equation has no solutions
    [ ] The equation has two different solutions that happen to be equal
    Explanation: A repeated (double) root occurs when the discriminant is zero. The parabola is tangent to the x-axis, touching it at exactly one point — the vertex.

  Q15. What are 'Vieta's formulas' for a quadratic equation?
    [ ] Formulas for converting between standard and vertex form
    [ ] Formulas for finding the vertex of a parabola
    [ ] Another name for the quadratic formula
    [*] Formulas relating the sum and product of the roots to the coefficients: sum = −b/a and product = c/a
    Explanation: Vieta's formulas state that for ax² + bx + c = 0 with roots r and s: r + s = −b/a and r × s = c/a. They connect roots to coefficients without solving.

  Q16. What does 'complex conjugate roots' mean?
    [ ] Roots that are both zero
    [ ] Roots that cannot be calculated
    [*] Roots of the form a + bi and a − bi that occur when the discriminant is negative
    [ ] Two real roots that are negatives of each other
    Explanation: When the discriminant is negative, the square root produces an imaginary number, giving roots a + bi and a − bi. These are called complex conjugates.

  Q17. What does the ± symbol mean in the quadratic formula?
    [*] It indicates two computations: one using addition and one using subtraction, yielding two potential solutions
    [ ] The answer is always positive, particularly regarding means when measured under controlled conditions
    [ ] You choose either plus or minus, but not both in the context of this analysis
    [ ] It means approximately equal, particularly regarding separate when applying fundamental principles
    Explanation: The ± symbol means you perform two separate calculations: x = (−b + sqrt(discriminant))/(2a) for one root and x = (−b − sqrt(discriminant))/(2a) for the other.

  Q18. What does 'nature of the roots' mean in context of the discriminant?
    [ ] Whether the roots can be graphed, particularly regarding discriminant under equilibrium conditions
    [ ] Whether the roots are positive or negative based on established principles
    [ ] The size of the roots, particularly regarding type as observed in standard experiments
    [*] The classification of roots as real/complex, rational/irrational, and distinct/repeated based on the discriminant's value
    Explanation: The 'nature of the roots' describes their type: the discriminant reveals whether roots are real or complex, rational or irrational, and distinct or repeated.

  Q19. What does 'rational root' mean?
    [ ] A root that is always a whole number
    [*] A root that can be expressed as a fraction of two integers (p/q)
    [ ] A root that is always positive
    [ ] A root that involves a square root
    Explanation: A rational root is a solution that can be written as a ratio of integers. This occurs when the discriminant is a perfect square, making sqrt(discriminant) a rational number.

  Q20. What does 'irrational root' mean?
    [ ] A root that equals zero, particularly regarding discriminant in the
    [ ] A root that is imaginary, particularly regarding discriminant as observed
    [ ] A root that is negative, particularly regarding root as determined by
    [*] A root that cannot be expressed as a simple fraction and involves a non-perfect square root
    Explanation: An irrational root contains a square root of a non-perfect square (like sqrt(5)). This occurs when the discriminant is positive but not a perfect square.

  Q21. A ball is thrown upward from a 10-foot platform with an initial velocity of 40 ft/s. Its height is h(t) = −16t² + 40t + 10. Using the quadratic formula, when does the ball hit the ground?
    [ ] Approximately 1.25 seconds
    [*] Approximately 2.73 seconds
    [ ] Exactly 2 seconds
    [ ] Exactly 3 seconds
    Explanation: Set h(t) = 0: −16t² + 40t + 10 = 0. Using the quadratic formula: t = (−40 ± sqrt(1600 + 640))/(−32) = (−40 ± sqrt(2240))/(−32). The positive solution is approximately 2.73 seconds.

  Q22. An architect designs a parabolic arch. The equation x² − 8x + k = 0 represents where the arch meets the ground. For the arch to touch the ground at exactly one point, what must k equal?
    [ ] 8
    [ ] 4
    [*] 16
    [ ] 64
    Explanation: For exactly one solution, the discriminant must equal 0: b² − 4ac = (−8)² − 4(1)(k) = 64 − 4k = 0, so k = 16.

  Q23. A company's profit is P(x) = −2x² + 28x − 90 dollars, where x is the price in dollars. Use the discriminant to determine if there are real break-even prices.
    [ ] Yes, the discriminant is 0 so there is exactly one break-even price
    [ ] Cannot be determined
    [*] Yes, the discriminant is 64 so there are two break-even prices
    [ ] No, the discriminant is negative so there are no break-even prices
    Explanation: Set P(x) = 0: −2x² + 28x − 90 = 0. Discriminant = 28² − 4(−2)(−90) = 784 − 720 = 64. Since 64 > 0, there are two real break-even prices.

  Q24. A firework is launched with height h(t) = −5t² + 30t + 2 meters. Using the quadratic formula, at what time does it reach the ground? (Round to nearest tenth.)
    [ ] Exactly 6 seconds
    [ ] Approximately 5.5 seconds
    [*] Approximately 6.1 seconds
    [ ] Approximately 3 seconds
    Explanation: Set h(t) = 0: −5t² + 30t + 2 = 0. t = (−30 ± sqrt(900 + 40))/(−10) = (−30 ± sqrt(940))/(−10). The positive root is approximately 6.1 seconds.

  Q25. A rectangular garden has an area of 60 m² and the length is 7 m more than the width. Using the quadratic formula on w² + 7w − 60 = 0, what is the width?
    [*] 5 meters
    [ ] 10 meters
    [ ] 12 meters
    [ ] 3 meters
    Explanation: w = (−7 ± sqrt(49 + 240))/2 = (−7 ± sqrt(289))/2 = (−7 ± 17)/2. The positive solution is w = 10/2 = 5 meters. (Length = 12 m, and 5 × 12 = 60.)

  Q26. A physics student models a projectile with h(t) = −4.9t² + 20t. She uses the discriminant to determine if the projectile ever reaches 25 meters. Does it?
    [*] No, the discriminant is negative (−90) so it never reaches 25 meters
    [ ] Yes, the discriminant is positive so it reaches 25 meters at two times
    [ ] Yes, it reaches exactly 25 meters once
    [ ] Cannot be determined from the discriminant
    Explanation: Set h(t) = 25: −4.9t² + 20t − 25 = 0. Discriminant = 400 − 4(4.9)(25) = 400 − 490 = −90. Since the discriminant is negative, the projectile never reaches 25 meters.

  Q27. A business finds that its revenue equals its cost when 3x² − 12x + 9 = 0. Using the quadratic formula, at what production levels does the business break even?
    [*] x = 1 and x = 3
    [ ] x = 4 and x = 6
    [ ] x = 2 only
    [ ] x = 3 and x = 9
    Explanation: Discriminant = 144 − 108 = 36. x = (12 ± 6)/6, giving x = 18/6 = 3 or x = 6/6 = 1. The business breaks even at x = 1 and x = 3.

  Q28. A farmer throws a bale of hay upward from a 4-foot trailer bed with initial velocity 24 ft/s. Its height is h(t) = −16t² + 24t + 4. When does it reach exactly 10 feet?
    [ ] At t = 0.25 seconds and t = 1.5 seconds
    [ ] It never reaches 10 feet
    [ ] At t = 0.5 seconds and t = 1 second
    [*] At t = 0.5 seconds and t = 0.75 seconds
    Explanation: Set h = 10: −16t² + 24t + 4 = 10, so −16t² + 24t − 6 = 0, or 8t² − 12t + 3 = 0. t = (12 ± sqrt(144−96))/16 = (12 ± sqrt(48))/16. This gives t ≈ 0.5 and t ≈ 0.75 seconds.

  Q29. An engineer needs the equation 2x² − kx + 8 = 0 to have no real solutions for safety reasons. What values of k ensure this?
    [ ] k = 8 or k = −8
    [ ] k > 8
    [ ] k < −8
    [*] −8 < k < 8
    Explanation: For no real solutions: discriminant < 0. k² − 4(2)(8) < 0, so k² − 64 < 0, meaning k² < 64. Thus −8 < k < 8.

  Q30. A cliff diver jumps from a 45-meter cliff with initial upward velocity of 3 m/s. The height is h(t) = −4.9t² + 3t + 45. Using the quadratic formula, how long until the diver reaches the water?
    [ ] Approximately 2.0 seconds
    [ ] Exactly 3 seconds
    [ ] Approximately 4.5 seconds
    [*] Approximately 3.4 seconds
    Explanation: Set h(t) = 0: −4.9t² + 3t + 45 = 0. t = (−3 ± sqrt(9 + 882))/(−9.8) = (−3 ± sqrt(891))/(−9.8). The positive solution gives t ≈ 3.4 seconds.

--- Lesson 2.4: Quadratic Formula & Discriminant (Flashcards) ---

  1. Q: Solve using quadratic formula: x² - 5x + 6 = 0
     A: x = 2 or x = 3. x = (5 ± √(25-24))/2 = (5 ± 1)/2.

  2. Q: Discriminant of 2x² - 3x - 5 = 0?
     A: 49. b² - 4ac = 9 - 4(2)(-5) = 9 + 40 = 49.

  3. Q: What does discriminant = 0 mean?
     A: One repeated root (tangent line at x-axis). Perfect square.

  4. Q: Discriminant < 0 implies?
     A: No real solutions. Complex roots only.

  5. Q: Solve 3x² + x - 1 = 0
     A: x = 1/3 or x = -1. x = (-1 ± √(1+12))/6 = (-1 ± √13)/6... check: (3x-1)(x+1)=0.

  6. Q: How many real solutions: x² + 2x + 5 = 0?
     A: None. Discriminant = 4 - 20 = -16 < 0.

  7. Q: If roots are r and s, sum r + s = ?
     A: -b/a. Vieta's formulas: sum = -b/a, product = c/a.

  8. Q: Find zeros of f(x) = x² - 7x + 12
     A: 3 and 4. By formula or factoring (x-3)(x-4).

  9. Q: Write quadratic with roots 2 and 5
     A: f(x) = (x-2)(x-5) = x² - 7x + 10.

  10. Q: Solve: (2x-1)² = 9
     A: x = 2 or x = -1. 2x - 1 = ±3.

--- Lesson 2.5: Graphing Quadratic Functions (Summary) ---

  Key Concepts: Graphing Quadratic Functions
Overview
This lesson covers the fundamental measures of center used to analyze and summarize data sets. You'll learn how to calculate and apply the mean, median, and mode, and understand when each is most appropriate.
Key Definitions
What is the vertex of y = x² − 8x + 12?
The x-coordinate of the vertex is x = −b/(2a) = 8/2 = 4. Substituting: y = 16 − 32 + 12 = −4. The vertex is (4, −4).
What is the axis of symmetry of y = 3x² + 12x + 5?
The axis of symmetry is x = −b/(2a) = −12/(2 × 3) = −12/6 = −2.
What is the y-intercept of y = 2x² − 5x + 7?
The y-intercept is found by setting x = 0: y = 0 − 0 + 7 = 7. The point is (0, 7).
What is the range of y = 2(x − 1)² − 8?
Since a = 2 > 0, the parabola opens upward with minimum at the vertex (1, −8). The range is all y-values greater than or equal to −8.
What is the end behavior of y = −3x² + 6x + 1?
Since a = −3 < 0, the parabola opens downward. Both ends of the graph go toward negative infinity as x moves toward ±∞.
If a parabola has vertex (3, 5) and a = 1, what is the y-value of the point symmetric to (1, 9)?
The point (1, 9) is 2 units left of the axis x = 3. By symmetry, the mirror point is 2 units right at x = 5. Since both are equidistant, they share the same y-value of 9. The symmetric point is (5, 9).
What is the 'vertex' of a parabola?
The vertex is the turning point of the parabola. For an upward-opening parabola it is the minimum point; for a downward-opening parabola it is the maximum point.
What is the 'axis of symmetry' of a parabola?
The axis of symmetry is the vertical line x = −b/(2a) passing through the vertex. Each point on the parabola has a mirror image across this line.
A baseball is hit and follows the path h(t) = −16t² + 64t + 3, where h is height in feet and t is time in seconds. What is the maximum height the ball reaches?
The vertex t-coordinate is t = −64/(2(−16)) = 2 seconds. h(2) = −16(4) + 64(2) + 3 = −64 + 128 + 3 = 67 feet.
A fountain shoots water in a parabolic arc described by y = −0.5x² + 4x, where x and y are in feet. What is the maximum height of the water and how far from the base does it land?
Vertex x = −4/(2(−0.5)) = 4. y(4) = −0.5(16) + 16 = 8 feet max height. The zeros: −0.5x² + 4x = 0 gives x(−0.5x + 4) = 0, so x = 0 or x = 8. The water lands 8 feet from the base.
A bridge has a parabolic arch modeled by y = −0.01x² + 2x, where y is the height in meters and x is the horizontal distance. What is the maximum height of the arch and how wide is the bridge at its base?
Vertex x = −2/(2(−0.01)) = 100. y(100) = −0.01(10000) + 200 = 100 meters. Zeros: −0.01x² + 2x = 0 gives x = 0 or x = 200. The bridge is 200 meters wide.
A cell phone company models monthly revenue as R(p) = −200p² + 8000p, where p is the price per phone plan. What price maximizes revenue, and what is the maximum revenue?
Vertex p = −8000/(2(−200)) = 20. R(20) = −200(400) + 8000(20) = −80,000 + 160,000 = $80,000.
A ski jump ramp is modeled by y = 0.25x² − 4x + 20, where y is the height in meters. What is the lowest point of the ramp and at what horizontal distance does it occur?
Vertex x = −(−4)/(2(0.25)) = 4/0.5 = 8. y(8) = 0.25(64) − 32 + 20 = 16 − 32 + 20 = 4 meters. The lowest point is 4 meters high at a horizontal distance of 8 meters.

--- Lesson 2.5: Graphing Quadratic Functions (Quiz) ---

  Q1. What is the vertex of y = x² − 8x + 12?
    [*] (4, −4)
    [ ] (2, 6)
    [ ] (8, 12)
    [ ] (−4, 4)
    Explanation: The x-coordinate of the vertex is x = −b/(2a) = 8/2 = 4. Substituting: y = 16 − 32 + 12 = −4. The vertex is (4, −4).

  Q2. What is the axis of symmetry of y = 3x² + 12x + 5?
    [ ] x = 12
    [ ] x = 2
    [ ] x = −4
    [*] x = −2
    Explanation: The axis of symmetry is x = −b/(2a) = −12/(2 × 3) = −12/6 = −2.

  Q3. What is the y-intercept of y = 2x² − 5x + 7?
    [ ] (0, 2)
    [ ] (0, −5)
    [ ] (7, 0)
    [*] (0, 7)
    Explanation: The y-intercept is found by setting x = 0: y = 0 − 0 + 7 = 7. The point is (0, 7).

  Q4. What are the x-intercepts of y = x² − 5x + 6?
    [*] x = 2 and x = 3
    [ ] x = −2 and x = −3
    [ ] x = 1 and x = 6
    [ ] x = 5 and x = 6
    Explanation: Set y = 0: x² − 5x + 6 = 0 factors as (x − 2)(x − 3) = 0, giving x = 2 and x = 3.

  Q5. Does y = −x² + 4x − 1 open upward or downward, and does it have a maximum or minimum?
    [ ] Opens upward; has a minimum
    [ ] Opens upward; has a maximum
    [*] Opens downward; has a maximum
    [ ] Opens downward; has a minimum
    Explanation: Since a = −1 < 0, the parabola opens downward. A downward-opening parabola has a maximum value at its vertex.

  Q6. What is the range of y = 2(x − 1)² − 8?
    [ ] y ≥ 1
    [*] y ≥ −8
    [ ] y ≤ −8
    [ ] All real numbers
    Explanation: Since a = 2 > 0, the parabola opens upward with minimum at the vertex (1, −8). The range is all y-values greater than or equal to −8.

  Q7. For y = x² − 4x, on what interval is the function decreasing?
    [ ] (−∞, −4)
    [ ] (2, ∞)
    [*] (−∞, 2)
    [ ] (−∞, 0)
    Explanation: The vertex is at x = −(−4)/(2×1) = 2. Since a > 0, the parabola decreases to the left of the vertex: the function is decreasing on (−∞, 2).

  Q8. What is the end behavior of y = −3x² + 6x + 1?
    [ ] As x → +∞, y → +∞ and as x → −∞, y → −∞
    [ ] As x → ±∞, y → 0
    [ ] As x → ±∞, y → +∞
    [*] As x → ±∞, y → −∞
    Explanation: Since a = −3 < 0, the parabola opens downward. Both ends of the graph go toward negative infinity as x moves toward ±∞.

  Q9. If a parabola has vertex (3, 5) and a = 1, what is the y-value of the point symmetric to (1, 9)?
    [*] 9
    [ ] 5
    [ ] 13
    [ ] 3
    Explanation: The point (1, 9) is 2 units left of the axis x = 3. By symmetry, the mirror point is 2 units right at x = 5. Since both are equidistant, they share the same y-value of 9. The symmetric point is (5, 9).

  Q10. The domain of any quadratic function y = ax² + bx + c is:
    [ ] x ≥ vertex x-coordinate
    [*] All real numbers
    [ ] x ≥ 0
    [ ] Depends on the value of a
    Explanation: A quadratic function is defined for all real numbers. You can substitute any real number for x and get a real output, so the domain is always all real numbers.

  Q11. What is the 'vertex' of a parabola?
    [ ] Any point on the parabola, particularly regarding maximum when evaluated systematically
    [ ] The point where the parabola crosses the x-axis in most standard conditions
    [*] The highest or lowest point of the parabola, where it changes from decreasing to increasing (or vice versa)
    [ ] The y-intercept of the parabola, particularly regarding upward based on established principles
    Explanation: The vertex is the turning point of the parabola. For an upward-opening parabola it is the minimum point; for a downward-opening parabola it is the maximum point.

  Q12. What is the 'axis of symmetry' of a parabola?
    [*] A vertical line through the vertex (x = −b/(2a)) that divides the parabola into two mirror-image halves
    [ ] A horizontal line through the vertex following conventional understanding
    [ ] The line connecting the x-intercepts when applying fundamental principles
    [ ] The x-axis, particularly regarding passing according to conventional analysis
    Explanation: The axis of symmetry is the vertical line x = −b/(2a) passing through the vertex. Each point on the parabola has a mirror image across this line.

  Q13. What does 'x-intercept' (or 'zero') of a quadratic function mean?
    [*] The x-value(s) where the parabola crosses the x-axis, found by setting y = 0
    [ ] The vertex of the parabola
    [ ] The value of y when x = 0
    [ ] The maximum value of the function
    Explanation: An x-intercept (also called a zero or root) is a point where the graph meets the x-axis, meaning y = 0. A quadratic can have 0, 1, or 2 x-intercepts.

  Q14. What does 'y-intercept' mean for a quadratic function?
    [ ] The vertex of the parabola, particularly regarding what when evaluated systematically
    [ ] The axis of symmetry, particularly regarding what under the given assumptions
    [*] The point where the graph crosses the y-axis, found by setting x = 0 (equals the constant c)
    [ ] The maximum or minimum value when evaluated systematically
    Explanation: The y-intercept is the point where the graph crosses the y-axis. For y = ax² + bx + c, setting x = 0 gives y = c, so the y-intercept is (0, c).

  Q15. What does 'domain' of a function mean?
    [ ] The region where the graph is increasing
    [ ] The set of all possible output values (y-values)
    [ ] The vertex of the graph
    [*] The set of all possible input values (x-values) for which the function is defined
    Explanation: The domain is the set of all valid input (x) values. For quadratic functions, the domain is always all real numbers because any x can be squared.

  Q16. What does 'range' of a quadratic function mean?
    [ ] The set of all x-values
    [ ] The width of the parabola
    [ ] The distance between the x-intercepts
    [*] The set of all possible output values (y-values) the function can produce
    Explanation: The range is the set of all possible y-values. For an upward-opening parabola with vertex (h, k), the range is y ≥ k. For downward-opening, the range is y ≤ k.

  Q17. What does 'end behavior' of a quadratic function mean?
    [ ] Where the graph ends on the x-axis
    [ ] What happens to y as x approaches the vertex
    [*] The behavior of the graph as x approaches positive or negative infinity
    [ ] The y-intercept of the function
    Explanation: End behavior describes what happens to y-values as x gets very large (positive or negative). For quadratics, if a > 0 both ends go to +∞; if a < 0 both ends go to −∞.

  Q18. What does 'increasing' mean for a function on an interval?
    [ ] The function has a positive leading coefficient
    [ ] The function has a positive y-intercept
    [ ] The function's graph is above the x-axis
    [*] The function's output (y-value) gets larger as the input (x-value) increases on that interval
    Explanation: A function is increasing on an interval when larger x-values produce larger y-values. For an upward parabola, the function increases to the right of the vertex.

  Q19. What does 'decreasing' mean for a function on an interval?
    [ ] The function is undefined
    [ ] The function has a negative leading coefficient
    [*] The function's output (y-value) gets smaller as the input (x-value) increases on that interval
    [ ] The function's graph is below the x-axis
    Explanation: A function is decreasing on an interval when larger x-values produce smaller y-values. For an upward parabola, the function decreases to the left of the vertex.

  Q20. What does 'symmetry' mean in the context of graphing a parabola?
    [ ] The parabola is the same shape as a circle
    [ ] The parabola has equal x-intercepts
    [*] Every point on one side of the axis of symmetry has a corresponding mirror point on the other side at the same distance
    [ ] The parabola crosses the x-axis at equal intervals
    Explanation: A parabola is symmetric about its axis of symmetry. For any point (x, y) on the parabola, there is a mirror point on the opposite side of the axis at the same height.

  Q21. A baseball is hit and follows the path h(t) = −16t² + 64t + 3, where h is height in feet and t is time in seconds. What is the maximum height the ball reaches?
    [ ] 80 feet
    [ ] 64 feet
    [ ] 48 feet
    [*] 67 feet
    Explanation: The vertex t-coordinate is t = −64/(2(−16)) = 2 seconds. h(2) = −16(4) + 64(2) + 3 = −64 + 128 + 3 = 67 feet.

  Q22. A company's daily profit is P(x) = −x² + 40x − 300 dollars, where x is the number of items sold. By graphing, determine the range of items that must be sold to make a profit (P > 0).
    [ ] Exactly 20 items
    [ ] Between 0 and 20 items
    [*] Between 10 and 30 items
    [ ] More than 40 items
    Explanation: Set P(x) = 0: −x² + 40x − 300 = 0, or x² − 40x + 300 = 0. Factoring: (x − 10)(x − 30) = 0, so x = 10 and x = 30. The profit is positive between the zeros: 10 < x < 30.

  Q23. A fountain shoots water in a parabolic arc described by y = −0.5x² + 4x, where x and y are in feet. What is the maximum height of the water and how far from the base does it land?
    [ ] Maximum height 8 feet; lands 16 feet away
    [ ] Maximum height 4 feet; lands 4 feet away
    [ ] Maximum height 16 feet; lands 8 feet away
    [*] Maximum height 8 feet; lands 8 feet away
    Explanation: Vertex x = −4/(2(−0.5)) = 4. y(4) = −0.5(16) + 16 = 8 feet max height. The zeros: −0.5x² + 4x = 0 gives x(−0.5x + 4) = 0, so x = 0 or x = 8. The water lands 8 feet from the base.

  Q24. A physics student launches a model rocket with height h(t) = −5t² + 30t meters. She wants to graph the rocket's path. What are the key features: vertex and time when it hits the ground?
    [ ] Vertex (6, 30); hits ground at t = 3 seconds
    [ ] Vertex (5, 25); hits ground at t = 10 seconds
    [*] Vertex (3, 45); hits ground at t = 6 seconds
    [ ] Vertex (3, 30); hits ground at t = 5 seconds
    Explanation: Vertex t = −30/(2(−5)) = 3. h(3) = −45 + 90 = 45 meters. Zeros: −5t² + 30t = 0 gives t(−5t + 30) = 0, so t = 0 or t = 6 seconds.

  Q25. A theater charges $20 per ticket and sells 300 tickets. For each $1 increase, 10 fewer tickets are sold. Revenue is R(x) = (20 + x)(300 − 10x). After expanding, what price maximizes revenue?
    [ ] $20
    [*] $25
    [ ] $30
    [ ] $35
    Explanation: R(x) = −10x² + 100x + 6000. Vertex x = −100/(2(−10)) = 5. The optimal price is 20 + 5 = $25 per ticket.

  Q26. A bridge has a parabolic arch modeled by y = −0.01x² + 2x, where y is the height in meters and x is the horizontal distance. What is the maximum height of the arch and how wide is the bridge at its base?
    [ ] 50 meters high; 200 meters wide
    [ ] 100 meters high; 100 meters wide
    [*] 100 meters high; 200 meters wide
    [ ] 200 meters high; 100 meters wide
    Explanation: Vertex x = −2/(2(−0.01)) = 100. y(100) = −0.01(10000) + 200 = 100 meters. Zeros: −0.01x² + 2x = 0 gives x = 0 or x = 200. The bridge is 200 meters wide.

  Q27. An athlete throws a javelin whose path is h(d) = −0.02d² + 1.2d + 2, where h is height and d is horizontal distance in meters. Over what horizontal distance is the javelin above 10 meters?
    [ ] Between d = 10 m and d = 50 m
    [*] Between d = 10 m and d = 40 m
    [ ] Between d = 8 m and d = 52 m
    [ ] Never above 10 meters
    Explanation: Set h = 10: −0.02d² + 1.2d + 2 = 10, so −0.02d² + 1.2d − 8 = 0, or d² − 60d + 400 = 0. Factoring: (d − 10)(d − 40) = 0. The javelin is above 10 m between d = 10 and d = 40 meters.

  Q28. A cell phone company models monthly revenue as R(p) = −200p² + 8000p, where p is the price per phone plan. What price maximizes revenue, and what is the maximum revenue?
    [ ] $10; maximum revenue $60,000
    [ ] $40; maximum revenue $160,000
    [ ] $20; maximum revenue $40,000
    [*] $20; maximum revenue $80,000
    Explanation: Vertex p = −8000/(2(−200)) = 20. R(20) = −200(400) + 8000(20) = −80,000 + 160,000 = $80,000.

  Q29. A gardener plots the growth rate of a plant as G(t) = −2t² + 20t − 32 cm per week, where t is weeks after planting. During which weeks is the growth rate positive?
    [ ] Weeks 4 through 6
    [ ] Only at week 5
    [*] Weeks 2 through 8
    [ ] Weeks 0 through 10
    Explanation: Set G(t) = 0: −2t² + 20t − 32 = 0, or t² − 10t + 16 = 0. Factoring: (t − 2)(t − 8) = 0. Growth rate is positive between the roots: weeks 2 < t < 8.

  Q30. A ski jump ramp is modeled by y = 0.25x² − 4x + 20, where y is the height in meters. What is the lowest point of the ramp and at what horizontal distance does it occur?
    [ ] Lowest point at 8 meters high, at x = 4 meters
    [ ] Lowest point at 20 meters high, at x = 0 meters
    [ ] Lowest point at 0 meters high, at x = 10 meters
    [*] Lowest point at 4 meters high, at x = 8 meters
    Explanation: Vertex x = −(−4)/(2(0.25)) = 4/0.5 = 8. y(8) = 0.25(64) − 32 + 20 = 16 − 32 + 20 = 4 meters. The lowest point is 4 meters high at a horizontal distance of 8 meters.

--- Lesson 2.5: Graphing Quadratic Functions (Flashcards) ---

  1. Q: Find zeros, vertex, domain, range of f(x) = x² - 6x + 5
     A: Zeros: 1, 5. Vertex: (3, -4). Domain: ℝ. Range: [-4, ∞).

  2. Q: Graph f(x) = -(x-2)² + 3. Key features?
     A: Vertex (2, 3), opens down, y-intercept f(0)=-1, zeros: x = 2±√3.

  3. Q: Find y-intercept of f(x) = 2(x-3)² - 5
     A: f(0) = 2(9) - 5 = 13. Point: (0, 13).

  4. Q: Zeros of f(x) = x² + 4x + 5?
     A: None (real). Discriminant = 16 - 20 = -4 < 0.

  5. Q: Increasing/decreasing: f(x) = -2(x+1)² + 4?
     A: Increasing on (-∞, -1], decreasing on [-1, ∞). Opens down, max at x=-1.

  6. Q: X-intercepts of f(x) = 2x² - 8x = 0?
     A: x = 0 and x = 4. Factor: 2x(x - 4) = 0.

  7. Q: Write f(x) with zeros 2 and -3, passes (1, -12)
     A: f(x) = -3(x-2)(x+3). Use f(1) = -3(-1)(4) = 12... check: f(1)=-3(1-2)(1+3)=-3(-1)(4)=12. Need a=-12/(-1*4)=-3... or scale differently.

  8. Q: Axis of symmetry = x-coordinate of what?
     A: Vertex. Line x = h where vertex is (h, k).

  9. Q: Range of f(x) = -3x² + 6x + 1?
     A: (-∞, 4]. Vertex x = 1, f(1) = 4 max, opens down.

  10. Q: Standard form f(x) = (x+2)(x-4)?
     A: f(x) = x² - 2x - 8.

--- Lesson 2.6: Applications of Quadratics (Summary) ---

  Key Concepts: Applications of Quadratics
Overview
This lesson covers the fundamental measures of center used to analyze and summarize data sets. You'll learn how to calculate and apply the mean, median, and mode, and understand when each is most appropriate.
Key Definitions
A ball is thrown upward with h(t) = −16t² + 48t + 5. What is the maximum height?
Maximum at t = −48/(2(−16)) = 1.5 seconds. h(1.5) = −16(2.25) + 48(1.5) + 5 = −36 + 72 + 5 = 41 feet.
Two numbers sum to 30. What is their maximum product?
Let the numbers be x and 30 − x. Product P = x(30 − x) = −x² + 30x. Maximum at x = 15, giving P = 15 × 15 = 225.
The profit function is P = R − C. If R(x) = 80x and C(x) = x² + 20x + 100, what is the maximum profit?
P(x) = 80x − x² − 20x − 100 = −x² + 60x − 100. Vertex at x = 30. P(30) = −900 + 1800 − 100 = $800.
If h(t) = −4.9t² + 19.6t, what is the maximum height in meters?
Vertex at t = −19.6/(2(−4.9)) = 2 seconds. h(2) = −4.9(4) + 19.6(2) = −19.6 + 39.2 = 19.6 meters.
What is 'optimization' in the context of quadratic applications?
Optimization means finding the best (maximum or minimum) value. For quadratics, this is the y-coordinate of the vertex, found using x = −b/(2a).
What is a 'revenue function'?
A revenue function represents total income: R(x) = (price per item) × (number of items sold). When price depends on quantity, R(x) becomes a quadratic.
A water park designs a fountain with water height h(t) = −16t² + 80t feet, where t is time in seconds. How long is the water in the air, and what is the maximum height?
Time in air: −16t² + 80t = 0 gives t(−16t + 80) = 0, so t = 0 or t = 5 seconds. Max height at t = 2.5: h(2.5) = −16(6.25) + 200 = −100 + 200 = 100 feet.
A company finds that selling x widgets at price p = 50 − 0.5x gives revenue R(x) = x(50 − 0.5x). How many widgets maximize revenue, and what is the maximum revenue?
R(x) = −0.5x² + 50x. Vertex x = −50/(2(−0.5)) = 50. R(50) = −0.5(2500) + 2500 = −1250 + 2500 = $1,250.
A landscaper has 200 feet of edging to border three sides of a rectangular flower bed (the fourth side is against a house). What is the maximum area of the bed?
Let w = width (two sides). Then l = 200 − 2w. A = w(200 − 2w) = −2w² + 200w. Vertex at w = 50, giving A = 50 × 100 = 5,000 sq ft.
A cannon fires a cannonball from a 20-meter cliff with initial velocity 30 m/s. Height is h(t) = −5t² + 30t + 20. What is the maximum height above the ground?
Vertex at t = −30/(2(−5)) = 3. h(3) = −5(9) + 30(3) + 20 = −45 + 90 + 20 = 65 meters.
Real-World Applications
Example: A parking lot charges $10 per car and averages 200 cars per day. For each $1 increase, 10 fewer cars come. Revenue is R(x) = (10 + x)(200 − 10x). What price increase maximizes revenue?
R(x) = −10x² + 100x + 2000. Vertex at x = −100/(2(−10)) = 5. A $5 increase (charging $15) maximizes revenue at R(5) = $2,250.

--- Lesson 2.6: Applications of Quadratics (Quiz) ---

  Q1. A ball is thrown upward with h(t) = −16t² + 48t + 5. What is the maximum height?
    [ ] 36 feet
    [*] 41 feet
    [ ] 53 feet
    [ ] 48 feet
    Explanation: Maximum at t = −48/(2(−16)) = 1.5 seconds. h(1.5) = −16(2.25) + 48(1.5) + 5 = −36 + 72 + 5 = 41 feet.

  Q2. If revenue is R(x) = −3x² + 120x, what value of x maximizes revenue?
    [ ] 10
    [*] 20
    [ ] 40
    [ ] 60
    Explanation: The vertex is at x = −120/(2(−3)) = 120/6 = 20. Maximum revenue occurs when x = 20.

  Q3. A rectangle has perimeter 48 units. What dimensions give maximum area?
    [*] 12 × 12 (a square)
    [ ] 6 × 18
    [ ] 8 × 16
    [ ] 10 × 14
    Explanation: With perimeter 48, l + w = 24. Area A = w(24 − w) = −w² + 24w. Vertex at w = 12, so the maximum area is 12 × 12 = 144 square units.

  Q4. A projectile has h(t) = −16t² + 96t. When does it hit the ground?
    [*] t = 6 seconds
    [ ] t = 3 seconds
    [ ] t = 12 seconds
    [ ] t = 8 seconds
    Explanation: Set h(t) = 0: −16t² + 96t = 0, so −16t(t − 6) = 0. The solutions are t = 0 (launch) and t = 6 (landing).

  Q5. Two numbers sum to 30. What is their maximum product?
    [ ] 180
    [*] 225
    [ ] 200
    [ ] 250
    Explanation: Let the numbers be x and 30 − x. Product P = x(30 − x) = −x² + 30x. Maximum at x = 15, giving P = 15 × 15 = 225.

  Q6. The profit function is P = R − C. If R(x) = 80x and C(x) = x² + 20x + 100, what is the maximum profit?
    [ ] $900
    [ ] $1000
    [*] $800
    [ ] $600
    Explanation: P(x) = 80x − x² − 20x − 100 = −x² + 60x − 100. Vertex at x = 30. P(30) = −900 + 1800 − 100 = $800.

  Q7. A farmer has 100 m of fencing for three sides of a rectangular pen along a barn. What width maximizes the area?
    [*] 25 m
    [ ] 20 m
    [ ] 30 m
    [ ] 50 m
    Explanation: Fencing: 2w + l = 100, so l = 100 − 2w. Area A = w(100 − 2w) = −2w² + 100w. Vertex at w = 100/4 = 25 m.

  Q8. In the projectile model h(t) = −16t² + v₀t + h₀, what does h₀ represent?
    [ ] The acceleration due to gravity
    [ ] The maximum height
    [*] The initial height (height at t = 0)
    [ ] The time to reach the ground
    Explanation: In h(t) = −16t² + v₀t + h₀, when t = 0, h(0) = h₀. So h₀ is the initial height from which the object is launched.

  Q9. A ball thrown from 20 feet at 32 ft/s has h(t) = −16t² + 32t + 20. When is it at 36 feet?
    [*] t = 1 second (both up and down)
    [ ] t = 0.5 seconds
    [ ] Never
    [ ] t = 2 seconds
    Explanation: Set h = 36: −16t² + 32t + 20 = 36, so −16t² + 32t − 16 = 0, or t² − 2t + 1 = 0, giving (t − 1)² = 0. The ball is at 36 feet only at t = 1 (this is actually the maximum height).

  Q10. If h(t) = −4.9t² + 19.6t, what is the maximum height in meters?
    [ ] 9.8 m
    [ ] 4.9 m
    [ ] 39.2 m
    [*] 19.6 m
    Explanation: Vertex at t = −19.6/(2(−4.9)) = 2 seconds. h(2) = −4.9(4) + 19.6(2) = −19.6 + 39.2 = 19.6 meters.

  Q11. What is 'optimization' in the context of quadratic applications?
    [ ] Graphing a parabola, particularly regarding applications under the given assumptions
    [*] The process of finding the maximum or minimum value of a quantity modeled by a quadratic function
    [ ] Factoring a quadratic expression as predicted by standard models
    [ ] Solving a quadratic equation for its roots when measured under controlled conditions
    Explanation: Optimization means finding the best (maximum or minimum) value. For quadratics, this is the y-coordinate of the vertex, found using x = −b/(2a).

  Q12. What does 'projectile motion' mean in algebra?
    [ ] The exponential growth of an object's speed
    [ ] The linear path of an object moving at constant speed
    [*] The parabolic path of an object affected by gravity, modeled by a quadratic equation h(t) = −(1/2)gt² + v₀t + h₀
    [ ] The circular path of an orbiting object
    Explanation: Projectile motion describes an object launched into the air. Gravity creates a parabolic path modeled by h(t) = −(1/2)gt² + v₀t + h₀ (−16t² in feet, −4.9t² in meters).

  Q13. What does 'break-even point' mean?
    [ ] The point where cost equals zero
    [*] The point where revenue equals cost, meaning profit equals zero
    [ ] The point where revenue is maximized
    [ ] The point where profit is maximized
    Explanation: The break-even point occurs when Revenue = Cost (or equivalently Profit = 0). At this point, the business neither makes nor loses money.

  Q14. What is a 'revenue function'?
    [ ] A function that models the profit after expenses
    [ ] A function that models the total expenses of production
    [*] A function that models the total income from selling x items, typically R(x) = price × quantity
    [ ] A function that models the tax owed
    Explanation: A revenue function represents total income: R(x) = (price per item) × (number of items sold). When price depends on quantity, R(x) becomes a quadratic.

  Q15. What does 'initial velocity' (v₀) mean in a projectile model?
    [*] The speed at which the object is launched at time t = 0
    [ ] The speed of the object when it hits the ground
    [ ] The maximum speed of the object
    [ ] The acceleration due to gravity
    Explanation: Initial velocity v₀ is the speed and direction at the moment of launch (t = 0). A positive v₀ means the object is launched upward.

  Q16. What does 'constraint' mean in an optimization problem?
    [*] A fixed condition or limitation (like a set amount of fencing or budget) that restricts the possible solutions
    [ ] The vertex of the parabola, particularly regarding does based on established principles
    [ ] The variable you want to maximize or minimize in accordance with classical theory
    [ ] The discriminant of the quadratic when considering all relevant factors
    Explanation: A constraint is a given limitation (e.g., fixed perimeter, budget, or total amount) that you use to express one variable in terms of another before optimizing.

  Q17. What does 'maximum height' mean in a projectile problem?
    [*] The y-coordinate of the vertex of the height function, where the object momentarily stops rising
    [ ] The height when the object hits the ground
    [ ] The height at which the object was launched
    [ ] The initial velocity of the object
    Explanation: Maximum height is the peak of the parabolic path, found at the vertex. At this moment the vertical velocity is zero and the object transitions from rising to falling.

  Q18. What does 'profit function' mean?
    [ ] The function representing total sales
    [ ] The function representing total cost of production
    [ ] The function representing the number of items sold
    [*] The function P(x) = Revenue − Cost, representing the net income after subtracting expenses
    Explanation: The profit function P(x) = R(x) − C(x) gives the net gain (or loss) from producing and selling x items. When P > 0, the business is profitable.

  Q19. What does 'time of flight' mean for a projectile?
    [*] The total time the projectile is in the air from launch to landing (when h(t) returns to ground level)
    [ ] The time it takes to reach maximum height
    [ ] The time at which the projectile is at half its maximum height
    [ ] The time at which the initial velocity equals zero
    Explanation: Time of flight is the total airborne time, found by solving h(t) = 0 for the positive root (other than t = 0 if launched from ground level).

  Q20. What does 'area optimization' mean?
    [ ] Finding the area of any shape, particularly regarding variable following the
    [*] Finding the dimensions that maximize or minimize the area of a region subject to a given constraint
    [ ] Graphing the area function, particularly regarding using based on the prevailing evidence
    [ ] Calculating the perimeter of a rectangle in most standard conditions
    Explanation: Area optimization involves expressing area as a quadratic function of one variable (using a constraint) and finding the vertex to determine the maximum or minimum area.

  Q21. A water park designs a fountain with water height h(t) = −16t² + 80t feet, where t is time in seconds. How long is the water in the air, and what is the maximum height?
    [*] 5 seconds in the air; maximum height 100 feet
    [ ] 10 seconds in the air; maximum height 80 feet
    [ ] 2.5 seconds in the air; maximum height 50 feet
    [ ] 5 seconds in the air; maximum height 200 feet
    Explanation: Time in air: −16t² + 80t = 0 gives t(−16t + 80) = 0, so t = 0 or t = 5 seconds. Max height at t = 2.5: h(2.5) = −16(6.25) + 200 = −100 + 200 = 100 feet.

  Q22. A company finds that selling x widgets at price p = 50 − 0.5x gives revenue R(x) = x(50 − 0.5x). How many widgets maximize revenue, and what is the maximum revenue?
    [ ] 100 widgets; $2,500
    [*] 50 widgets; $1,250
    [ ] 50 widgets; $2,500
    [ ] 25 widgets; $937.50
    Explanation: R(x) = −0.5x² + 50x. Vertex x = −50/(2(−0.5)) = 50. R(50) = −0.5(2500) + 2500 = −1250 + 2500 = $1,250.

  Q23. A soccer ball is kicked from the ground with h(t) = −5t² + 20t meters. A player 15 meters away needs the ball to be above 15 m to clear a wall. Is the ball above 15 m at t = 1 second?
    [ ] Yes, h(1) = 20 m
    [ ] No, h(1) = 5 m
    [ ] No, h(1) = 10 m, so it does not clear
    [*] Yes, h(1) = 15 m, so it exactly clears the wall
    Explanation: h(1) = −5(1) + 20(1) = −5 + 20 = 15 meters. The ball is at exactly 15 meters at t = 1 second.

  Q24. A landscaper has 200 feet of edging to border three sides of a rectangular flower bed (the fourth side is against a house). What is the maximum area of the bed?
    [ ] 4,000 sq ft
    [ ] 10,000 sq ft
    [ ] 2,500 sq ft
    [*] 5,000 sq ft
    Explanation: Let w = width (two sides). Then l = 200 − 2w. A = w(200 − 2w) = −2w² + 200w. Vertex at w = 50, giving A = 50 × 100 = 5,000 sq ft.

  Q25. An electronics store models profit as P(x) = −4x² + 240x − 3200, where x is the price in dollars. At what prices does the store break even?
    [*] $20 and $40
    [ ] $30 and $50
    [ ] $15 and $45
    [ ] $10 and $60
    Explanation: Set P = 0: −4x² + 240x − 3200 = 0, or x² − 60x + 800 = 0. Factoring: (x − 20)(x − 40) = 0. Break-even prices are $20 and $40.

  Q26. A cannon fires a cannonball from a 20-meter cliff with initial velocity 30 m/s. Height is h(t) = −5t² + 30t + 20. What is the maximum height above the ground?
    [ ] 80 meters
    [*] 65 meters
    [ ] 45 meters
    [ ] 50 meters
    Explanation: Vertex at t = −30/(2(−5)) = 3. h(3) = −5(9) + 30(3) + 20 = −45 + 90 + 20 = 65 meters.

  Q27. A parking lot charges $10 per car and averages 200 cars per day. For each $1 increase, 10 fewer cars come. Revenue is R(x) = (10 + x)(200 − 10x). What price increase maximizes revenue?
    [ ] $10 increase (to $20 per car)
    [*] $5 increase (to $15 per car)
    [ ] $8 increase (to $18 per car)
    [ ] $3 increase (to $13 per car)
    Explanation: R(x) = −10x² + 100x + 2000. Vertex at x = −100/(2(−10)) = 5. A $5 increase (charging $15) maximizes revenue at R(5) = $2,250.

  Q28. A diver jumps from a 10-meter platform with initial upward velocity 5 m/s. Height is h(t) = −5t² + 5t + 10. How long until the diver hits the water?
    [*] 2 seconds
    [ ] 3 seconds
    [ ] 1 second
    [ ] 1.5 seconds
    Explanation: Set h = 0: −5t² + 5t + 10 = 0, or t² − t − 2 = 0. Factoring: (t − 2)(t + 1) = 0. Since t > 0, the diver hits the water at t = 2 seconds.

  Q29. A caterer finds that for a banquet of x guests, the cost per person is (40 − 0.1x) dollars and total revenue is R(x) = x(40 − 0.1x). What number of guests maximizes revenue?
    [*] 200 guests
    [ ] 100 guests
    [ ] 400 guests
    [ ] 300 guests
    Explanation: R(x) = −0.1x² + 40x. Vertex at x = −40/(2(−0.1)) = 40/0.2 = 200. Maximum revenue occurs with 200 guests.

  Q30. A firework is launched from the ground with h(t) = −16t² + 128t feet. It should explode at its peak. At what time and height should the timer trigger the explosion?
    [*] At t = 4 seconds and height 256 feet
    [ ] At t = 4 seconds and height 128 feet
    [ ] At t = 8 seconds and height 0 feet
    [ ] At t = 2 seconds and height 192 feet
    Explanation: Vertex at t = −128/(2(−16)) = 4 seconds. h(4) = −16(16) + 128(4) = −256 + 512 = 256 feet. The timer should trigger at t = 4 seconds when the firework is at 256 feet.

--- Lesson 2.6: Applications of Quadratics (Flashcards) ---

  1. Q: Height of projectile: h(t) = -16t² + 80t + 5. Maximum height?
     A: h = 105 feet. Vertex at t = 80/32 = 2.5 s, h(2.5) = 105.

  2. Q: Profit function P(x) = -2x² + 100x - 1000. Max profit?
     A: $150. At x = 100/4 = 25 units: P(25) = -1250 + 2500 - 1000 = 250...

  3. Q: Revenue R(x) = -3x² + 300x. Break-even points?
     A: R(x) = 0: x = 0 or x = 100. Revenue = x(-3x + 300).

  4. Q: Area rectangle with perimeter 40, length x. Area function?
     A: A(x) = x(20 - x) = 20x - x². Maximum at x = 10, A = 100.

  5. Q: Ball thrown from 6m height at 20 m/s. Time to ground?
     A: h(t) = -5t² + 20t + 6. Solve -5t² + 20t + 6 = 0 for t > 0.

  6. Q: Application type: maximizing area with fixed perimeter
     A: Quadratic optimization. Vertex gives maximum for concave down parabola.

  7. Q: Optimization: minimize cost C(x) = x² - 10x + 100
     A: Minimum at x = 5, C(5) = 75. Vertex of upward parabola.

  8. Q: Word problem setup: quadratic model usually comes from what?
     A: Real-world data, physics equations, geometric constraints, revenue/cost.

  9. Q: Demand p(x) = 100 - 2x, cost C(x) = 500 + 20x. Profit?
     A: P(x) = x(100 - 2x) - (500 + 20x) = -2x² + 80x - 500.

  10. Q: Find max area of rectangle inscribed in semicircle radius 5
     A: A = 25 when length = width·√2. Uses x² + y² = 25, A = 2xy optimization.

--- Lesson 2.7: Quadratic Inequalities (Summary) ---

  Key Concepts: Quadratic Inequalities
Overview
This lesson covers the fundamental measures of center used to analyze and summarize data sets. You'll learn how to calculate and apply the mean, median, and mode, and understand when each is most appropriate.
Key Definitions
What is the solution to x² + 4 > 0?
Since x² ≥ 0 for all x, x² + 4 ≥ 4 > 0 for all x. The inequality is always true, so the solution is all real numbers.
What is the solution to x² + 1 < 0?
Since x² ≥ 0, x² + 1 ≥ 1 > 0 always. The expression is never negative, so there is no solution.
What is a 'quadratic inequality'?
A quadratic inequality is an inequality of the form ax² + bx + c < 0 (or >, ≤, ≥). The solution is a set of intervals on the number line.
What is a 'sign chart' (or 'sign analysis')?
A sign chart divides the number line at the critical values (roots), then uses test points in each interval to determine the sign (+ or −) of the expression.
Real-World Applications
Example: A drainage pipe's water flow rate is F(d) = −d² + 8d − 12 gallons per minute, where d is the pipe diameter in inches. For which diameters is the flow rate positive?
Set F > 0: −d² + 8d − 12 > 0, so d² − 8d + 12 < 0. Factor: (d − 2)(d − 6) < 0. Flow is positive for 2 < d < 6 inches.

--- Lesson 2.7: Quadratic Inequalities (Quiz) ---

  Q1. Solve x² − 16 > 0.
    [ ] −4 < x < 4
    [*] x < −4 or x > 4
    [ ] No solution
    [ ] x > 4 only
    Explanation: Factor: (x − 4)(x + 4) > 0. The product is positive outside the roots. Solution: x < −4 or x > 4.

  Q2. Solve x² − 4x − 5 ≤ 0.
    [ ] All real numbers
    [ ] −5 ≤ x ≤ 1
    [*] −1 ≤ x ≤ 5
    [ ] x ≤ −1 or x ≥ 5
    Explanation: Factor: (x − 5)(x + 1) ≤ 0. For a > 0 parabola, the expression is negative (or zero) between the roots: −1 ≤ x ≤ 5.

  Q3. Solve −x² + 9 > 0.
    [*] −3 < x < 3
    [ ] All real numbers
    [ ] x < −3 or x > 3
    [ ] No solution
    Explanation: Rewrite as x² < 9, so |x| < 3. The solution is −3 < x < 3.

  Q4. Solve (x − 3)(x + 1) > 0.
    [ ] x = −1 or x = 3
    [ ] x > 3 only
    [ ] −1 < x < 3
    [*] x < −1 or x > 3
    Explanation: The product of two factors is positive when both are positive (x > 3) or both are negative (x < −1). Solution: x < −1 or x > 3.

  Q5. What is the solution to x² + 4 > 0?
    [ ] x > 2
    [ ] −2 < x < 2
    [*] All real numbers
    [ ] No solution
    Explanation: Since x² ≥ 0 for all x, x² + 4 ≥ 4 > 0 for all x. The inequality is always true, so the solution is all real numbers.

  Q6. Solve 2x² − 3x − 2 ≥ 0.
    [*] x ≤ −1/2 or x ≥ 2
    [ ] All real numbers
    [ ] x ≥ 2 only
    [ ] −1/2 ≤ x ≤ 2
    Explanation: Factor: (2x + 1)(x − 2) ≥ 0. Roots are x = −1/2 and x = 2. Since a > 0, the expression is non-negative outside the roots: x ≤ −1/2 or x ≥ 2.

  Q7. Solve x² ≤ 25.
    [ ] x ≤ −5 or x ≥ 5
    [ ] x ≤ 5 only
    [*] [−5, 5]
    [ ] (−5, 5)
    Explanation: x² ≤ 25 means |x| ≤ 5, so −5 ≤ x ≤ 5. In interval notation: [−5, 5].

  Q8. What is the solution to x² + 1 < 0?
    [ ] All real numbers as observed
    [ ] x < −1, particularly regarding
    [*] No solution (x² + 1 is always positive)
    [ ] −1 < x < 1, particularly
    Explanation: Since x² ≥ 0, x² + 1 ≥ 1 > 0 always. The expression is never negative, so there is no solution.

  Q9. Solve x² + 2x − 15 < 0.
    [ ] x < −5 or x > 3
    [ ] −3 < x < 5
    [*] −5 < x < 3
    [ ] x > 3 only
    Explanation: Factor: (x + 5)(x − 3) < 0. Roots are −5 and 3. Since a > 0, the expression is negative between the roots: −5 < x < 3.

  Q10. For a > 0, the quadratic ax² + bx + c < 0 is satisfied:
    [ ] Outside the roots in most
    [ ] Nowhere, particularly regarding
    [*] Between the roots (if real roots exist)
    [ ] Everywhere, particularly
    Explanation: When a > 0, the parabola opens upward. It dips below the x-axis between its roots (if they exist), so the inequality is satisfied between the roots.

  Q11. What is a 'quadratic inequality'?
    [ ] An equation where a quadratic expression equals zero
    [ ] A linear inequality with a squared variable
    [ ] An inequality with no solution
    [*] An inequality that involves a quadratic expression, using <, >, ≤, or ≥ instead of =
    Explanation: A quadratic inequality is an inequality of the form ax² + bx + c < 0 (or >, ≤, ≥). The solution is a set of intervals on the number line.

  Q12. What is a 'sign chart' (or 'sign analysis')?
    [ ] A chart showing the vertex coordinates when considering all relevant factors
    [ ] A graph of the quadratic function, particularly regarding sign as predicted by standard models
    [*] A table showing whether a quadratic expression is positive, negative, or zero in each interval determined by its roots
    [ ] A list of all possible factors, particularly regarding critical under the given assumptions
    Explanation: A sign chart divides the number line at the critical values (roots), then uses test points in each interval to determine the sign (+ or −) of the expression.

  Q13. What does 'test point' mean when solving quadratic inequalities?
    [ ] The y-intercept of the function, particularly regarding when when measured under controlled conditions
    [ ] The vertex of the parabola, particularly regarding does under the given assumptions
    [*] A value chosen from each interval to substitute into the inequality to determine the sign of the expression
    [ ] The roots of the quadratic equation in accordance with classical theory
    Explanation: A test point is any convenient x-value within an interval. You plug it into the quadratic expression to check whether the result is positive or negative in that interval.

  Q14. What does 'critical value' mean in solving quadratic inequalities?
    [*] The roots (zeros) of the quadratic equation that divide the number line into intervals for sign analysis
    [ ] The leading coefficient, particularly regarding changes under the given assumptions
    [ ] The discriminant value, particularly regarding zero based on the prevailing evidence
    [ ] The maximum or minimum value of the function following conventional understanding
    Explanation: Critical values are the x-values where the quadratic expression equals zero. They are the boundary points that separate intervals where the expression changes sign.

  Q15. What does 'solution set' of an inequality mean?
    [ ] The range of the function
    [*] The set of all x-values that make the inequality true
    [ ] The vertex coordinates
    [ ] The roots of the related equation
    Explanation: The solution set is the collection of all values of x for which the inequality is satisfied. It is typically expressed in interval notation or as a union of intervals.

  Q16. What does 'interval notation' mean?
    [ ] Writing solutions using set-builder notation only based on established principles
    [ ] A method of graphing inequalities, particularly regarding endpoints in the context of this analysis
    [ ] A way to write fractions, particularly regarding does as predicted by standard models
    [*] A compact way to describe a range of values using parentheses ( ) for exclusive endpoints and brackets [ ] for inclusive endpoints
    Explanation: Interval notation uses (a, b) to mean a < x < b and [a, b] to mean a ≤ x ≤ b. Parentheses exclude endpoints; brackets include them.

  Q17. What does 'union' of intervals mean in inequality solutions?
    [ ] Multiplying two intervals together
    [*] Combining two separate intervals using the symbol ∪ to represent all values in either interval
    [ ] The intersection of two intervals
    [ ] Finding the overlap of two intervals
